# IDWT Appendix A: Patterns in the Mathematical Structure

**Working document — not for publication as-is.**  
This appendix records every mathematical pattern found or checked in the IDWT framework, organised by topic. Sections 1–9 cover patterns that are stated, derived, or used in the main documents (Parts 1–10). Sections 10–14 cover patterns found in this document set that have not yet been placed in the main documents. Section 15 records attempts that returned null results, so those searches do not get repeated.

When a pattern from §10–14 gets incorporated into a main document, move its entry to the appropriate §1–9 section and note the location.

---

## Part I — Patterns in the documented theory

### §1. Mode index set — the 15 visible particles

The 15 physical particles selected by the co-fixed-point condition. Each carries a mode index n and a sector dimension d; mass = m_scale_d × S(n,d).

| n | Particle | Sector d | S(n,d) | Notes |
|---|----------|----------|--------|-------|
| 0 | photon γ | 2 | 0 | n=0 is universal; S(0,d)=0 for all d |
| 1 | down quark | 3 | 1 | universal ground state; S(1,d)=1 for all d |
| 3 | up quark | 4 | 15 | = S(3,4) = C(6,4) |
| 4 | strange quark | 3 | 20 | = n_s; S(4,3) = C(6,3) |
| 10 | ν₁ | 5 | 2002 | = S(3,3) in a different sense; see §5 |
| 13 | electron | 6 | 18564 | unit reference |
| 15 | ν₂ | 5 | 11628 | |
| 20 | charm quark | 4 | 8855 | = S(4,3) index, d=4 sector |
| 22 | ν₃ | 5 | 65780 | |
| 23 | tau lepton | 10 | 64512240 | |
| 35 | muon | 6 | 3838380 | |
| 72 | top quark | 4 | 1215450 | |
| 76 | W boson | 2 | 2926 | |
| 81 | Z boson | 2 | 3321 | |
| 95 | Higgs | 2 | 4560 | |

The selection mechanism is documented in Part 7: the mode-sector pair (n,d) must be a member of Σ_pairs — the co-fixed-point set produced by the generation tower (the hockey-stick recursion from seeds {n_d=1, n_u=3} and their composite n_s=4). Stability of the pair is established by the l-parity and dephasing mechanisms (Part 7 §1.2); membership requires both the correct mode index and the correct sector.

### §2. Mode index set — unselected candidates

Modes generated by the hockey-stick recursion that are not co-fixed-points (fail the Σ_pairs membership condition), or are never generated. Documented in Part 7 §1 and idwt.py Step 29.

**d=3 modes that are not co-fixed-points:**
- n=2 (level N=1, odd): l-parity disconnected from the seeds (Part 7 §1.2) — a broad colour-triplet excitation, not a stable particle.
- n=3 (level N=2, even): dephases in the infinite-dimensional coupled system — not stable.
- n=5 and above: not co-fixed-points; absent as stable states.

Note: n=4 (= n_s) is a co-fixed-point (strange quark), selected by the co-fixed-point condition.

**The d=2 gap (n=1 through n=75):**  
No Vandermonde combination of any fermion (n,d) pair produces a d=2 mode index below 76. The fermion Vandermonde values g = n+d−1 are {3, 6, 6, 14, 18, 19, 23, 26, 32, 40, 75} — all occupied as mode indices in their own sectors. The gap is the mass range where matter lives in its own sectors; d=2 has no eigenmode there.

### §3. The sector set D = {2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 10}

**What it is.** Six geometric strata of Ξ₁₀, each hosting one particle family. Documented in Part 1 §3 and the Euler characteristic chain article.

**The six dimensions as CP^k (even-d sectors) and S^k (odd-d sectors):**
- d=2: CP¹ (isometry U(1))
- d=3: S³ (isometry SO(4))
- d=4: CP² (isometry SU(3))
- d=5: S⁵ (isometry SO(6) ≅ SU(4))
- d=6: CP³ (isometry SU(4))
- d=10: CP⁵ (isometry SU(6))

**Why d=7, 8, 9 are absent.** The coupling fixed-point equation for g₈₈ has no solution (d=8 gap). The terminal sector is set by Gegenbauer criticality: b_{k₀}(d) = ½ exactly at d = 2(N_c+2) = 10 (Theorem T5, Part 1 §4b). The sequence is consecutive from d=2 through d=6, then jumps to d=10.

**Jump from d=6 to d=10:**  d=10 − d=6 = 4 = n_s. The final active sector is 4 steps above d=6 in dimension, spanning the inactive d=7,8,9 coordinates (which are absent not for lack of dimension but for lack of a valid coupling fixed point or Gegenbauer-critical endpoint at those values of d).

**Sum of occupied dimensions:** 2+3+4+5+6+10 = 30 = (n_s+1) × N_f = 5 × 6. (Not assigned structural meaning yet; noted for reference.)

**Products within the set:** 2×3 = 6 ∈ D, 2×5 = 10 ∈ D. Products 3×4=12 and 2×6=12 are not in D. The two products that land in D both involve d=2.

**Rule B criticality inequality — direction correction of record (2026-06-10, `claude/explore_hopf_uniqueness.py`).** Part 9 T3 Rule B stated $b_{k_0}(d)\geq\tfrac12$ iff $4k_0\leq(d-2)^2$. The direction is reversed. With $b_{k_0}(d)=\sqrt{k_0(k_0+d-1)}/(2k_0+d-2)$ and positive denominators, $b_{k_0}-\tfrac12$ has the sign of $4k_0(k_0+d-1)-(2k_0+d-2)^2 = -d^2+4d+60 = -(d-10)(d+6)$ at $k_0=16$. Hence $b_{k_0}\geq\tfrac12 \Leftrightarrow (d-2)^2\leq 4k_0 \Leftrightarrow d\leq 10$, and $b_{k_0}<\tfrac12$ (subcritical) $\Leftrightarrow d\geq 11$ — matching the §3/T3 table (d=2…6 supercritical, d=10 critical, d≥11 excluded) and the equality endpoint $4k_0=(d-2)^2$ used in T5/T15a. The mis-stated form would instead admit $d\geq10$ and exclude $d=2$…$9$, contradicting the table. Part 9 T3 Rule B corrected to $b_{k_0}\geq\tfrac12$ iff $(d-2)^2\leq 4k_0$ (equivalently $d\leq 2+2\sqrt{k_0}$); the equality endpoint and all downstream logic were already correct. Verified algebraically (factor $-(d-10)(d+6)$) and numerically ($b(2)=0.5154$, $b(10)=0.5000$, $b(11)=0.4975$). The same script confirms the full sector selection (Rule A χ-gap at $\chi=N_c+2=5$ → $d=8$; odd total spaces routing over a non-fixed-point base → $d=7,9$; Rule B → $d\geq11$) reproduces the pass-set exactly $\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$; the routing-exhaustiveness step of Rule A stays the open 🔶 item (Part 6).

**Rule A exhaustiveness — closure candidate (2026-06-12, `claude/explore_rulea_routing.py` + `claude/explore_rulea_closure.py`).** The open Rule A lemma (Part 6) asked for a proof that Hopf-universality routing requires a fixed-point base. The bottom-up form is not provable as posed: a transported *value* for $g_{77}$ is always writable, and once $g_{66}$ exists every coupling-consistency test the kernel supplies is satisfied by $g_{77}=w^2 g_{66}$ with $w^2=g_{33}/g_{22}$ (the would-be value $0.00732$ is even seed-expressible). The closure instead runs top-down. (i) **Induced-base lemma (candidate ✅):** the complex Hopf fiber is a unit great circle with inner-product profile $\cos t$ in every $S^{2k+1}$ (⭐), and $L^2(S^{2k+1})=\bigoplus_m L^2(\mathbb{CP}^k,\mathcal{O}(m))$ with $m{=}0$ block exactly $L^2(\mathbb{CP}^k)$ (⭐); an active total space therefore carries the base sector problem on its $S^1$-invariant block, and T2 rank-1 (one coupling per sector pair) forces the induced coupling to coincide with the base's own. Verified exactly at both real pairs with a single reduction constant: $g_{22}/g_{33}=g_{44}/g_{55}=34.1349\ldots$ (machine-exact; the equality is T9a). Read bottom-up this *derives* T9b as a consistency relation between active pairs — universality is necessary, never an activation mechanism. (ii) **d=9 (candidate ✅):** an active $S^9$ induces a $d{=}8$ coupling on its invariant block, but $d{=}8$ has no admissible value — no seed residency, no back-reaction source, no fixed point (T15b: the $g_{88}$ equation has no solution), $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^4)=5$ the unique seed-unmatched $\chi$ — so the induced coupling would be the one constant outside the seed-closed coupling algebra (Part 2 §9 completeness). (iii) **d=7 — the μ–τ/Rule-B squeeze (candidate ✅, the new result):** at the T3 stage (sector set logically prior to mode occupancy, Part 1 §3a before §3b; Appendix §5), the kernel-visible data of base $d{=}6$ and base $d{=}10$ are identical — full coupling rows equal exactly ($v_6=v_{10}=1/2$, T9c; rank-1 makes the entire rows equal), both $\chi$ seed-matched ($\chi(\mathbb{CP}^3)=n_s$, $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^5)=N_f$), same fiber. So any activation route for $S^7$ over $\mathbb{CP}^3$ activates $S^{11}$ over $\mathbb{CP}^5$ with the same output ($g_{11,11}=g_{77}$). Both readings of that output are excluded: as an active sector, $d{=}11$ is Gegenbauer-subcritical ($b_{k_0}(11)=0.4975<\tfrac12$, ⭐) and cannot host the discrete eigenmodes activity requires; as a bare coupling row, $v_{11}\neq0$ links every sector mode to the $d{=}11$ free continuum (subcritical ⟹ scattering states only, no gap), giving e, u, and the neutrinos generic nonzero widths against absolute stability (Part 7 §1.2 stability equivalence; $\tau_e>6.6\times10^{28}$ yr). Hence no activation route for $d{=}7$ exists. The squeeze does not over-fire: $(6,10)$ is the only $v$-degenerate sector pair, so $d{=}3$ and $d{=}5$ activations (unique base rows) are untouched — Rule A's seal is the *conjunction* of T9c (terminal coupling degeneracy) and Rule B (criticality endpoint one step above the last base). Honest residuals: the route-input classification (activation routes see only T3-stage kernel data) is P1–P4 minimality plus the documented logical ordering — flagged as the premise a referee must grant; the induced-coupling positivity/blockwise-self-consistency step of (i) is a functional-analytic sketch verified exactly at the two real pairs, not yet a written functional; the tau back-reaction contamination test of an active $d{=}7$ is inconclusive at T10b order ($\sim1.7\times10^{-5}$ relative vs PDG $5.1\times10^{-5}$ — 0.34σ), so the empirical backstop has no power and the exclusion rests on the squeeze. Status upgrade of Rule A in T3/Part 1/Part 6 awaits Fedge's adversarial read; nothing in the Parts has been changed by this entry.

**Adversarial-read correction to the above (2026-06-12, same day, prompted by Fedge).** The squeeze's premise "criticality is the only asymmetry between the $d{=}6$ and $d{=}10$ bases" is an overclaim, and item (iii) is downgraded from candidate ✅ to **partial result, Rule A $d{=}7$ stays 🔶**. The coupling rows are exactly equal and both $\chi$'s are seed-matched, but the $\chi$ *values* differ (4 vs 6) and are integer-layer data, visible at sector-set-determination time. T15b's own consecutive $\chi$-run $\{N_c{-}1,N_c,N_c{+}1\}=\{2,3,4\}$ supplies a separating predicate with documented standing: an activation route keyed on "base $\chi$ in the consecutive run" is instantiated by both real activations ($d{=}3$ over $\chi{=}2$, $d{=}5$ over $\chi{=}3$), fires at $d{=}7$ (over $\chi{=}4$), and is silent at $d{=}11$ ($\chi{=}6$ lies past the gap) — evading the squeeze. With only two real activation instances the activation law is underdetermined: "base coupling solves a kernel equation" fits both instances and excludes $d{=}7$; "base $\chi$ in the consecutive run" fits both and admits it; nothing at the integer layer arbitrates, and the empirical discriminators lack power (the $\tau$ back-reaction test above; mass ratios are coupling-free and insensitive). What survives the correction: the $d{=}9$ closure (independent of the squeeze; the $\chi$-run route does not fire there, $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^4)=5\notin$ run — consistent); the T9b direction-of-implication result (universality as consistency relation, not activation mechanism); and the squeeze as a partial theorem excluding every activation route that is symmetric in the $6/10$ base data (rows, $\chi$-set membership, fiber). The arbitration between the two surviving route-predicates is a dynamical question: it requires the explicit vacuum-stability functional (Part 2 §5), under which activation becomes solvability of an equation rather than a predicate fitted to two instances.

**Second adversarial round and propagation (2026-06-12, same day, Fedge-authorized).** Stress-testing what survived the first correction. (1) *Quotient caveat on the induced-base lemma:* the Hopf base is a quotient $S^{2k+1}/S^1$, not a coordinate subspace, while the sector nesting $\Xi_d\subset\Xi_{d'}$ is coordinate-plane containment — so the invariant block is a $\mathbb{CP}^k$-*symmetric* kernel self-consistency problem, not literally the $\Xi_{2k}$ coordinate-plane sector, and the constant equality $g_{22}/g_{33}=g_{44}/g_{55}$ is *consistent with* the induced-base reading rather than an independent verification of it (it is T9a restated). (2) *d=9 survives the caveat:* T15b's no-solution reason ($\chi=5$ seed-unmatched) applies to the equation *form*, hence to the induced $\mathbb{CP}^4$-symmetric problem regardless of the quotient/subspace distinction — and the $\chi$-run predicate does not fire at $d=9$ ($\chi(\mathbb{CP}^4)=5\notin$ run), so the $d=9$ exclusion is route-independent. The principled asymmetry stands: $d=9$ has a genuine obstruction, $d=7$ does not, which is why only $d=7$ needs the (leaky) squeeze. (3) *Stability-leg caveat:* the $(d',11)$ kernel term has support on coordinates $\leq d'$, so only $d=11$ continuum slices with structure confined to shared coordinates couple; such slices exist down to zero energy (subcritical ⟹ no well, scattering threshold at the bottom), so phase space stays open and the generic-width conclusion holds. (4) *New corroborating constraint (🔶, conditional):* an active $d=7$ would extend the matter quartet to five sectors, breaking the count $2n_s-4=n_s$ that independently certifies $n_s=4$ (§19 quartet derivation; the requirement itself is 🔵-motivated, so this corroborates rather than proves). (5) *d=5 activation under the consistency reading of T9b:* shifts to the quartet/family structure (the quartet derivation already places $d=5$ among the matter sectors independently of coupling construction); the routing rule (T9b corollary) is about mode routing and is unaffected. Propagated with Rule A kept 🔶 throughout: Part 9 T3 (Rule A bullets, open item, Jacobi-table notes, distinct-types paragraph), Part 1 §3a (Rule A paragraph, inactive-dimension remark, the d=7 exclusion paragraph), Part 6 (Rule A entry rewritten around the actual residual), `files/idwt.py` STEP 2 comment. The promised-and-unprovable "routing requires a fixed-point base" lemma no longer appears as an open item anywhere; the open item is the activation-law arbitration via the vacuum-stability functional.

**Mean-field non-selectivity of the Rule A arbiter; the "Part 2 §5 functional" misdirection corrected (2026-06-12, `claude/explore_meanfield_selectivity.py`; `files/idwt.py` STEP 76).** The preceding addenda left the $d=7$ arbitration to "the explicit vacuum-stability functional (Part 2 §5)," under which activation would become solvability of an equation. The nonlinear-EoM object that Part 2 §5 would have to supply is the Part 4 §3.10 condensate mean-field self-consistency $\lambda_d = g_{dd}\langle r^2\rangle_d/d$ with the $d$-dimensional isotropic-oscillator ground state $\langle r^2\rangle_d = d/(2\sqrt{\lambda_d})$. Substituting, the dimension cancels exactly: $2\lambda_d^{3/2}=g_{dd}$ (verified, max self-consistency residual over the active set $7\times10^{-15}$). This equation is solvable for any $g_{dd}>0$ in any dimension — it is **non-selective in $d$**. Feeding the inactive band a formal coupling (the Hopf continuation $g_{77}=g_{55}g_{66}/g_{44}=0.00732$) solves it just as well; it is not rejected. The only cross-sector coupling-fixer available in the mean field, Hopf universality $v_3/v_2=v_5/v_4$, *writes* that same $g_{77}$ rather than forbidding it (it fixes the scale of a sector already required active but lacking its own fixed point — $d=5$, $\chi(S^5)=0$ — and is not an activation mechanism, the T9b reading). The single mean-field-adjacent asymmetry is the quartet *count* (an active $d=7$ extends the matter quartet to five sectors, breaking $2n_s-4=n_s$), which is itself 🔵 and corroborates rather than proves. **Conclusion:** no mean-field functional arbitrates $d=7$; Part 2 §5 contains no such object and the "minima at $\{1,4\}$" reading there is separately null (§15, kernel positivity). The genuine arbiter is the coupled $(\Psi_\infty,\{M_d\})$ fixed point — concretely **Part 6 Open Theorem A**, the ground-state directional-covariance operator $\hat C$ whose spectral plateaux should fall at exactly $d\in D$ (and Part 1 §1's dependency note, where $D$ is to emerge from the joint field–geometry fixed point when $V_d$ is derived from the action, MC-2). The cross-references citing "the vacuum-stability functional (Part 2 §5)" as the arbiter (Part 1 §3a, Part 6, Part 9 T3) were repointed to Open Theorem A. Rule A stays 🔶: the result relocates the open object to its correct home and shows mean field cannot close it, but does not itself close $d=7$.

**Bott mod-8 corroborating observation (2026-06-09).** The even active sectors {2,4,6,10} have d mod 8 = {2,4,6,2}. The d=10 row is identical in spinor type to the d=2 row (Weyl ✓, Majorana ✓, Majorana-Weyl ✓; Part 8 §2.1 table). The even chain therefore terminates at the first even d whose Clifford algebra class returns to the d=2 class under Bott periodicity. The gap at d=8 falls in class 0 (d mod 8 = 0), the one class not present in the active chain. This is a fourth independent convergence on d=10 as the terminal sector, alongside the Hopf chain, Gegenbauer b_{k₀}=½ (T5), and the φ(χ)≤2 cyclotomic criterion (Appendix §15 F1-ext). Treat as a corroborating observation, not a derivation: the Bott period is 8 for any sequence of Clifford algebras, so the return is automatic; the non-trivial content is only that the even chain stops exactly at the return point rather than extending past it.

### §4. Euler characteristics and sector-mode index correlations

The Euler characteristic chain (Theorem T15, Part 9):

χ(CP^k) = k + 1

| Space | χ | Role in IDWT |
|-------|---|--------------|
| CP¹ | 2 | d=2 sector; number of photon polarisations |
| CP² | 3 | = N_c; number of quark colours |
| CP³ | 4 | = n_s; the strange-quark composite index |
| CP⁴ | 5 | **missing sector**; χ(CP⁴) = n_s+1 = q |
| CP⁵ | 6 | = N_f; number of quark/lepton flavours |

Mode indices expressible in N_c alone:

| Identity | Value | Theorem |
|----------|-------|---------|
| n_s = N_c + 1 | 4 | T15 |
| n_e = N_c² + N_c + 1 | 13 | T15d |
| n_ν₁ = N_c² + 1 | 10 | T15d |
| n_top = N_c(N_c+1)(N_c+3) | 72 | T15b |
| d_terminal = 2(N_c+2) | 10 | T15a |
| Hopf product = N_c(N_c+1)³/2 | 96 | T15c |

### §5. The Generation Tower — documented derivation

Seeds: n_down = 1 (universal ground state, S(1,d)=1 for all d) in d=3; n_s = 4 (unique solution to the muon fixed point) in d=3. Every other mode index is derived; none are postulated. Documented in Part 2 §2–4.

The co-fixed-point condition applies to the (n,d) pair. The n and d for each particle come from **two independent derivation chains**:
- **n** is derived by the generation tower operations (hockey-stick, additive, g-rule) below.
- **d** is assigned by the sector structure established in Part 1 §3: the Hopf fibration assigns particle families to sectors (quarks→d=3,4; neutrinos→d=5; charged leptons→d=6; tau→d=10; bosons→d=2) prior to and independently of the mode index derivation. There is no equation d=f(n) — the sector cannot be derived from the mode index alone (Appendix A §15), and the same tower operation (e.g. HS with d_eval=3) can produce particles in different sectors depending on which seed is used.

The table below records both derivation chains side by side. The d-source column cites which sector-structure result assigns that family to that d; it is not a derivation of d from n.

**Derivation chain — n and d with sources:**

| Particle | n derivation | n | d | d source (sector family assignment) |
|----------|-------------|---|---|--------------------------------------|
| down | universal ground state S(1,d)=1 | 1 | 3 | seed sector — the observable d=3 spacetime is the starting point |
| strange | composite n_s = n_d+n_u (T4; muon fixed-point S(4,4)=35) | 4 | 3 | seed sector |
| up | n_s − 1 | 3 | 4 | d=4 is the CP² colour sector; χ(CP²)=N_c=3; up-type quarks defined as d=4 family (Part 1 §3b, T15a) |
| ν₁ | S(n_up, 3) | 10 | 5 | d=5 is the Hopf total space S¹→S⁵→CP²; neutrinos defined as the d=5 family, Hopf partner of d=4 (Part 1 §3b, Part 2 §2) |
| ν₂ | S(n_up, 4) | 15 | 5 | same |
| ν₃ | n_ν₁ + n_ν₂ − n_up | 22 | 5 | same |
| electron | n_ν₁ + n_up | 13 | 6 | d=6=d=3⊗d=3; charged leptons defined as the d=6 family, colour-neutral by tensor-product geometry (Part 1 §3b, Part 2 §4) |
| charm | S(n_s, 3) | 20 | 4 | up-type quark family (same sector as up) |
| muon | n_charm + n_ν₂ | 35 = S(n_s,4) | 6 | charged-lepton family (same sector as electron) |
| tau | n_ν₃ + n_down | 23 | 10 | d=10 is the Gegenbauer-critical sector; tau defined as the d=10 family; b_{k₀}=½ at d=2(N_c+2)=10 (Part 1 T5) |
| top | S(n_e,2) − n_charm + 1 | 72 = N_c·n_s·N_f | 4 | up-type quark family (same sector as up and charm) |
| photon | n=0 universal S(0,d)=0 | 0 | 2 | d=2 is the EM sector CP¹; U(1)_EM isometry (Part 1 §3) |
| W | g(d_ν, n_top) = d_ν+n_top−1 | 76 | 2 | Vandermonde g-rule produces gauge-sector modes in d=2 (Part 3 §11) |
| Z | g(d_ℓ, n_W) = d_ℓ+n_W−1 | 81 | 2 | same |
| Higgs | n_Z + n_ν₂ − 1 | 95 = n_up+n_charm+n_top | 2 | same |

**The 2×2 Pascal block.** The four indices n_ν₁, n_ν₂, n_charm, n_μ form the 2×2 submatrix of the simplex table at the seed coordinates (n_up, n_s) = (3, 4):

```
           d=3       d=4
n=3:    S(3,3)=10  S(3,4)=15    (ν₁, ν₂)
n=4:    S(4,3)=20  S(4,4)=35    (charm, muon)
```

The second generation and the neutrino sector occupy one contiguous 2×2 cell in Pascal's triangle at the composite coordinates $(n_s=4, n_u=3)$.

**Muon self-referential fixed point.** n_μ = S(n_s, 4) = S(4,4) = 35 is both the eigenmode selection rule output (n_charm + n_ν₂ = 35) and the d=4 self-image of the composite. The coincidence is what confirms n_s = 4 as the composite; it is the unique solution.

### §5a. Coupling constants — derivation sequence

All six self-couplings are derived from n_s = 4, n_u = 3 in a fixed order. Each is fully determined before the next is computed. Source: Part 2 §9, Part 9 T9, T15.

| Step | Coupling | Derivation | Exact value |
|------|----------|-----------|-------------|
| 1 | g₃₃ | Kernel fixed-point at k₀ = n_s²: n_s²√(n_s+n_u)/2 | 8√7 ≈ 21.166 |
| 2 | g₄₄ | Kernel fixed-point: n_s·n_u/√(n_s+n_u) | 12/√7 ≈ 4.536 |
| 3 | g₆₆ | Composite ratio for CP³ base: 1/n_s | 1/4 |
| 4 | g₁₀,₁₀ | Shared composite coupling (μ-τ symmetry): = g₆₆ | 1/4 |
| 5 | g₂₂ | Cross-sector back-reaction fixed-point: (S(n_s,3)−n_u)² · (S(n_u,4)−S(n_u,3)) / 2 | 722.5 |
| 6 | g₅₅ | Hopf universality v₃/v₂ = v₅/v₄: g₃₃·g₄₄/g₂₂ = 96/g₂₂ | 96/722.5 ≈ 0.133 |

Cross-check: g₃₃ × g₄₄ = g₂₂ × g₅₅ = 96 = N_c(N_c+1)³/2 exactly (Part 9 T9a, T15c).

### §5b. Sector scales — derivation sequence

All scales follow from m_e and the couplings above. The d=6 scale is the unit anchor; d=5 is derived last because it requires both m_scale_6 and m_scale_4. Source: Part 2 §10, Part 9 T11a.

| Step | Scale | Formula | Value |
|------|-------|---------|-------|
| 1 | m_scale_6 | m_e / S(n_e, 6) = m_e / 18564 | 2.753×10⁻⁵ MeV |
| 2 | m_scale_10 | = m_scale_6 (shared coupling g₁₀,₁₀ = g₆₆) | 2.753×10⁻⁵ MeV |
| 3 | m_scale_3 | m_e × √(g₃₃/g₆₆) | 4.702 MeV |
| 4 | m_scale_4 | m_scale_3 × √(g₄₄/g₃₃) / S(n_u, 4) | 0.1451 MeV |
| 5 | m_scale_2 | m_e × √(g₂₂/g₆₆) | 27.47 MeV |
| 6 | m_scale_5 | (n_u/n_s) × m_scale_6³ / m_scale_4² | 7.43×10⁻¹³ MeV |

The d=5 suppression factor (n_u/n_s) = 3/4 = 1 − g₆₆ is the complement of the lepton sector coupling: the coupling strength the charged-lepton sector retains (g₆₆) is what the neutrino sector surrenders (Part 9 T15e).

### §6. Structural constants

Constants derived from the seeds that appear across multiple derivations.

| Constant | Definition | Value | Appearances |
|----------|-----------|-------|-------------|
| k₀ | n_s² | 16 | Gegenbauer resonance site; g₃₃ factor; GTC |
| p | S(n_s,3) − n_up | 17 | Enters g₂₂ = p²q/2 as Dirac eigenstate count |
| q | S(n_up,4) − S(n_up,3) | 5 | Enters g₂₂; equals n_Z − n_W; equals n_s+1; equals χ(CP⁴) |
| ε | 1/(280√7) | ≈ 0.001350 | GTC per-quark correction; ε·g₃₃ = 1/35 = δ_ν₃ |
| back-reaction | 1 + 1/(n_up·n_s²·S(n_s,4)) | ≈ 1.000595 | Tau mass resummation factor |

**Multiple characterisations of k₀:**
- k₀ = n_s² = 16
- k₀ = n_e + n_up = 13 + 3 = 16
- k₀ = S(n_s,3) − S(2,3) = 20 − 4 = 16
- k₀ = n_charm − n_s = 20 − 4 = 16

**Back-reaction denominator:**  
n_up · k₀ · n_μ = 3 · 16 · 35 = **1680** = n_s · n_up · (n_s + n_up) · S(n_s,3) = 4·3·7·20. Appears as the resummation denominator for the tau mass correction.

**GTC correction:** ε · g₃₃ = [1/(280√7)] · [8√7] = 8/280 = **1/35 = 1/n_μ** exactly. The per-mode GTC shift is the reciprocal of the muon mode index.

### §7. Sector scales

Each m_scale_d is the mass unit for sector d; particle masses are m = m_scale_d × S(n,d).

| Sector | Scale | Derivation | Value (MeV) |
|--------|-------|-----------|-------------|
| d=2 | m_scale₂ = m_e √(g₂₂/g₆₆) | coupling ratio | 27.4706 |
| d=3 | m_scale₃ = m_e √(g₃₃/g₆₆) | coupling ratio | 4.7019 |
| d=4 | m_scale₄ = m_scale₃ √(g₄₄/g₃₃) / S(n_up,4) | fixed-point + up quark | 0.14510 |
| d=5 | m_scale₅ = (n_up/n_s) · m_scale₆³ / m_scale₄² | cross-sector consistency | 7.43×10⁻¹³ |
| d=6 | m_scale₆ = m_e / S(n_e,6) | electron anchor | 2.753×10⁻⁵ |
| d=10 | m_scale₁₀ = m_scale₆ | shared composite coupling g₆₆=g₁₀,₁₀=1/n_s | 2.753×10⁻⁵ |

**Key relationships:**
- m_scale₂ = m_e √(g₂₂/g₆₆); m_scale₃ = m_e √(g₃₃/g₆₆) — both scale as m_e times the square root of their coupling over the lepton coupling
- m_scale₆ = m_scale₁₀ because g₆₆ = g₁₀,₁₀ = 1/n_s (shared composite coupling); the tau-to-muon mass ratio is purely S(n_τ,10)/S(n_μ,6), not a scale difference
- m_scale₄ is the only scale set by dividing by an explicit S(n,d): the up quark is the anchor for d=4 because n_up = 3 is a seed (χ(CP²) = N_c = 3, T15), providing the first occupied mode in d=4

**Ground state vs. lightest particle:**  
m_scale_d × S(1,d) = m_scale_d (since S(1,d)=1 for all d). This is the hypothetical n=1 mass. It equals the lightest occupied mode only in d=3 (down quark, n_down=1). In all other sectors the lightest occupied mode is at n > 1.

### §8. Coupling constants

| Coupling | Formula | Value | Geometry |
|----------|---------|-------|---------|
| g₃₃ | n_s² √(n_s+n_up) / 2 | 8√7 ≈ 21.166 | d=3 vacuum fixed-point; CP¹ base |
| g₄₄ | n_s · n_up / √(n_s+n_up) | 12/√7 ≈ 4.536 | d=3↔d=4 fixed-point |
| g₅₅ | 96 / g₂₂ | 96/722.5 ≈ 0.133 | Hopf universality |
| g₆₆ | 1/n_s | 1/4 | composite coupling (=1/χ(CP³)) |
| g₁₀,₁₀ | 1/n_s | 1/4 | = g₆₆ (shared) |
| g₂₂ | p² · q / 2 | 17²·5/2 = 722.5 | S³ Dirac spectrum + d=4 threshold |

**Anti-correlation with isometry dimension (T15f):** g_dd decreases as the isometry group dimension increases. SO(4) (6 generators): g₃₃ ≈ 21.2; SU(3) (8 generators): g₄₄ ≈ 4.5; SU(4) (15 generators): g₆₆ = 1/4 (at d=6). The physically strongest coupling sits in the sector with the smallest symmetry group. This is a trend across the three sectors named, not a law: the d=5 sector has isometry SO(6) with 15 generators — the same dimension as the d=6 SU(4) — yet g₅₅ ≈ 0.133 < g₆₆ = 1/4, so equal isometry dimension does not fix equal coupling and the monotonic reading fails at d=5.

**T9a — both Hopf coupling products equal 96:**
- g₃₃ × g₄₄ = 8√7 × 12/√7 = 96 (the √7 cancels exactly)
- g₂₂ × g₅₅ = 722.5 × (96/722.5) = 96 (by construction of g₅₅)
- 96 = N_c(N_c+1)³/2 = 3·64/2 (T15c)

The two independent derivation chains (d=3↔d=4 from vacuum fixed-point; d=2↔d=5 from Hopf universality) both yield 96 — this is the non-trivial content of T9a.

**Rank-1 coupling matrix:** G_{dd'} = √(g_dd) · √(g_d'd') = v_d · v_d'. All cross-sector couplings factorise. The effective coupling is g_eff(n,d) = g_dd / S(n,d) (geometric dilution).

### §9. Key algebraic identities used in derivations

**Hockey-stick identity:**  
S(n,d) = S(n,d−1) + S(n−1,d)  
Used in every mode-index recursion step; the algebraic engine of the Generation Tower.

**Simplex ground state universality:**  
S(1,d) = C(d,d) = 1 for all d ≥ 0.  
Forces n_down = 1 as the unique universal ground state mode.

**Vandermonde combination rule for bosons:**  
n_boson = n_fermion + d_partner − 1 (where d_partner is the mediating sector dimension).  
Source: Part 3 §11. Used to derive n_W, n_Z, n_H from fermion quantities.

**Triangular number relation for n_W:**  
S(n_e, 2) = C(14,2) = 91; n_W = 91 − n_ν₂ = 91 − 15 = 76.  
The electron's d=2 simplex number partitions into W mode and second neutrino mode.

**Muon fixed-point self-consistency:**  
n_μ = S(n_s, 4) = 35 AND n_μ = n_charm + n_ν₂ = 20 + 15 = 35.  
These being identical is the condition that forces n_s = 4.

**Back-reaction denominator factorisation:**  
n_up · n_s² · S(n_s,4) = n_up · k₀ · n_μ = 3 · 16 · 35 = 1680.  
Also = n_s · n_up · (n_s+n_up) · S(n_s,3) = 4·3·7·20 = 1680.
