## Part II — Patterns found, not yet placed in main documents

These have been verified numerically and are stated precisely. None has been assigned a theorem number or document location yet.

### §10. New additive forms of the mode indices

**Cross-sector ratio identity:**  
n_charm × N_c = n_ν₁ × N_f = 4 × n_ν₂  
✅ Polynomial identity (holds for all n_s). All three equal n_s(n_s−1)(n_s+1)(n_s+2)/6. Proof: n_charm = C(n_s+2,3), N_c = n_s−1 → product = C(n_s+2,3)·(n_s−1) = n_s(n_s+1)(n_s+2)(n_s-1)/6. n_ν₁ = C(n_s+1,3), N_f = n_s+2 → product = same. 4·n_ν₂ = 4·C(n_s+2,4) = same. Equivalently: n_ν₁/n_ν₂ = 4/N_f and n_charm/n_ν₁ = N_f/N_c. These are simplex ratio identities following directly from the binomial formula. The ratio of the first two neutrino mode indices equals 4/(n_s+2) for any n_s; at n_s=4 this is 2/3. Verified: n_s=3: 10=10=20 ✓; n_s=4: 60=60=60 ✓; n_s=5: 140=140=140 ✓.

**Charm–up spacing equals p:**  
n_charm − n_up = **p** (for all n_s)  
✅ By definition: p = S(n_s,3) − n_up = n_charm − n_up. Restated as a sector-spacing identity: the quark mode-index gap within d=4 from depth-0 to depth-1 equals the Dirac eigenstate count p that enters g₂₂.

**Neutrino spacing identity:**  
n_ν₃ − n_ν₂ = n_ν₁ − n_up (for all n_s)  
✅ Follows from n_ν₃ = n_ν₁ + n_ν₂ − n_up → n_ν₃ − n_ν₂ = n_ν₁ − n_up. At n_s=4: 22−15 = 10−3 = 7.  
❓ Additional claim: n_ν₃ − n_ν₂ = n_s + n_up = 7 at n_s=4. True numerically but fails at n_s=5 (n_ν₃−n_ν₂=16≠9). The value 7 = n_s+n_up also appears as the radicand under √ in g₃₃; whether this connection is structural is unresolved.

**Second neutrino minus electron equals q minus n_up:**  
n_ν₂ − n_e = q − n_up  
✅ Proof: n_ν₂ − n_e = [S(n_up,4)] − [S(n_up,3) + n_up] = [S(n_up,4)−S(n_up,3)] − n_up = q − n_up, using the definition q = S(n_up,4)−S(n_up,3) and the tower identity n_e = n_ν₁ + n_up. At n_s=4: q−n_up = 5−3 = 2, so n_ν₂ = n_e + 2.

**d=3 sector sum equals q:**  
n_down + n_strange = 1 + 4 = **5 = q** (for any n_s: n_down + n_s = n_s+1 = q)  
✅ Immediate from n_down = 1 and n_strange = n_s.

**d=4 sector sum equals Higgs:**  
n_up + n_charm + n_top = **n_H** (documented, §5)

**Higgs as Z plus electron plus down:**  
n_H = n_Z + n_e + n_down  
✅ Follows from n_H = n_Z + n_ν₂ − n_down (§5) and n_ν₂ = n_e + 2·n_down (from n_ν₂ − n_e = q − n_up = 2 at n_s=4, with n_down=1).

---

The following identities hold **only at n_s=4** (verified to fail at n_s=3,5,6). They are recorded as observed coincidences without mechanism. Status: ❓

**n_μ + n_ν₂ + n_ν₃ = 72 = n_top** ❓ (fails at n_s=3: 27≠12; n_s=5: 156≠266)

**n_top + n_τ = 95 = n_H** ❓ (fails at n_s=3: 19≠8; n_s=5: 318≠309)

**(n_s+1)(n_s+n_up) = n_μ** ❓ (fails at n_s=5: 54≠70)

**n_e + n_τ = 36 = N_f²** ❓ (fails at n_s=5: 76≠49)

**n_ν₁ + n_ν₃ = 32 = 2⁵** ❓ (fails at n_s=5: 71≠64; note 32 = 2^(n_s+1) only at n_s=4)

**n_charm = 2·n_ν₁** ❓ (C(n_s+2,3)/C(n_s+1,3) = (n_s+2)/(n_s-1) = 2 only at n_s=4; consequence of Pascal row n_s+1=5 having equal middle entries C(5,2)=C(5,3)=10)

**n_top − n_charm = n_s·n_e = 52** ❓ (fails at n_s=5: 231≠120)

**Each massive d=2 boson pairs with one matter mode to the Hopf product 96 = N_c(N_c+1)³/2 = g₃₃g₄₄ = g₂₂g₅₅** ❓ (2026-06-13, `claude/explore_mi_prism3.py`):
n_W + n_charm = 76 + 20 = 96 (charm, d=4);
n_Z + n_ν₂ = 81 + 15 = 96 (ν₂, d=5);
n_H + n_down = 95 + 1 = 96 (down, d=3).
One matter primary from each of the three matter sectors d=3,4,5, reflected through the carrier 96, lands on a d=2 boson — ascending bosons W<Z<H pair with descending matter charm>ν₂>down (the sideband-about-carrier reflection that surfaced in the modulational-comb run, §15 2026-06-13). All three are n_s=4 specific exactly as the single n_Z+n_ν₂ case is (fails at n_s=5: 310≠192; the value 96=N_c(N_c+1)³/2 is fixed by N_c while the indices scale with n_s). Honest caveat: 96 minus the seven primaries also produces four non-tower values {61,86,92,93}, so the pairing is an exact relation for {W,Z,H} but not a spurious-free generator. Not a structural identity; companion to the run #5 heavy-boson-off-top cascade (Part 3 §11) and the §13 Vandermonde forms, recorded here as the completed ❓ pattern. Do not promote to a Part document without an n_s-general derivation.

**Tau identities at n_s=4:**  
n_τ = n_charm + n_up = n_e + n_ν₁ = 23 🔵 (both are consequences of n_charm=2·n_ν₁ which is itself ❓)

**n_μ = n_ν₃ + n_e = 22 + 13 = 35** ❓ (fails at n_s=3: 13≠15; n_s=5: 75≠70. Equivalent to n_charm = 2·n_ν₁: n_ν₃ + n_e = 2n_ν₁ + n_ν₂ while n_μ = n_charm + n_ν₂. Found 2026-06-10, `claude/verify_gifts_fusion_stepping.py`)

**Three "+1" offsets in the compact tower form all equal n_down = 1. ❓** (2026-06-09, Fable-5 pass)

The compact tower relations for the three heaviest modes contain a "+1" offset whose origin is underived:
- n_τ = n_ν₃ + n_down (explicit in Part 5 §6; the +1 here is n_down = 1)
- n_top = T − r + 1 (compact form; r is a simplex evaluation; the +1 is uninterpreted)
- n_H = T + a + 1 (compact form; a is an additive index; the +1 is uninterpreted)

Observation: all three are consistent with the +1 being the down-quark seed n_down = 1. Reading the two underived offsets as T − r + n_down and T + a + n_down reduces the unexplained residue from "three bare integer units" to "why n_down = 1 attaches at the three anchor/heaviest-mode vertices." This is a physical question — the d=3 seed touching the three heaviest modes — rather than an arithmetic blemish. At n_s = 4 this is numerically invisible (n_down = 1 regardless), but the reframing is consistent with the DAG structure where every additive edge adds either a seed index or a simplex evaluation.

Status: ❓ Observation only; no mechanism derived. Fails to add new numerical content but unifies the three offsets under a single seed label.

### §11. Modular structure (mod n_s)

Writing n = n_s · a + r, the working set partitions into four residue classes mod n_s = 4:

| r | Members | Character |
|---|---------|----------|
| 0 | 0 (γ), 4 (s), 16 (k₀), 20 (c), 72 (t), 76 (W) | bosons and quark scale anchors; all divisible by n_s |
| 1 | 1 (d), 13 (e), 17 (p), 81 (Z) | d=3 ground state, d=6 ground state, g₂₂ parameter, Z boson |
| 2 | 10 (ν₁), 22 (ν₃) | **exclusively ν₁ and ν₃** |
| 3 | 3 (u), 15 (ν₂), 23 (τ), 35 (μ), 95 (H) | up quark plus lepton/Higgs cluster |

Residue 2 contains only ν₁ and ν₃. The algebraic reason: n_ν₃ − n_ν₁ = n_ν₂ − n_up = 15 − 3 = 12 = 3·n_s ≡ 0 mod n_s. The second neutrino escapes to residue 3 because S(n_up,4) − S(n_up,3) = q = 5 ≡ 1 mod 4, not 0.

### §12. Factor 19

19 = n_charm − 1 = n_W/n_s = n_H/(n_s+1). Numerically: n_W = 4·19 = 76, n_H = 5·19 = 95, n_τ+n_ν₂ = 38 = 2·19. No geometric interpretation has been found. The factorisation n_W = n_s·19 and n_H = (n_s+1)·19 are numerical properties of the specific values at n_s=4; they do not generalise (at n_s=5: n_W=270=2·5·27, n_H=309=3·103). The Z does not share the factor (81=3⁴). ❓ Numerological until a mechanism is identified.

### §13. W-Z mode gap equals q

n_Z − n_W = q = n_s + 1  
✅ Polynomial identity (holds for all n_s). Proof: n_W = g(d_ν, n_top) = d_ν + n_top − 1 = (n_s+1) + n_top − 1 = n_top + n_s. n_Z = g(d_ℓ, n_W) = d_ℓ + n_W − 1 = (n_s+2) + n_W − 1 = n_W + (n_s+1). So n_Z − n_W = n_s+1 = q exactly.

The same q appears in three further contexts (all polynomial identities or definitions):
- q = S(n_up,4) − S(n_up,3) (definition, §6)
- n_ν₂ − n_ν₁ = q (follows from q's definition and n_ν₁ = S(n_up,3), n_ν₂ = S(n_up,4))
- n_down + n_strange = q (= 1+n_s = n_s+1 = q, trivially)
- n_Z − n_W = q (proved above)

❓ Additional observation at n_s=4: q = 5 = χ(CP⁴), the Euler characteristic of the missing sector d=8. Whether the W-Z spacing equalling the missing sector's Euler characteristic is structural or coincidental at n_s=4 is unresolved.

### §13a. The Vandermonde g-rule transition graph on the mode set

Define g(d, n) = d + n − 1, the row index of mode (n,d) in the Pascal triangle. Computing g(d, n_j) for every d ∈ D = {2,3,4,5,6,10} and every n_j ∈ NS yields **19 NS → NS transitions** out of 90 candidate (d, n_j) pairs. (Hit rate ≈ 21%; random baseline ≈ 16%.)

**The 19 transitions, by sector:**

| d | NS → NS transitions |
|---|--------------------|
| 2 | 0→1, 3→4, 22→23 |
| 3 | 1→3, 13→15, 20→22 |
| 4 | 0→3, 1→4, 10→13, 20→23 |
| 5 | 72→76 |
| 6 | 10→15, 15→20, 76→81 |
| 10 | 1→10, 4→13, 13→22, 72→81 |

**Graph structure on NS:**  
- **Sources** (no in-edge): **{0, 35, 72, 95}** = {photon, muon, top, Higgs}.  
- **Component A** (reachable from photon via g-rule alone): {0, 1, 3, 4, 10, 13, 15, 20, 22, 23} — the ten lightest particles, equivalently the seeds plus depth-1 HS evaluations plus the electron and tau.  
- **Component B** (reachable from top): {72, 76, 81} — top → W (d=5) and top → Z (d=10), W → Z (d=6).  
- **Isolated sources**: {35, 95} — muon and Higgs have no g-rule predecessor in NS.

**Why the four sources.** For each source s, no (d, n_j) ∈ D × NS satisfies d + n_j − 1 = s with n_j ≠ s:

- 0 (photon): trivially a source.  
- 35 (muon): 35 = S(n_s, n_s) is the composite-square self-image; not a g-rule output of any other NS member.  
- 72 (top): the open eigenmode-selection mode index; not in the g-rule image of NS.  
- 95 (Higgs): the high-mass empirical closure; not in the g-rule image of NS.

**Structural reading.** The g-rule alone organises ten of the fifteen particles into a single connected component rooted at the photon. The W and Z sit one and two g-steps from the top quark, making them genuinely "top-anchored" rather than independent generators. Muon and Higgs are g-rule isolated: the muon is a pure depth-1 HS evaluation (S(4,4) = 35) and the Higgs is the empirical closure. Both top and Higgs are presently the un-derived rules of the generation tower, and both are graph sources — suggesting that the open derivation problem (§5, n_top) and the empirical closure (§5, n_H) are at the *structural* source of the spectrum, not anomalies layered on top of it.

**Own-sector stepping sub-pattern (❓, 2026-06-10).** Four of the 19 transitions use d' = d_own + 1, i.e. the g-step n → n + d_own: down (1,3) → strange (4), ν₁ (10,5) → ν₂ (15), ν₂ (15,5) → charm (20), top (72,4) → W (76). Equivalently, for exactly these four particles n + d_own is itself a tower mode index; the other eleven all fail (verified over the full 15, `claude/verify_gifts_fusion_stepping.py`). The steps chain — down → strange, ν₁ → ν₂ → charm, top → W — with each step equal to the particle's own sector dimension. Whether d' = d_own + 1 has a kernel or Hopf-chain interpretation is open. Side observation: strange (4,3) and up (3,4) share n + d = 7.

### §13b. Confluence of the generation tower — corrected analysis (2026-05-29)

**Two distinct predecessor relations.** The §13b analysis was initially run with the GENERAL additive predecessor: any n = a+b−c with a,b ∈ NS, c ∈ {0,1,3,4}. This was then corrected to examine the TOWER-SPECIFIC directed predecessor: the actual named operations of the generation tower (Part 2 §6). The two give very different results.

**GENERAL additive predecessor: cyclic graph, no source nodes.**
Under any a+b−c=n (a,b ∈ NS, c ∈ {0,1,3,4}), ALL 15 NS particles have predecessors in NS. Specifically:
- Photon (0,2): (1,3)+(3,4)−4 = 0 — predecessors: down and up.
- Down (1,3): (0,2)+(4,3)−3 = 1 — predecessors: photon and strange.
- Up (3,4): (0,2)+(4,3)−1 = 3 — predecessors: photon and strange.
- Strange (4,3): (1,3)+(3,4)−0 = 4 — predecessors: down and up.

The L-particles form a cycle: photon ↔ {down,up}; strange ↔ {down,up}. There are **no source nodes** under the general relation. The original §13b claim "seeds have no predecessors" was a verification gap: Test 5 hardcoded {(1,3),(4,3)} as seeds and skipped computing their predecessors.

**TOWER-SPECIFIC directed predecessor: acyclic DAG, unique seeds. ✅**
Using only the actual operations of the generation tower (Part 2 §6), the derivation is a finite acyclic DAG (verified: `has_cycle = False`). Each particle has a unique tower-derivation predecessor:

| Particle | Derivation | Tower predecessors |
|----------|------------|-------------------|
| photon (0,2) | d=2 ground state (n=0 trivially) | none — always present |
| down (1,3) | SEED: S(1,d)=1 for all d | none |
| strange (4,3) | COMPOSITE: n_s = n_d + n_u = 1+3 = 4 (🔶 MC-4.4); confirmed by muon fixed point S(4,4)=35 | {down, up} |
| up (3,4) | SEED: n_u = χ(CP²) = N_c = 3 (T15); unique ΔN=+2 image of ground seed | none |
| nu1 (10,5) | S(n_u,3) = 10 | {up} |
| charm (20,4) | S(n_s,3) = 20 | {strange} |
| electron (13,6) | n_nu1 + n_u = 13 | {nu1, up} |
| nu2 (15,5) | S(n_u,4) = 15 | {up} |
| muon (35,6) | n_charm + n_nu2 = 35 | {charm, nu2} |
| nu3 (22,5) | n_nu1 + n_nu2 − n_u = 22 | {nu1, nu2, up} |
| tau (23,10) | n_nu3 + n_down = 23 | {nu3, down} |
| top (72,4) | S(n_e,2) − n_charm + 1 = 72 | {electron, charm} |
| W (76,2) | g-rule: n_top + d_ν − 1 = 76 | {top} |
| Z (81,2) | g-rule: n_W + d_ℓ − 1 = 81 | {W} |
| Higgs (95,2) | n_u + n_charm + n_top = 95 | {up, charm, top} |

Derivation depths: down and up at 0 (seeds); strange, nu1, nu2 at 1; electron, charm, nu3 at 2; tau, muon, top at 3; W, Higgs at 4; Z at 5. All 13 derived particles (excluding photon ground state) reach {(1,3),(3,4)} in at most 5 backward steps. Verified: `all particles reduce to {down, up}`.

**Seed minimality.** Neither single seed alone generates all NS via tower operations (down alone: 1/15; up alone: 2/15). Together, {down, up} generate all 14 non-photon particles (14/15), with strange as their offset-additive composite at depth 1. The photon (n=0, d=2 ground state) is always present independently of the seeds — it does not require derivation.

**Why {(1,3),(3,4)} and not some other pair.** n_down=1 is forced by S(1,d)=1 for all d (the universal harmonic oscillator ground state); n_u=3 is forced by χ(CP²)=N_c=3 (T15, ✅). The composite n_s=4 = n_d+n_u is confirmed by T4 (Part 9) and χ(CP³)=4.

**Status.** The tower derivation is a finite acyclic DAG with unique source nodes {(1,3),(3,4)} (⭐, verified), composite (4,3) at depth 1. The general additive predecessor graph is cyclic with no source nodes (verified, §15 dead end).

**Seed sector derivation (🔵, 2026-05-29).** The seed sector is d=3: it is the observable spacetime sector and the first total space S³ of the complex Hopf chain, the natural starting point of the generation tower. The primitive seeds are n_d=1 (ground state S(1,d)=1 in d=3) and n_u=3 (forced by χ(CP²)=N_c=3, T15). The composite n_s=4 = n_d+n_u is confirmed by T4 (Part 9) and the muon fixed-point S(4,4)=35. Full sector assignments then propagate via the Hopf chain structure (d=3→4→5→6,10) and trivial automorphism group — see P8 update in Part 1.

**DAG automorphism group is trivial (⭐, 2026-05-29).** The tower DAG has no non-trivial automorphisms. The only degree-compatible candidate swaps are {down ↔ strange}, {nu1 ↔ nu2}, and {tau ↔ muon}; all three fail because they violate specific predecessor constraints:

- down ↔ strange: blocked because charm has predecessor {strange} only; no NS particle has predecessor {down} only.
- nu1 ↔ nu2: blocked because electron has predecessors {nu1, up}; no NS particle has predecessors {nu2, up}.
- tau ↔ muon: blocked because muon has predecessors {nu2, charm}; tau has predecessors {down, nu3} — different composition entirely.

The full backtracking search over all 15! possible permutations (with degree-pruning) confirms: **exactly one automorphism exists — the identity**. The particle labeling is uniquely determined by the DAG structure. No alternative sector/mode-index assignment preserves the derivation order. This resolves GPT's question about graph automorphisms: there is no relabeling freedom, so the coupling vector v and the rank-1 structure G_{dd'} = v_d v_{d'} are the unique coupling structure consistent with the tower DAG. The seed values (n_d=1, n_u=3) and composite n_s=4 remain the fundamental inputs; the automorphism result says that given those values, the entire labeling of the spectrum is rigid.

### §14. n_Z = N_c⁴ (N_c = 3 specific)

n_Z = 81 = 3⁴ = N_c⁴. This holds because:

n_Z = n_top + N_c² = N_c(N_c+1)(N_c+3) + N_c²

Setting this equal to N_c⁴ requires N_c⁴ − N_c(N_c+1)(N_c+3) − N_c² = 0, which factors as N_c(N_c−3)(N_c+1)² = 0. This is satisfied only at N_c = 3 (and the unphysical N_c = 0, −1).

**The form that generalises:** n_Z = n_top + N_c² = n_top + n_up². Valid for any N_c. The form n_Z = N_c⁴ is a numerical coincidence of our world's N_c = 3.

### §21. Composite hadron masses — GOR formula with IDWT chiral condensate

**Context (2026-05-29).** Pion, kaon, and heavier mesons are not elementary sector modes and cannot be assigned (n,d) pairs. Their masses must come from a formula using constituent quark masses. The natural candidate is the Gell-Mann–Oakes–Renner (GOR) relation:

$$m_{\rm meson}^2 = (m_{q_1} + m_{q_2}) \times B_0$$

where B₀ is the chiral condensate parameter. In IDWT, B₀ is fully determined (🔵):

$$B_0 = \Lambda_{\rm QCD} \times \frac{S(n_s,3)}{2} = \frac{N_c}{2} \times \frac{f_\pi^2}{m_{\rm scale,3}} = 2821 \text{ MeV}$$

where every factor is IDWT-derived: Λ_QCD = N_c f_π = 282.1 MeV, S(n_s,3) = 20, N_c = χ(CP²) = 3. Equivalently B₀ = Λ_QCD × n_s(n_s²−1)/6, the composite's own combinatorial factor divided into the QCD scale.

**Pseudoscalar meson predictions** (m_meson = √((m_q1+m_q2)×B₀)):

| Meson | Content | m_q1+m_q2 (MeV) | Predicted (MeV) | PDG (MeV) | Error |
|-------|---------|-----------------|-----------------|-----------|-------|
| π± | ūd | 6.88 | 139.3 | 139.6 | −0.2% |
| K± | ūs | 96.2 | 521.0 | 493.7 | +5.5% |
| K⁰ | d̄s | 98.7 | 527.8 | 497.6 | +6.1% |
| D± | c̄d | 1284.4 | 1903.6 | 1869.7 | +1.8% |
| D⁰ | c̄u | 1281.9 | 1901.7 | 1864.8 | +2.0% |
| Ds | c̄s | 1373.7 | 1968.7 | 1968.4 | 0.0% |

**Pattern:** The formula works precisely (< 3%) for cross-sector pseudoscalars (q from d=3, q̄ from d=4 or vice versa). It works at the leading-order ChPT level (5–6%) for kaons. It fails for same-sector vector mesons (φ, J/ψ) and B mesons: vector mesons are sector resonances (see §21a below), not GOR composites; B mesons require the heavy-quark formula; the b quark is a beat mode not a pure harmonic eigenmode.

The Gell-Mann–Okubo relation 4m_K² − m_π² = 3m_η², applied to IDWT predictions, gives m_η = 596 MeV (PDG: 548, +9%) — consistent with leading-order SU(3) ChPT accuracy.

**Baryons (2026-05-31, `files/idwt.py`).** The correct formula is the (N_c−1) colour-bond formula, not GOR. When one quark in a colour-singlet baryon is replaced by a heavier quark, each of the remaining (N_c−1) = 2 = χ(CP¹) colour bonds contributes the mass difference:

m(baryon) = m_N + (N_c−1) × Σ(m_s − m_replaced)

Key structural identity discovered: N_c × Λ_QCD / n_u² = m_s exactly (94.04 MeV), so m_N = N_c × Λ_QCD + m_s — the nucleon mass is the colour confinement scale plus the strange quark mass, forced by seeds alone.

Results: Λ +0.3%, Ξ⁰ −0.9%, Ξ⁻ −1.4%. The Σ(uds) has identical quark content to Λ, so the formula gives both the same mass; the 77 MeV Σ−Λ difference is a small same-type residual the formula does not resolve. The Ω(sss, J=3/2) is in the baryon decuplet, outside this formula's scope.

**Status:** 🔵 (formula verified for N, Λ, Ξ). The small Σ−Λ residual (77 MeV) is not resolved by the formula. Script: `files/idwt.py`.

**Two-formula picture and the bottom quark (2026-05-29, `files/idwt.py`).** There are two distinct mass formulas depending on whether m_quark ≪ Λ_QCD (chiral regime) or m_quark ≫ Λ_QCD (heavy-quark regime). The boundary is at Λ_QCD = 282 MeV.

*Chiral (light quarks):* m² = (m_q1+m_q2)×B₀ as above — u, d, s quarks.

*Heavy-quark binding formula* (🔵):
$$m_{\rm meson} = m_{q_1} + m_{q_2} + \sqrt{m_{\rm heavy} \times \Lambda_{\rm QCD}}$$

| Meson | Predicted | PDG | Error |
|-------|-----------|-----|-------|
| B+ | 5269.3 MeV | 5279.3 | −0.19% |
| B⁰ | 5271.9 | 5279.7 | −0.15% |
| Bs | 5361.2 | 5366.9 | −0.11% |
| Υ(1S) | 9448.3 | 9460.3 | −0.13% |
| J/ψ | 3160.3 | 3096.9 | +2.0% |

D mesons sit at the crossover: both formulas give ~1% accuracy.

**The k₀ = n_s² connection.** The binding energy of every B meson and bottomonium is:
$$E_{\rm bind} = \sqrt{m_b \times \Lambda_{\rm QCD}} = m_{\rm scale,3} \times \sqrt{N_c \, S(n_s,3) \times \sqrt{S(n_s^2,3)\,S(n_s^2+1,3)}}$$

The beat level k₀ = n_s² = 16 (already derived in Part 2 as the three-resonance coincidence) appears here again: the same structural fact that fixes m_b also determines the binding energy of all B mesons. The binding energy is fully expressible in terms of n_s, N_c, and m_scale_3 — no external input.

**Remaining:** (a) J/ψ +2.0% — the expansion parameter Λ_QCD/m_c = 0.22 makes the leading-order formula approximate; the J/ψ–η_c difference is a vector–pseudoscalar object-type distinction (as ρ vs π), not a single-formula correction. (b) Σ−Λ (77 MeV): a small same-type residual. φ(1020) is handled as a d=3 sector resonance (§21a). Script: `files/idwt.py`.

### §21a. d=3 hadronic resonance spectrum — vector mesons as sector modes (🔵, 2026-05-31)

The d=3 sector supports modes at $m = m_{\rm scale,3} \times S(n,3)$ for integer $n \geq 9$. These modes are not co-fixed-points and are therefore not stable particles; they appear as broad short-lived resonances. Unlike the pseudoscalar mesons (which are GOR composites), the vector mesons are identified with specific modes in this tower. The mode indices are forced by seed algebra alone (n_up=3, n_down=1, composite n_s=n_strange=4):

$$n_\rho = n_s + n_{\rm up} + 2n_{\rm down} = 4+3+1+1 = 9 \qquad ({\rm u\bar{u}/d\bar{d}\ nonet,\ J=1})$$
$$n_\phi = 2n_s + 2n_{\rm down} = 4+4+1+1 = 10 \qquad ({\rm s\bar{s}\ nonet,\ J=1})$$

The step $n_\phi - n_\rho = n_{\rm strange} - n_{\rm up} = 4 - 3 = 1$ reflects replacing one u quark by one s quark in the composite: each such replacement shifts n by exactly $\Delta n = n_{\rm strange} - n_{\rm up} = 1$.

| n | S(n,3) | IDWT (MeV) | PDG (MeV) | Error | Resonance |
|---|--------|------------|-----------|-------|-----------|
| 9 | 165 | 775.8 | 775.3 (ρ) / 782.7 (ω) | +0.1% | ρ/ω (uū/dd̄) |
| 10 | 220 | 1034.4 | 1019.5 (φ) | +1.4% | φ (ss̄) |
| 11 | 286 | 1344.8 | 1318.2 (a₂) | +2.0% | a₂(1320) tensor |
| 12 | 364 | 1711.5 | 1720 (ρ(1700)) | −0.5% | ρ(1700) excited |
| 18 | 1140 | 5360.3 | 5366.9 (B_s) | −0.1% | B_s (bs̄) |
| 19 | 1330 | 6253.7 | 6274.5 (B_c) | −0.3% | B_c (bc̄) |
| 22 | 2024 | 9516.8 | 9460.3 (Υ(1S)) | +0.6% | Υ(1S) (bb̄) |

The ρ is independently confirmed at +0.069% by the cross-sector filter $\Gamma_{346}$ (Part 2 §10). All other entries use the sector mode formula.

Additional mode index identities (all exact from seeds):
- $n=18 = n_{\rm charm} - n_{\rm up} + n_{\rm down} = 20-3+1$ (B_s: one b + one s̄)
- $n=19 = n_{\rm charm} - n_{\rm down} = 20-1$ (B_c: one b + one c̄)
- $n=22 = n_\tau - n_{\rm down} = 23-1$ (Υ(1S): bb̄ ground state)

**Status: 🔵** (sector mode formula verified across 7 resonances). Script: `files/idwt.py` (hadronic resonance spectrum section).

### §22. Co-fixed-point stability via l-parity selection (⭐ exact + 🔵 partial, 2026-05-31)

**The kernel angular structure.** The coupling $(ξ_d \cdot ξ_{d'})^2$ decomposes on $S^{d-1}$ into $l=0$ (scalar) and $l=2$ (tensor) components only. Each application of $V_{\rm kernel}$ changes the sector angular momentum quantum number by $0$ or $\pm 2$. Angular momentum parity (even vs odd $l$) is therefore an exact conserved quantity under all powers of $V_{\rm kernel}$.

**d=3 level structure.** The d=3 sector has $d+1=4$ harmonic oscillator coordinates ($\mathbb{R}^4$ oscillator). Level $N = n-1$ contains angular momentum values $l = N, N-2, \ldots, 0$ or $1$ (same parity as $N$).

| n | Level N | l values | Parity | In Σ? | Kernel-reachable from l=0 seed? |
|---|---------|----------|--------|-------|----------------------------------|
| 1 | 0 | {0} | even | ✓ | yes (seed) |
| 2 | 1 | {1} | odd | — | **NO** (l-parity blocks) |
| 3 | 2 | {0,2} | even | — | yes (l=0 and l=2 components) |
| 4 | 3 | {1,3} | odd | ✓ | **NO** (l-parity blocks intra-sector) |
| 5 | 4 | {0,2,4} | even | — | yes |
| 6 | 5 | {1,3,5} | odd | — | **NO** |

**Exact result (⭐).** All non-$\Sigma_{\rm pairs}$ modes at odd levels ($n=2,6,8,10,\ldots$ in $d=3$) are permanently disconnected from the $l=0$ seeds by $V_{\rm kernel}$. No power of the kernel can generate odd-$l$ modes from even-$l$ starting points. These modes cannot be excited from the vacuum and cannot be sustained by the coupling chain. Their exclusion from Σ_pairs is exact.

**Strange quark (n=4) special case.** The strange quark sits at level $N=3$ (odd $l$ only). It is protected from intra-sector destabilisation by the same l-parity rule. Its stability comes instead from the cross-sector coupling $V_{34}$: the up quark ($n=3$, $d=4$) is at level $N=2$ in the $d=4$ oscillator, which has $l=0$ and $l=2$ components — making the cross-sector coupling from the $l=0$ seed allowed. The generation tower chain ($n=1,d=3$) $\to$ ($n=3,d=4$) $\to$ ($n=4,d=3$) then closes via the hockey-stick identity.

**l=0 kernel matrix elements (numerical, d=3).** Computed from harmonic oscillator mode functions ($\lambda_3 = 4.820$, $w=\sqrt{\lambda_3}$):

| n_r | n (d=3) | I(n) | ME ~ $(g_{33}/3) \cdot I_{\rm seed} \cdot I(n)$ | In Σ? |
|-----|---------|------|------|-------|
| 0 | 1 | 1.475 | 15.35 | ✓ (self) |
| 1 | 3 | 0.602 | 6.27 | — |
| 2 | 5 | 0.224 | 2.33 | — |
| 3 | 7 | 0.081 | 0.84 | — |
| 4 | 9 | 0.029 | 0.30 | — |

The matrix elements fall geometrically with $n_r$. The non-$\Sigma_{\rm pairs}$ even-level modes ($n=3,5,7,\ldots$) do couple to the seed, with matrix elements proportional to $I(n_r)$.

**Cross-sector coupling (n=1,d=3) → (n=3,d=4).** The up quark level $N=2$ in $d=4$ has an $l=0$ component. Numerically: $I_4(n=3, l=0) = 0.389$, giving cross-sector matrix element $\sim 1.88$ in sector units (with $g_{34} = 4\sqrt{6}$). The coupling is non-zero, confirming the generation tower connection is active.

**Self-energy of n=3 mode (numerical).** The n=3 mode at $m_{n=3} = S(3,3) \times m_{\rm scale,3} = 47.0$ MeV receives a 2nd-order self-energy correction from its coupling to the $n=1$ seed:

$$\delta E^{(2)}_{n=3} = \frac{|\langle n=3 | V_{33}^{l=0} | n=1 \rangle|^2}{m_{n=3} - m_{n=1}} = \frac{6.27^2}{47.0 - 4.7} \approx 0.93 \text{ sector units} \approx 16.4 \text{ MeV}$$

Adding the 1st-order self-coupling ($\delta E^{(1)} = 2.56$ sector units $\approx 12.0$ MeV), the total shift is $\approx +16.4$ MeV, placing the mode at $\approx 63.4$ MeV. This is between the Σ_pairs modes (down quark at 4.7 MeV, strange at 94.0 MeV) and falls on no sector resonance. The mode is off-resonance with the self-consistent coupling structure.

However: in a discrete harmonic oscillator spectrum, 2nd-order perturbation theory shifts eigenvalues but does not give them finite width. Exact irreversibility requires the mode to couple to a continuous spectrum. The multi-sector coupling chain ($d=3\to d=4\to\cdots\to d=10$) acts as a bath that time-averages the return amplitude to zero via incommensurability (§15 ✅), but these $d\le 10$ towers are countable and discrete and cannot supply a continuous spectral measure. The $d>10$ free-dimension spectrum is the bath that can (see addendum below; Part 4 §4).

**Dephasing in the multi-sector coupled system (🔵).**

Even-level non-$\Sigma_{\rm pairs}$ modes are not eigenstates of $H$: their self-energy shifts them off every $\Sigma_{\rm pairs}$ resonance, and they have nonzero off-diagonal matrix elements to the mode towers of the five active sectors. The cross-sector mass scales are incommensurate (all ratios irrational except the $\mu$–$\tau$ pair; §15 ✅), so no common revival period exists and the time-averaged return amplitude vanishes (Wiener). The $d\le 10$ mode towers form a countable discrete spectrum, however, and a countable discrete spectrum gives an almost-periodic survival amplitude that recurs (Poincaré) — time-averaged dephasing is not the same as permanent decay. Exact irreversibility requires the reduced spectral measure to be continuous; the $d>10$ free-dimension continuum is the bath that can supply it (see addendum below; Part 4 §4). Establishing this coupling is the remaining step the status 🔵 records.

Decoherence time: $\tau \sim 1/(\text{ME} \times m_{\rm scale,3})$. For $n=3$: ME $\approx 6.3$ sector units, $\tau \approx 0.034\ \text{MeV}^{-1} \sim 1/m_{\rm scale,3}$.

**Co-fixed-point stability derivation complete (🔵).** All non-$\Sigma_{\rm pairs}$ modes are unstable:
- Odd-level modes: $l$-parity selection rule (⭐ exact)
- Even-level modes: off-diagonal mixing + time-averaged dephasing; exact irreversibility requires d>10 continuum bath (🔵)

The even-level 🔵 is the proven ceiling, not merely the current best: the seed-coupling overlap has no node at the kernel weight $s=3/2$ (its only zero is $s=1$), so the coupling is strictly nonzero for every even-level mode and no exact $l$-parity-style cut exists for this class under the $(\xi\cdot\xi')^2$ kernel (§15, 2026-06-05; `files/idwt.py` STEP 34). The open item is the EOM derivation of the dephasing, not a further exact cut.

**Quantitative revival amplitude bound (2026-06-09, `files/idwt.py` STEP 49).** The within-sector Rabi coupling between a non-tower even-level mode and the nearest tower mode gives a maximum return amplitude of order $(J/\Delta S)^2$, where $\Delta S = S(n_{\rm nt},d) - S(n_{\rm tower},d)$ is the energy detuning in simplex units. By spectral independence (⭐, sum-free $S$-values, Part 1 §5 Uniqueness Theorem), all detunings are strictly positive. Summing over all non-tower even modes per sector:

| Sector $d$ | $\sum_n (J/\Delta S)^2$ |
|:---:|:---:|
| 2 | $2.0\times10^{-5}$ |
| 3 | $4.2\times10^{-4}$ |
| 4 | $5.5\times10^{-5}$ |
| 5 | $1.7\times10^{-7}$ |
| 6 | $1.2\times10^{-10}$ |
| 10 | $1.1\times10^{-17}$ |

The worst case ($d=3$) bounds the coherent within-sector return amplitude at $\lesssim 2\%$; all other sectors are smaller by factors of $10^1$–$10^{13}$. Cross-sector revival is separately time-averaged to zero by the incommensurability lemma (✅, §15 STEP 40). Total return probability therefore $\lesssim 4\times10^{-4}$. This is the tightest available quantitative bound on T0.5 even-level dephasing; it does not reach exact zero (which would require the vacuum-dimension bath argument), so 🔵 remains the correct status.

**Addendum — the even-level bath is the d>10 continuum, not the d≤10 towers; spectral-measure reframing and an exact-width-cancellation null (2026-06-10, opus, `claude/explore_bic_selection.py`).** Sharpens the even-level argument and resolves the internal tension between the paragraph above (line 585: exact decay "requires the mode to couple to a continuum") and the "infinite-dimensional dephasing" paragraph (which treats the countable multi-sector tower as that continuum).

*Reframing (RAGE/Wiener, rigorous).* A mode $(n,d)$ is a stable particle $\iff$ its spectral measure under the full $H=H_0+V_{\rm kernel}$ has a point mass (atom); it decays $\iff$ the measure is purely continuous (survival amplitude $\to 0$ by Riemann–Lebesgue). This is the exact form of "dephasing," and it matches T0 ("physical masses are eigenvalues of the projected operator" — eigenvalues are the point spectrum).

*No-go (closes the d≤10 route).* The five active sectors $d\le 10$ each carry a **countable, discrete** mode tower, and $S(n,d)\sim n^d$ makes the level spacing grow, not accumulate. A countable discrete spectrum gives an **almost-periodic** survival amplitude: by Wiener's theorem its time-average vanishes, but it **recurs** (Poincaré) — it never reaches an exact continuous measure. So coupling to the $d\le 10$ towers, however many, cannot upgrade the even-level cut to ✅; the residual $\lesssim 4\times10^{-4}$ is the structural ceiling of *that* bath, not a temporary bound. Demonstrated numerically on the actual IDWT energies $S(n,d)m_{\rm scale,d}$: the discrete sector bath drives the even non-tower mode $(3,3)$ down to $|A|=0.12$ but it **recurs to $0.88$**; an equal-width genuine continuum decays it to $|A|=0$ with the revival $\to 0$ as the level spacing $\to 0$ (`explore_bic_selection.py` part a).

*The actual bath.* The continuum line 585 requires is the **$d>10$ free-dimension spectrum**: by "Bound within, free without" (subsection below) the outer dimensions carry absolutely continuous spectrum $[0,\infty)$ and the mode is uniformly present there ("present, not absent"). This is the "vacuum-dimension bath" line 612 flags as the missing ingredient — now identified concretely. The seed-coupling overlap's non-node at $s=3/2$ ($J(n_r,3/2)\ne 0$, STEP 34) — the fact that *blocks* an exact intra-sector $l$-parity cut — is exactly the nonzero coupling that *drives* irreversible decay into this continuum: the obstruction becomes the mechanism.

*Tower protection — exact-width-cancellation test (NULL).* For a tower mode to remain in the point spectrum while its radiative coupling to the $[0,\infty)$ continuum is open, its decay width at the tower site would have to vanish by an exact cancellation. IDWT's rank-1 kernel $g_{dd'}=v_dv_{d'}$ (T2) makes the decay matrix rank-1 ($\det\Gamma=0$), the structural setting in which such a cancellation could occur. But the concrete test fails: scanning adjacent pairs $(n,n+1)$ with continuum couplings modelled by $J(n_r,3/2)^2$ and inter-mode coupling $V=\sqrt{b_nb_{n+1}}$, the narrowed-width pattern tracks only the odd/even parity of $n$ (an artifact of the $n_r=\lfloor(n-1)/2\rfloor$ overlap proxy), not tower membership, and the exact zero-width condition $V(\gamma_1-\gamma_2)=(E_1-E_2)\sqrt{\gamma_1\gamma_2}$ is not satisfied at the tower sites — so no protective width-cancellation forms in this model. A coupling-level mechanism that zeroes a tower mode's width is therefore **not** established by this proxy; the tower-protection question remains 🔶.

*Net.* Status unchanged (odd-level ⭐ exact; even-level 🔵/🔶). The advance is structural: the open problem is re-posed from the unreachable "prove the discrete multi-sector dephasing is irreversible" to the well-posed pair (i) compute the Wigner–Weisskopf width of a non-tower even mode coupling into the $d>10$ free-dimension continuum (occupied-sector presence there is established), and (ii) decide whether any exact width-cancellation protects the tower modes — the width-cancellation route is now a logged null, and the 2026-06-13 radiative-width companion below settles (ii) negatively: the stable members carry no width suppression, so their stability is target-absence, not a protective mechanism. Wording items for Fedge (report-before-edit, left unedited): Part 7 §1.2 and the line-589 paragraph above state "infinite-dimensional ⟹ permanent dephasing"; a countable *discrete* spectrum still recurs (Wiener), so the bath must be named as the $d>10$ continuum specifically, not the multi-sector towers.

---

### Bound within, free without — a particle in the dimensions beyond its sector (resolves a Fedge question, 2026-06-04)

**Question.** A particle is bound in its $d$ sector dimensions. In the dimensions beyond $d$ (the ones it is "not in"), does it (A) drift freely as a localized lump, (B) stay put at a point, or float in some other sense — and does any of it survive normalizability?

**Setup.** Harmonic sector confinement $V_d = \lambda_d r^2$ (Part 4 §3.9); ground state Gaussian of width $L_d = \lambda_d^{-1/4}$, normalizable on $\Xi_d$ ($\int_{\Xi_d}|\chi|^2 = 1$). A $d$-particle feels $V_d$ in its $d$ coordinates only; in every dimension past $d$ it is **free** ($H_{\rm outer} = -\Delta_{\rm outer}$), since the $d=7,8,9$ band carries no sector geometry (T3) and $V_{10}$ belongs to the tau, not to a $d<10$ mode.

**Result (✅ for the normalizability core).**
- $-d^2/dy^2$ on a free direction has spectrum $[0,\infty)$: no negative eigenvalue, hence **no normalizable bound state in a free dimension.** Solutions: $e^{iky}$ ($E>0$, momentum), $\text{const}$ ($E=0$, uniform), $e^{+|k|y}$ ($E<0$, divergent — unphysical).
- The unique zero-momentum (rest) configuration in a free dimension is the **constant.** So a massive particle, in the dimensions beyond its sector, is **uniform — present everywhere, pinned to no point.** This is "floats freely," made precise.
- Localizing to width $\Delta$ costs $E_{\rm kin}\sim 1/(2m\Delta^2)$ (uncertainty); rest ($E\to0$) $\Leftrightarrow \Delta\to\infty \Leftrightarrow$ uniform. So "stay put at a point" (B) is not a rest state, and "drift as a lump" (A) needs momentum (excited). Neither as posed — the answer is **uniform co-presence.**
- **Normalizability:** the mode is normalized on $\Xi_d$. Uniformity in the outer dims is the nesting embedding $C^\infty(\Xi_d)\subset C^\infty(\Xi_{d'})$; the divergent "norm over the outer volume" only says "normalize on $\Xi_d$ — it is a $d$-object." Cross-sector coupling is the overlap on the shared coords (Part 1 §3g), consistent with the §3i "already there" framing.
- **Massless vs massive:** dispersion $E^2 = p_{\rm outer}^2 + m^2$. $m>0$ admits a rest state (uniform); $m=0$ (photon) has no rest frame, so its free state in the outer dims necessarily carries momentum → **propagation.** Same principle; masslessness upgrades uniform presence to propagation. Orientation freedom (rotating $\Xi_d$) is the separate, symmetry-protected, always-normalizable piece.

**Status.** ✅ for the normalizability core (no bound state in a free direction; rest = uniform; normalize on $\Xi_d$). The reading "uniform presence = floats freely" and the massless→propagation upgrade are 🔵 structural interpretation. Placed in Part 1 §3i as the "Bound within, free without" subsection (after "Cross-sector interaction involves no separate objects"), carrying the ✅/🔵 split. Recorded in `files/idwt.py` as STEP 33 (computation block in the compute section, output block at the end). Exploration script: `claude/explore_floating_normalizability.py`.

**Addendum — the dimensions beyond $d$ are not a selective channel for the even-level distinction (2026-06-10, `claude/explore_t05_vacuum_coupling.py`).** Part 7 §1.2 frames the even-level non-members as excluded by coupling to the $d>10$ dimensions, where the wave is uniformly present (Part 1 §3i) and any feature entering disperses (T5; Part 4 §3.12.2). Tested whether that coupling can distinguish a persistent (co-fixed-point) sector excitation from one that disperses. The self-coupling kernel $(\xi_d\cdot\xi_{d'})^2$ is quadratic, so it links a level-$N$ sector excitation ($N=n-1$; harmonic sector well, Part 4 §3.10) to level $N\pm2$, with strength $|\langle N{-}2|r^2|N\rangle|^2 \propto N(N-1)$. That strength has no special value at the tower indices (only the $n=1$ ground state, $N=0$, gives zero), grows monotonically with $n$, and is shared by members and non-members — the electron ($n=13$, $d=6$) and the $d=3$ non-member $n=13$ both give $N(N-1)=132$; $\nu_2$ ($n=15$, $d=5$) and the $d=3$ non-member $n=15$ both give $182$. So the wave's coupling into the dimensions beyond $d$ cannot be what selects the tower: it singles out no index, and a coupling strong enough to disperse the non-members would disperse the heaviest members ($t$, $H$, $Z$, largest $N(N-1)$) faster, contradicting their persistence. The dimensions beyond $d$ are therefore a non-selective channel. Consequence for the standing goal: the even-level distinction between a persistent excitation and a dispersing one has to come from the self-coupled wave's own dynamics — the nonlinear equation of motion for $\Psi_\infty$ — not from coupling to the dimensions beyond $d$. This is consistent with §1.2's own dephasing reading (the wave's amplitude at a non-member index spreads across the tower with no revival) and redirects effort there. No document status edited.

**Companion — the self-consistency / standing-wave closure is also non-selective for the even-level index (2026-06-10, `claude/explore_t05_closure.py`).** The other quanta-free handle on T0.5 is the existence side: a particle is a self-consistent standing solution of the nonlinear self-coupled equation $D\phi + W[|\phi|^2]\phi = E\phi$, and the proposal is that the 15 are the closure of the seeds under that condition. Tested the three closure conditions a standing configuration of the one wave can obey; none selects the even-level tower index. (i) *Intra-sector* — the self-generated well is harmonic ($\lambda_d=(g_{dd}/2)^{2/3}$, a density-sourced fixed point independent of which level sits in it; Part 4 §3.10), so it admits a standing state at every level $N=0,1,2,\dots$ and singles out no $n$. (ii) *Closure under kernel links* — the quadratic kernel allows $\Delta N=0,\pm2$ links with nonzero radial overlap ($J(n_r,3/2)\neq0$, STEP 34), so every massive member has an allowed link to a same-sector non-member (28 such member→non-member links among the 15); the 15-set is not an invariant/closed configuration. (iii) *Stationarity* — a transition is driven only between degenerate modes; $S(n,d)$ is strictly increasing (no intra-sector degeneracy) and all cross-sector scale ratios are irrational except the $d=6/d=10$ commensurate pair (STEP 40), whose only coincidences are between non-members (e.g. $(1,6)$–$(1,10)$), so stationarity isolates nothing. The one place the kernel forbids a link outright is $l$-parity (odd levels) — which is exactly the part already ⭐ exact. **Net:** two independent IDWT routes — coupling to the dimensions beyond $d$ (addendum above) and the standing-wave self-consistency closure (here) — both come back non-selective for the even-level index. The exact structural cut exists only where the kernel forbids a connection outright ($l$-parity, odd levels). For the even levels the distinction between a persistent and a dispersing excitation is a robustness/persistence difference (the dephasing hierarchy), i.e. a quantitative 🔵 statement, not an exact theorem — which is the honest reading of the T0.5 even-level status. What is NOT excluded by (i)–(iii): a finer self-consistency that fixes mode amplitudes (the nonlinear equation does fix them, via the $\lambda_d=(g_{dd}/2)^{2/3}$ well and $m_{{\rm scale},d}^2=g_{dd}\langle|\Psi^{(d)}|^2\rangle$) and asks whether the amplitude fixed point exists only at the tower indices.

**Amplitude-pinned self-consistency tested — also non-selective, for a counting reason (2026-06-11, `claude/explore_t05_amplitude.py`).** Pinning the amplitude makes the well an output of the occupied density rather than a free background, which is the last place the index could be fixed dynamically. It is not: the self-consistency equations fix the *continuous* data $(\lambda_d, m_{{\rm scale},d})$ — already T9/T11 — and the mode index $n$ does not enter them at leading order ($\lambda_d=(g_{dd}/2)^{2/3}$ is ground-state-sourced and carries no $n$; the same $\lambda_d$ holds for any occupancy). The only $n$-dependence is the sub-leading back-reaction dressing, IDWT's geometric dilution $g_{\rm eff}=g_{dd}/S(n,d)$; sorted across all low modes, members and non-members interleave with no separating threshold (143 non-members fall inside the member $g_{\rm eff}$ range, which runs from the seed's $\approx21$ down to $\sim10^{-8}$). A scalar/continuous condition cannot pin a discrete integer set: per sector the self-consistency supplies $\sim2$ real constraints, fixing the well and the scale, and *zero* constraints on which integer levels are occupied. **This closes the self-consistency route.** Across the whole investigation — coupling to the dimensions beyond $d$, kernel-link closure, stationarity, and now amplitude-pinning — every condition the wave's continuous self-dynamics supplies is non-selective for the index. The one exact discrete selector in the dynamics is $l$-parity, and it fixes parity only (kills the odd levels). The 15-index selection is therefore finer than anything the continuous dynamics determines; it is irreducibly the combinatorial generation tower, and the dynamical necessity of *that specific* combinatorial structure is the open core of T0.5 (the standing-goal residue). Honest status reading unchanged: odd-level exclusion ⭐ exact ($l$-parity); even-level/index selection a combinatorial backbone (🔶) plus a quantitative persistence hierarchy (🔵); no ✅ is available for it from the continuous dynamics. No document status edited.

**Addendum — the $d>10$ vacuum-dimension bath is dynamically closed: zero decay width at all orders (2026-06-11, `claude/explore_t05_outer_width.py`).** This closes T0.5 sub-problem (a) — the width of a non-tower even mode coupling into the $d>10$ continuum — negatively and exactly. The kernel $\tfrac12\sum_{d,d'\in D} g_{dd'}(\xi_d\cdot\xi_{d'})^2 J_d J_{d'}$ has support only on sector coordinates $1..10$: the dot product runs over the shared coordinates, so coordinate axis $j$ appears in the $(d,d')$ term iff $j\le\min(d,d')$ — the band $7$–$9$ enters only through the $g_{10,10}$ self-term, and no coordinate beyond 10 appears in any term (verified programmatically over $D^2$). Translations of every coordinate beyond 10 are therefore exact symmetries of the full action, the conjugate outer momentum is conserved, and a stationary sector mode — outer-uniform by Part 1 §3i (✅), an exact zero of outer momentum — has identically vanishing matrix element to every outer-momentum state $k\neq0$. Any product of outer-independent operators is outer-independent, so the vanishing holds at all orders in the kernel: the width into the $d>10$ absolutely continuous spectrum is zero by symmetry, for members and non-members alike. ✅ (symmetry consequence of the stated action). Numerical demonstration: a toy sector⊗outer-ring evolution under an outer-independent coupling keeps the $k\neq0$ outer occupation at $5.9\times10^{-28}$ (machine zero), while an artificial $\cos(qy)$ control coupling populates $k=\pm q$ to $8.5\times10^{-2}$ — the zero is structural (absence of outer support), not numerical. Consequence: the "decay into the $d>10$ continuum" completion route that the 🔵 status of Part 7 §1.2 records as its remaining step is not merely unproved — it is unavailable under the current action. This sharpens the 2026-06-10 addendum (non-selective channel) to a closed channel. (The §1.2 and Part 9 T0.5 wording edits were executed 2026-06-11 with Fedge's approval; the result is recorded as `files/idwt.py` STEP 64.)

**Companion — the only absolutely continuous spectrum coupled to sector excitations is the spacetime momentum continuum; channel catalog and the stability equivalence (same script).** All active sector wells are purely discrete ($\sigma_{\rm ess}=\emptyset$, harmonic; Part 4 §3.13 Part I); the band $7$–$9$ and $d>10$ free directions are closed by the symmetry above (for non-tau modes the band coordinates are touched only by $g_{10,10}$, which acts through the $d=10$ density, itself well-bound in all 10 coordinates). What remains is the spatial momentum of the propagation factor $\psi(x)$: exact irreversibility of a non-member's dephasing, if it exists, must be ordinary radiation — kernel redistribution of the excitation into lighter linked configurations carrying continuous spatial momentum. The downward-channel catalog over the 14 single tower modes: every member with $n\ge3$ has a parity-allowed same-sector link $(n,d)\to(n-2,d)$ ($N$ and $N-2$ share parity; radial ME generically nonzero, proved nonzero for $d=3$, $l=0$ at the kernel weight, STEP 34), and in all 13 such cases the target is a non-member; only the $N=0$ ground mode $d\,(1,3)$ is structurally closed. The spatial-radiation channel is therefore again non-selective in itself — and phenomenologically right-shaped: the members observed to be unstable ($s,c,t,b,W,Z,H,\mu,\tau$) all have open links, and the channel picture assigns finite widths to exactly such modes. The sharp residue is the other direction: the members observed to be absolutely stable with **open** links — $e\,(13,6)\to(11,6)$ (would release $0.29$ MeV into spatial radiation), $u\,(3,4)\to(1,4)$, and the neutrinos $(10,5)\to(8,5)$, $(15,5)\to(13,5)$, $(22,5)\to(20,5)$ — are protected only if their downward targets are absent from the physical spectrum, which is exactly the even-level selection of T0.5. **At kernel level, the T0.5 even-level selection is equivalent to the absolute stability of the electron, the u quark, and the neutrinos**, giving T0.5 a sharp empirical witness ($\tau_e > 6.6\times10^{28}$ yr; proton-decay bounds): the selection does falsifiable work, while its derivation remains the open core (status unchanged: 🔶 backbone + 🔵 persistence hierarchy). Caveats: kernel-level statements (EOM confirmation open, MC-4 line); the radiated configuration and the rate require the nonlinear redistribution calculation (Part 6, "sector transition rates"); sector-granular coupling rows (`idwt.py` STEP 2b) mean no conserved coupling structure closes a same-sector downward channel — only non-existence of the target does; for $d=5$ the anomalous BdG block vanishes (STEP 36) but the normal density-channel link is the relevant object here, its radial ME not separately computed; the $b$ quark (beat resonance) poses a structurally different channel question. No document status edited.

**Companion — the stable members are not protected by a small radiative width; their stability is the absence of the downward target, and the tower is downward-independent (necessary, not sufficient) (2026-06-13, `claude/explore_radiative_widths.py`).** Computed the downward-link width $\Gamma(n,d)\sim (v_dv_2)^2\,N(N-1)\,\Delta E^3$ ($\Delta E=[S(n,d)-S(n-2,d)]\,m_{\rm scale,d}$, $d=2$ radiated quantum, 3D phase space) for all 14 modes. **Result (i):** the absolutely stable charged members carry no width suppression — $u(3,4)\to(1,4)$ has $\Delta E=2.03$ MeV and $e(13,6)\to(11,6)$ has $\Delta E=0.29$ MeV, both with open widths were the target present, and the kernel matrix element does not vanish at the member sites; $e$'s smaller width tracks its smaller $\Delta E$, not a cancelled coupling. So the stability of $e,u$ is **target-absence** — the link has no physical final state because $(n-2,d)\notin\Sigma$ — not a dynamical protection of the member itself. This confirms the stability equivalence is exactly an equivalence (member stable $\iff$ its downward target absent from $\Sigma$), with no separate protective mechanism behind it. (The neutrino widths are tiny only because $m_{\rm scale,5}\sim10^{-13}$, the scale that makes them light — again not a protection.) **Result (ii):** the tower is downward-independent — no member's $(n-2,d)$ is itself a member, equivalently no two same-sector members differ by 2 in $n$ (gaps $\{3\}$ d=3, $\{17,52\}$ d=4, $\{5,7\}$ d=5, $\{22\}$ d=6, $\{5,14\}$ d=2). A member cannot radiatively decay to a member: a genuine self-consistency property of $\Sigma$. **Result (iii):** it is not selective — within each sector "no two 2 apart" admits many same-parity subsets (47 candidates in d=2, 36 in d=4, …). Net: the radiative channel does not by itself select the even-level set; the residue is a set-level self-consistency (Σ downward-independent, and every member's downward target absent) that the generation tower satisfies but that many other sets also satisfy — the pinning is still the tower combinatorics, consistent with every prior null. T0.5 unchanged. No document status edited.

### §23. Koide lepton-mass relation as a scale-free simplex identity (2026-06-06)

**Conjecture.** The Koide relation $Q = (m_e+m_\mu+m_\tau)/(\sqrt{m_e}+\sqrt{m_\mu}+\sqrt{m_\tau})^2 = 2/3$ (empirical to ~5 sig figs; listed "not derived" in `IDWT_paper.md`) follows from the IDWT lepton-sector structure.

**Setup.** Charged leptons: $e,\mu$ at $d=6$ ($n=13,35$); $\tau$ at $d=10$ ($n=23$, back-reaction $1+1/1680$). The lepton sectors share one mass scale, $m_{\rm scale,6}=m_{\rm scale,10}$ (Part 2 §9, Part 3 §0.8b). Each mass is that common scale times a pure simplex number, so the scale **cancels** in Koide's degree-0 ratio: $Q$ depends only on $S(13,6)=18564$, $S(35,6)=3{,}838{,}380$, and $S(23,10)(1+1/1680)=64{,}550{,}640$.

**Checked** (`claude/koide_check.py`):
- $Q_{\rm IDWT} = 0.666661$ vs $2/3 = 0.666667$ — deviation $-0.001\%$. Bare $S(23,10)$ (no back-reaction) gives $Q=0.66664$; the $+1/1680$ correction sharpens it.
- Non-triviality: with $e,\mu$ fixed, $Q$ swings strongly with the tau index — $n{=}21{:}\,0.591$, $22{:}\,0.629$, $\mathbf{23{:}\,0.6667}$, $24{:}\,0.702$, $25{:}\,0.736$. The index that the generation-tower co-fixed-point selection picks **independently** (n=23) is the one that lands on $2/3$.

**Result — two parts: a real positive reframing, and a PROVEN negative on the headline ("forced?") question.**

*Positive (structural, holds):* because the $d{=}6$ and $d{=}10$ leptons share one mass scale ($m_{\rm scale,6}=m_{\rm scale,10}$), $Q$ is exactly scale-free and reduces to a relation among three cross-sector simplex integers. At the independently selected indices $(13,35,23)$, $Q=0.6666611$ — within $8.3$ ppm of $2/3$, where neighbouring tau indices miss by whole percent ($n{=}22{:}\,0.6290$, $n{=}24{:}\,0.7024$). A genuine "structural near-coincidence."

*Negative (PROVEN, 2026-06-06): Koide $Q=2/3$ is NOT an algebraic identity of the simplex values.* Proof. Set $a=S(13,6),\,b=S(35,6),\,c=S(23,10)(1+\tfrac1{1680})$. Then
$$Q=\tfrac23 \iff (\sqrt a+\sqrt b+\sqrt c)^2=\tfrac32(a+b+c)\iff \sqrt{ab}+\sqrt{bc}+\sqrt{ca}=\tfrac{a+b+c}{4}.\quad(*)$$
The right side of $(*)$ is rational ($a,b\in\mathbb{Z}$; $c=451854481/7\in\mathbb{Q}$). But $a=2^2\!\cdot3\cdot7\cdot13\cdot17$ and $b=2^2\!\cdot3\cdot5\cdot7\cdot13\cdot19\cdot37$, so $ab=2^4\!\cdot3^2\!\cdot5\cdot7^2\!\cdot13^2\!\cdot17\cdot19\cdot37$ has squarefree part $5\cdot17\cdot19\cdot37=59755\neq1$; hence $\sqrt{ab}=1092\sqrt{59755}$ is irrational. A sum of square roots of positive rationals is rational only if each root is rational, and the three terms of $(*)$ are all positive (no cancellation). With $\sqrt{ab}$ irrational, the left side of $(*)$ is irrational, contradicting the rational right side. Therefore $(*)$ is impossible and $Q\neq2/3$ exactly. $\blacksquare$ Numerically $(*)$ misses by $426.7$ in $1.71\times10^7$ ($Q-2/3=-5.5\times10^{-6}$). Script: `claude/koide_check.py`.

**Cross-sector extension (2026-06-06, null).** Each sector triple is (one common scale)×(combinatorial factor), so a scale-free $Q$ exists for all four. Computed (`claude/koide_check.py` companion run): charged leptons $Q=0.6667$ (=2/3, −0.001%); up $(u,c,t)$ $Q=0.849$; down $(d,s,b)$ $Q=0.731$; neutrinos $(\nu_1,\nu_2,\nu_3)$ $Q=0.477$ (corr.) / $0.475$ (bare). Only the charged leptons hit a simple fraction. Best low-denominator rationals for the others are 17/20 (up, off 0.12%), 11/15 (down, off 0.35%), 9/19 (ν, off ~0.2–0.8%) — i.e. denominator $\sim$15–20 matched only to $\sim10^{-3}$, which is the generic spacing of denominator-20 fractions and therefore not structural. $Q$ simply tracks each sector's mass-hierarchy span ($Q\to1$ steep, $Q\to1/3$ degenerate). So Koide's $2/3$ is charged-lepton-specific — matching the empirical fact that Koide works for leptons and fails for quarks/neutrinos — and reveals no new cross-sector pattern. Do not re-chase clean-fraction $Q$ in the quark/neutrino sectors.

**Conclusion.** The "is Koide forced by the simplex structure?" question is settled: no. This is the expected and honest answer — the empirical Koide relation is itself only approximate ($\sim10^{-5}$), not an exact law; IDWT reproduces the lepton masses and therefore reproduces the empirical $Q\approx2/3$ to the same accuracy, without elevating it to a theorem (so it is not independent evidence beyond the mass fit). What stands as IDWT content is the scale-free reduction to three cross-sector simplex integers and the 8-ppm near-coincidence at the selected indices. Status: ⭐ for the non-identity proof (pure number theory); 🔵 for the structural near-coincidence. Do not re-attempt to prove $Q=2/3$ exact — it is provably not.

### §24. Null-model significance of the parameter-free dimensionless postdictions (2026-06-06)

**Question (self-directed).** A skeptic's first objection to any "masses from integers" theory is that the formula is flexible enough to fit anything. Quantify it: how unlikely is IDWT's agreement with the precisely-measured *dimensionless, parameter-free* quantities — treating every mode index as a *free* integer (maximally skeptical), with the sector scales only as derived from $m_e$ and $n_s$ (verified in `idwt.py`: $m_{\rm scale,d}$ come from the tower couplings, not refit per sector)?

**Method** (`claude/significance_audit.py`). For each quantity that is a ratio of simplex numbers fixed by one free index: $\varepsilon=|{\rm pred}-{\rm obs}|/{\rm obs}$ (floored at measurement error); grid spacing $g = S(n{+}1,d)/S(n,d)-1$ (the simplex grid is coarse at large $n$, so a tight hit is not generic even picking the nearest integer); luck $L=\min(1,2\varepsilon/g)$ — the chance the nearest grid point lands within $\varepsilon$ of the true value. Joint $=\prod L$ over independent indices/measurements.

**Quantities** (precisely measured, no correction-knob except the τ back-reaction):

| quantity | IDWT | obs | $\varepsilon$ | grid $g$ | $L$ |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| $m_\mu/m_e=S(35,6)/S(13,6)$ | 206.7647 | 206.76828 | $1.7\times10^{-5}$ | 0.171 | $2.0\times10^{-4}$ |
| $m_\tau/m_e=\tfrac{S(23,10)}{S(13,6)}(1{+}\tfrac1{1680})$ | 3477.19 | 3477.37 | $5.1\times10^{-5}$ | 0.435 | $2.3\times10^{-4}$ |
| $m_Z/m_W=S(81,2)/S(76,2)$ | 1.13500 | 1.13461 | $3.4\times10^{-4}$ | 0.0247 | $2.7\times10^{-2}$ |
| $m_H/m_W=S(95,2)/S(76,2)$ | 1.55844 | 1.55781 | $4.1\times10^{-4}$ | 0.0211 | $8.5\times10^{-2}$ |

(τ row: PDG 2024, $m_\tau = 1776.93\pm0.09$ MeV; its $\varepsilon$ is the measurement floor, fit residual $4.9\times10^{-5}$.) Joint $\approx1.1\times10^{-10}$ (≈1 in $9\times10^{9}$); even with a generous look-elsewhere ($\times100$ candidate quantities) $\sim10^{-8}$ (~$5\sigma$-scale). The two lepton ratios dominate because the $d=6,10$ grids are coarse — a sub-$10^{-4}$ hit on a 17–43% grid is the strong part.

**Result and the honest reading.** Even granting the skeptic *every index as a free integer*, the precisely-measured dimensionless ratios sit on the simplex grid far more tightly than a flexible fit would produce: the spectrum is **not** a generic "fit anything" structure. Caveats: (i) the $2\varepsilon/g$ luck model is order-of-magnitude, not a rigorous likelihood; (ii) conditional on the scales being derived (verified) not refit; (iii) selection is principled (precisely-measured + parameter-free) — looser predictions exist and are not cherry-pick-excluded ($g_A$ +4%, $f_\pi$ +2.1%, nucleon moments use fitted parameters). **Key structural point:** the *full* evidential weight hinges on whether the indices are forced from $n_s$ — the open T0.5 problem. If forced: ~2 inputs → these outputs, overwhelming. If free: still $\sim10^{-8}$ from grid tightness alone. Either way T0.5 is the load-bearing question; closing it converts an already-significant postdiction into a near-parameter-free one. Status: 🔵 (statistical, order-of-magnitude). Written up in Part 5 §2a with `idwt.py` STEP 38; superseded as the quantitative statement by the follow-up below (Part 5 §2b, STEP 39).

**Follow-up (2026-06-09): exact joint p-value + random-theory Monte Carlo** (`claude/significance_mc.py`; `idwt.py` STEP 39; Part 5 §2b). The heuristic $\prod L$ replaced by two proper null models.

*Null A — random target position.* H0: each measured value sits at a uniformly random position in its local inter-rung cell, so the normalized distance to the nearest rung is $p\sim U(0,1)$; with measurement floor $f=\min(1,2\sigma/g)$ the per-quantity luck is $L=\max(p,f)$; statistic $X=-\sum\ln L_i$; joint $p=P(X\ge X_{\rm obs})$ computed exactly (convolution of the per-quantity densities, MC-validated at every resolvable tail depth) and by Fisher's $\chi^2_{2k}$ closed form (conservative under floors). Quantity set fixed by a pre-stated rule — dimensionless, parameter-free, measurement resolves the grid ($\sigma<g/2$): the four §24 ratios plus $\sin\theta_C$, $m_s/m_d$, $m_t/m_c$, $\Delta m^2_{31}/\Delta m^2_{21}$ (8 quantities; conservative grid convention $\min$ over $n\to n\pm1$; one free index per quantity, the other anchored — the "both free" objection is Null B's job). The PMNS angles and $m_c/m_u$ fail the resolution rule (grid finer than current errors — uninformative either way); as consistency checks they pull $+0.30\sigma$, $+0.13\sigma$, $+0.19\sigma$, $-0.00\sigma$. Inputs: PDG 2024 + FLAG 2024 ($m_s/m_d = 19.81(13)$ — IDWT's 20 is $+1.5\sigma$, the largest pull in the set, scored as found). **Result: $X_{\rm obs}=31.56$, joint $p = 8.9\times10^{-11}$ (6.4σ) exact; $1.5\times10^{-7}$ (5.1σ) Fisher-conservative; $\times100$ look-elsewhere $\to 8.9\times10^{-9}$ (5.6σ); core-4 subset $3.8\times10^{-7}$ (4.9σ).**

*Null B — random theories.* Every mode index drawn independently and uniformly from its window (sector mass ≤ 1 TeV at the seed-chain scales; d=5 ≤ 1 eV: windows d=2:269, d=3:107, d=4:111, d=5:41, d=6:169, d=10:47); all 12 quantities recomputed per draw ($g_{55}$ fixed by seeds); scored by $T=\sum\ln\varepsilon_{{\rm eff},i}$. **Result: 0 of $8.4\times10^6$ draws (incl. halved/doubled-window runs) matched as well as IDWT $\Rightarrow p_B < 5\times10^{-7}$ (95% CL) at the stated windows; best random theory short by 36 ln-units.** Per-quantity chance match rates: $m_\mu/m_e$ $3\times10^{-5}$, $m_\tau/m_e$ 0 in all draws, $m_Z/m_W$ $2\times10^{-4}$, $m_H/m_W$ $4\times10^{-4}$, others $10^{-3}$–$10^{-2}$, PMNS $10^{-2}$–$0.3$. Status: 🔵 (statistical, now a proper likelihood under the stated nulls). The conclusion of the original audit stands with rigorous arithmetic; the load-bearing open question remains T0.5.

### §25. Tower edges as condensate matrix elements; the subtractive-edge sign (F5/F16, 2026-06-09)

Source: Fable-5 findings F5/F16/F9; computation `claude/verify_f5f16_joint.py`, `files/idwt.py` STEP 41. Oscillator proxy (T1: level $n\leftrightarrow$ Hermite degree $k=n-1$); the P6 condensate-linearized kernel supplies the degree-1 vertex (a single $\xi$ insertion).

**Additive edges = one degree-1 condensate insertion at top-of-band (⭐).** Each additive tower edge $n_c=n_a+n_b$ — $n_e=n_{\nu_1}+n_u$, $n_\mu=n_{\nu_2}+n_c$, $n_\tau=n_{\nu_3}+n_d$ — is the matrix element $\langle H_{n_c-1}\,|\,x\,|\,H_{n_a-1}H_{n_b-1}\rangle$ taken at its top-of-band component. The top coefficient is the leading-coefficient ratio $2^{k_a+k_b}/2^{k_a+k_b+1}=\tfrac12$ — positive, nonzero, with no leakage above (verified exactly per edge). So the single degree-1 raising insertion lands precisely at $n_c=n_a+n_b$, giving the additive DAG edges a kernel-matrix-element reading. (This corrects the F5-strengthened note's transcription "$\Leftrightarrow n_c=n_a+n_b-1$"; the bookkeeping $(n_c-1)=(n_a-1)+(n_b-1)+1$ gives $n_c=n_a+n_b$.)

**The unique subtractive edge carries the inclusion-exclusion minus (T8 gap (ii)).** $n_{\nu_3}=n_{\nu_1}+n_{\nu_2}-n_u$ is the one edge with a net degree change $-(n_u-1)=-2$ relative to the product — a lowering, opposite to the additive raising. The $-n_u$ is inclusion-exclusion (Part 2 §9c: $n_{\nu_1}=S(n_u,3)$ and $n_{\nu_2}=S(n_u,4)$ share the seed $n_u$, counted once too many), i.e. the cumulant/connected-correlator minus sign $\langle AB\rangle_c=\langle AB\rangle-\langle A\rangle\langle B\rangle$. The electron ($n_e=13$, itself seed-built) overlaps the subtracted shared-seed leg, so the $W[e,3]$ coupling inherits the minus: $\partial U_{e3}/\partial\theta_{13}|_{0^+}<0$ relative to the positive additive edges. This is the convention-independent **relative** sign that Part 10 §2 asserts; the overall branch ($\delta\to\pi$) is the PDG-convention bracket already stated in Part 10 §4. Identifies the mechanism for T8 gap (ii); gaps (i) and (iii) are untouched, so T8 stays 🔶.

**Photon protection consistency (F9).** The condensate vertex $2(\xi_d\!\cdot\!\langle\xi_{d'}\rangle)(\xi_d\!\cdot\!\delta\xi_{d'})$ is degree 1 (odd) only in the fluctuation leg $\delta\xi_{d'}$ and degree 2 (even) in the spectator leg $\xi_d$; the photon's own $d=2$ leg is always the even spectator, so $m_\gamma=0$ (Part 3 §16.2) survives the degree-1 vertices that drive the tower edges.

Placement: the explicit gap-(ii) mechanism is recorded in Part 10 §2 (with the matching wording in the §4 status note), here, and in `idwt.py` STEP 41. T8 remains 🔶 — gaps (i) and (iii) are untouched, and the overall branch stays the §4 convention bracket.

**Addendum — full production census in segment terms; the insertion dichotomy (❓, 2026-06-10, `claude/explore_prism_latesplit.py` Test B; Fedge late-split discussion).** Writing every production of the tower DAG as $n_c = \sum(\text{operands}) - \text{overlap}$ (rungs of a common ladder; sharing $k$ rungs subtracts $k$), all 13 productions are consistent and the overlap takes only four values:

| overlap | productions | reading |
|---|---|---|
| 0 | additive edges e, μ, τ, H-additive | one degree-1 condensate insertion above level addition (the ⭐ result above; the "+1 joint rung") |
| 1 | every g-rule join: up-from-strange, W, Z, H | exact level addition — insertion-free; shares one rung |
| n_u = 3 | ν₃ | shared-base inclusion-exclusion (documented above) |
| n_charm−1 = 19 | top ($S(n_e,2) - (n_{\rm charm}-1)$) | the §12 factor 19, appearing here as an overlap |

The new content beyond the ⭐ result above is the dichotomy: the fermion-type edges all carry exactly one condensate insertion (overlap 0), while every g-rule join — which produces the three heavy bosons and the up — is insertion-free pure level addition (overlap 1). Hockey-stick evaluations (ν₁, ν₂, charm) are themselves segment concatenations of the lower Pascal column, which is just the identity restated. Status ❓: a consistent organizing reading with two genuinely patterned cells (the insertion dichotomy; the factor-19 overlap), no mechanism for why boson joins are insertion-free. Companion Test A (sector assignment from blind-lattice invariants) is the §15 null of the same date.

**The d=2 even-insertion selection rule — mechanism for the insertion dichotomy (🔶, 2026-06-10, `claude/explore_insertion_dichotomy.py`).** The dichotomy above reduces to documented structure. The degree-1 condensate vertex exists only where a sector condensate $\langle\xi_{d'}\rangle\neq0$ supplies the linearization (Part 1 P6, STEP 41); and the all-orders photon-mass theorem states that the condensate-linearized vertices "remain even (degree 2) in the photon's own d=2 variable" (Part 3 §16.2) — there is no odd vertex in the d=2 variable, the same fact that protects $m_\gamma = 0$ in condensate backgrounds. Proposed selection rule: **a tower production landing on a d=2 mode carries an even number of condensate insertions in its own variable; matter-sector targets are unconstrained.** Checked in the T1 Hermite proxy (top-of-band landing exact in all cases):

- W, Z, H g-joins: 0 insertions (even ✓), landing at $n_f + d - 1$ with the $-1$ as the shared vacuum unit (✅, Part 3 §11);
- the Higgs additive closure $n_H = n_u + n_{\rm charm} + n_{\rm top}$ (🔶, Part 2 §6): exactly 2 insertions (even ✓) — the rule renders the two documented Higgs routes mutually consistent rather than competing;
- fermion edges e, μ, τ: exactly 1 insertion (odd — available only off d=2);
- counterfactual odd-insertion boson indices 77, 82, 96 are unoccupied; insertion-free fermion counterfactuals 12, 34 unoccupied (22 is occupied but as (22,5)=ν₃, a different sector).

One structural fact — no d=2 condensate — thus yields both $m_\gamma = 0$ and the boson $-1$: the insertion dichotomy is the photon-protection mechanism seen from the production side. Honest limits: (i) the bridge from single-variable proxy insertion count to multi-leg vertex L-parity in the d=2 variable is stated, not derived — that is the 🔶 gap; (ii) the rule does not explain why matter edges use exactly one insertion (odd is allowed, not forced); (iii) it does not single out routes — even-insertion alternative boson routes exist arithmetically (e.g. top+up+down = 76; the §15 route-multiplicity null applies), so the rule constrains channel parity, not route choice.

Placed (2026-06-10, Fedge-approved): `idwt.py` STEP 55; Part 3 §11 (mechanism paragraph after the −1 derivation); Part 3 §16.2 (production-side corollary); Part 2 §6 (insertion-parity note before the n_u status paragraph). Carries 🔶 in all locations with limits (i)–(iii) summarised in Part 3 §11.

**Addendum — ray-classification audit of the dimensionless postdictions (consistent, 2026-06-10, `claude/audit_ray_classification.py`; late-prism move (a), `claude/late_prism_notes.md` item 4).** Test of the late-prism prediction that a dimensionless quantity built within one ray (one sector scale, the degenerate $d=6/d=10$ pair, or a pure angle) is prism-immune — fixed at the integer layer, so its only residual is a pure-number (Level-2) correction plus measurement floor — while a quantity crossing rays carries derived scale ratios (Level-1 residuals). Classified the STEP 39 resolving set (8 quantities plus the $m_c/m_u$ consistency check) and recomputed residuals against PDG 2024. Findings: (i) every correction applied to an intra-ray quantity is a pure number with no scale ratio — GTC $\varepsilon=1/(280\sqrt7)$, back-reaction $1/1680$, $\nu_3$ shift $1/35$, Cabibbo curvature $1/240$ — the central auditable demand passes with no exceptions; (ii) no intra-ray quantity carries a large unexplained residual: $m_s/m_d$, $m_t/m_c$, $m_c/m_u$ and $\Delta m^2_{31}/\Delta m^2_{21}$ sit within their measurement floors, and the scale-free $m_\mu/m_e=S(35,6)/S(13,6)$ sits at $1.7\times10^{-5}$ (its pure-simplex precision floor; it exceeds the $2\times10^{-9}$ mass-ratio measurement floor but carries no correction term and no scale dependence). Honest limit: the prediction's magnitude-separation form (intra-ray residual $<$ cross-ray) is only weakly confirmed — the worst intra-ray residual is $\Delta m^2_{31}/\Delta m^2_{21}$ at $3.8\times10^{-2}$, larger than any cross-ray residual, but it is measurement-floor-limited (floor $2.6\times10^{-2}$), not unexplained. The discriminating content that passes is the correction-*type* prediction (pure number vs scale ratio), not the residual-magnitude ordering. Supports late-prism item 4; cross-checks the Part 2 §12 two-layer split without requiring an edit to it.

**Addendum — mixing angles are scale-free lattice quantities (consistent, 2026-06-10, `claude/audit_mixing_angles.py`; late-prism move (b), `claude/late_prism_notes.md` item 5).** Test of the prediction that the lattice/mass-basis misalignment is fixed before scales exist, so no mixing angle may carry a mass-scale ratio. Checks: (i) **scale-invariance** — rescaling every $m_{\text{scale},d}$ by an arbitrary $\kappa$ leaves all three PMNS angles unchanged ($\max|\Delta| = 0$); the CKM forms contain no scale token at all. (ii) **Scale-cancellation mechanism (the structural finding):** the PMNS angles, recomputed from the masses $m_{\text{scale},d}S(n,d)$ instead of the bare counts $S(n,d)$, give identical values — because every mode-pair a PMNS angle compares shares one scale. $\sin^2\theta_{12}$ compares $\nu_1,\nu_2$ (both $d=5$, intra-ray); $\sin^2\theta_{23}$ and $\sin^2\theta_{13}$ compare $n_\mu$ ($d=6$) with $n_\tau$ ($d=10$) — the degenerate pair $m_{\text{scale},6}=m_{\text{scale},10}$. The angles are scale-free not by a formula choice but because they only ever compare scale-sharing modes; a cross-ray pair would leave a surviving scale ratio and the angle would not be prism-immune. This is the same degeneracy that makes Koide (§23) and the audit-(a) $m_\tau/m_e$ entry prism-immune, here seen in the mixing sector. (iii) **Residuals** vs PDG 2024 all sit within measurement floor: CKM $\sin\theta_C$, $|V_{cb}|$, $A$ at $0.1$–$0.4\%$; PMNS $\sin^2\theta_{23,12,13}$ at $0.5$–$1.1\%$; $|V_{ub}|=|V_{td}|=0$ at tree level (the open non-zero route is the Hopf Chern–Simons geometric phase, Part 5 §3f — not a mass scale). (iv) corrections/couplings are pure numbers: Cabibbo $1+1/240=1+\chi(\mathbb{CP}^1)/(24\,S(n_s,3))$; $g_{55}=96/g_{22}=96/722.5$ rational ($\sqrt7$ cancels); $|V_{cb}|$ and $A$ bare simplex ratios with no correction. Honest form distinction: the CKM angles fit the strong "lattice number $\times$ small pure correction" form item 5 states literally; the PMNS angles fit only the weaker scale-free form — a rational-coupling-weighted ($g_{55}$) average of two lattice ratios, not a single lattice number with a perturbative correction. Both pass the falsifiable scale-content claim. Supports late-prism item 5; no document edit warranted — the mixing-angle derivations (Part 3 §12, Part 5 §3g–3i) already use only counts and couplings.

**Addendum — single-input structure, the algebraic split tower, and the k₀=16 "triple coincidence" audited to a double (2026-06-10, `claude/explore_prism_singleinput.py`; Fedge question: does the spectrum exist "all ×1" then split, or form as observed?).** Four results bearing on the late-prism hypothesis. (i) **One dimensional input.** Every sector scale satisfies $m_{\text{scale},d}=m_e\,c_d$ with $c_d$ a pure seed-built number ($m_{\text{scale},5}$ included, via the cross-sector fixed point $m_{\text{scale},5}m_{\text{scale},4}^2=(n_u/n_s)m_{\text{scale},6}^3$); the full 15-mass spectrum is $m_e\times[c_d\,S(n,d)]$ — one anchor plus the integer seed $n_s=4$. (Gravity adds a second input $\Lambda/G_\infty$, Part 4 §3.12.4; the mass spectrum does not.) (ii) **Algebraic split tower (⭐ identity).** The split factors $c_d=m_{\text{scale},d}/m_e$ form a clean minimal-polynomial-degree tower over $\mathbb{Q}$: $c_6=c_{10}=1/S(n_e,6)$ rational (deg 1); $c_2=\sqrt{g_{22}/g_{66}}$ and $c_5\propto\sqrt7$ quadratic (deg 2); $c_3=\sqrt{g_{33}/g_{66}}$ and $c_4$ quartic (deg 4, a $\sqrt{}$ of a $\mathbb{Q}(\sqrt7)$ number). The degree is set by how $\sqrt7=\sqrt{n_s+n_u}$ threads each scale formula (odd inner power of $\sqrt7\to$ quartic). The comb teeth $S(n,d)$ are integers, so the integer lattice and the scale overlay are genuinely distinct algebraic objects — the split carries integers to irrationals, not a trivial refactor — while both stay fixed by the one seed. (iii) **The k₀=16 "triple coincidence" is a double in cross-sector reach.** The three expressions $16=n_s^2=n_e+n_u=n_{\rm charm}-n_s$ all hold at $n_s=4$ (paper §5.3), but $n_s^2$ is the *definition* of $k_0$, and $n_{\rm charm}-n_s=n_s^2$ reduces to the $d=3$ simplex identity $S(n_s,3)=n_s(n_s+1)$ ($\Leftrightarrow(n_s+2)/6=1\Leftrightarrow n_s=4$) — internal to the quark sectors. The only equality reaching the $d=6$ lepton sector is $n_e+n_u=n_s^2$. Both $B=n_e+n_u$ and $C=n_{\rm charm}-n_s$ are $n_s=4$-specific (each singles out $n_s=4$ uniquely for $n_s<500$; their intersection $\{4\}$ re-derives the b-quark-beat uniqueness), but the genuinely cross-sector content is a double (quark-side $k_0\leftrightarrow$ lepton-side $n_e+n_u$), not a triple. The "triple coincidence" wording is literally correct as three coincident expressions; "double in cross-sector reach" measures a different quantity (how many of the three bridge two sectors), so the two statements do not conflict. RESOLVED (2026-06-10, Fedge): the late-prism ordering settles it in favour of "triple." Cross-sector reach is a post-prism notion — the index arithmetic lives in one sector-blind integer lattice and the sectors attach downstream — so at the layer where the coincidence lives there is no "quark-internal vs cross-sector" distinction to demote $C$ with; all three are integer-lattice characterizations on equal footing. Independent of prism timing, the precise structure is: $A$ is the definition; $B$ and $C$ are two *independent* non-trivial coincidences (their $n_s$-solution sets intersect only at $\{4\}$, so neither is redundant — $C$ is not "near-tautological"), each forcing the seed. The documents keep "triple coincidence," now affirmatively justified; Part 2 §8 gained one sentence stating the definition/two-coincidence split and the sole cross-sector index pair. (iv) **Discriminator (the answer to the question).** The dependency is asymmetric: $S(n,d)$ and the seed $n_s=4$ are pure combinatorics with no scale input ($n_s=4$ is selected by an integer eigenvalue condition, the $4/7$ resonance), while the scales $c_d$ are functions of the integers and nothing flows back. So the integer layer is **logically/generatively prior** to the scales — "integers first" follows from the dependency structure alone (⭐). The earlier "underdetermined / same object" reading conflated two questions: *observational* distinguishability of a temporal "before" (which would need a condensation equation of motion — not derived) is genuinely open, but the *generative-order* question is settled by the asymmetry. What remains ❓ is therefore only the dynamical dressing of the prism (a massless phase existing in cosmic time, a condensation event switching scales on), which "integers prior" does not depend on. Net: the late-prism's core ordering claim — the integers generate the scales — is established; the structural two-layer factorization (sector-blind integer comb × seed-locked irrational scales) is exact; only the thermal/temporal phase story stays open (`late_prism_notes.md` move (d)). Wording item RESOLVED (2026-06-10, Fedge): "triple coincidence" kept across all locations (Part 2 §8, Part 5 §5, Part 6) — affirmatively justified by the late-prism sector-blind ordering, not merely tolerated. See the resolution under (iii) above.

### §26. Single-electron double slit — exact 6D separation, the marginal pattern, and the one-slit excitation (2026-06-10)

Question (Fedge): a d=6 electron passes through one slit — what carries the slit separation $D$ into its landing statistics, given the sector confinement? Resolved; script `claude/double_slit_6d.py` (all four checks pass).

1. **Where the asymmetry is (the keystone).** No three of the electron's six dimensions are special (Part 1 sector reality); the split in this experiment belongs to the apparatus. Panel, source, and screen are baryonic, hence d=3 structures (colour confinement, Part 1 §2.4): each has structure in its three dimensions and is uniform through the electron's other three. The sector well is the electron's own self-binding (width $L_6$, Part 4 §3.9) and marks out no direction; what it binds is the excitation, and it does not narrow the configuration the excitation rides. In the separated problem the well term enters on the coordinates the apparatus has no structure in — Part 8 §14.2 writes $V_6(|\xi_{4,5,6}|)$ for hydrogen, a split anchored there by the d=3 nucleus and here by the d=3 panel, not by the observer. "The electron is confined" (the excitation is compact) and "the configuration spans both slits" are statements about two different objects — both true. [Correction of record: this entry first framed the well as acting on "the hidden three" coordinates per se; Fedge flagged the 3+3 split as an observational artifact wrongly placed in the dynamics, and the article and this entry were rewritten apparatus-anchored, 2026-06-10.]
2. **Separation ✅.** The slit panel is a potential built from 3D sources → by the projection theorem (Part 3 §0.8a) uniform in $\xi_{4,5,6}$ → the 6D problem separates exactly (Lemma 1 structure): $\Psi=\psi(\mathbf{r},t)\,\chi(\xi)$ with the sector factor a spectator (marginal deviation between distinct $\chi$: $8\times10^{-16}$).
