Interim conclusion (later superseded by the n=1 result below): the seesaw form does not close; the *source-side* picture is confirmed: gravity couples to $|\partial\Psi|^2$ (frequency $\to$ mass via the derivative/highpass), universally to mass because the filter corner lies outside the particle band (equivalence principle).

*Follow-up — the n=1 relation (2026-06-04, `claude/explore_gravity_n1_solve.py`): strongest lead, 🔵.* The corner is the **n=1 mode** $m(1,5)=m_{{\rm scale},5}$ (S(1,d)=1, so $m(1,5)$ is the single lowest-frequency mode in the theory — exactly "way below the neutrinos"). The gravitational scale fits

$$M_{\rm Pl} = \frac{m_e^3}{C'\,m_{{\rm scale},5}^2}.$$

**The power law is uniquely selected, not fitted:** among integer $M_{\rm Pl}=C\,m_e^{a}\,m_{{\rm scale},5}^{b}$ with $a+b=1$ (mass dimension), only $(a,b)=(3,-2)$ gives a coefficient of order $1$–$100$ ($C'=19.80$); every other integer power gives $C$ of order $10^{\pm(10\text{–}34)}$. The demanded $C'=19.800$ matches **$2\pi^2=\mathrm{Vol}(S^3)$** — the volume of the $d=3$ observer sector — to **+0.31%** (next: $S(n_s,3)=20$ at $-1.0\%$). So

$$M_{\rm Pl}\approx \frac{m_e^3}{\mathrm{Vol}(S^3)\,m_{{\rm scale},5}^2},$$

expressing the Planck scale in $m_e+N_c+\mathrm{Vol}(S^3)$ — which *would* mean no second input, **if it had a derivation.** It does not. **Derivation attempted (2026-06-04) and the physical motivation fails:** (i) substituting the exact definitions, $M_{\rm Pl}\propto m_{{\rm scale},4}^4/m_{{\rm scale},6}^3$ — a combination with no physical meaning, i.e. the clean form is algebraic accident, not mechanism; (ii) $\mathrm{Vol}(S^3)=2\pi^2$ is reverse-engineered from the number — no integral in the actual gravity computation produces it (the real spectral action, §3.12.4, gives prefactor $\approx 8.5$ and $\Lambda^{51/10}$, not $1/2\pi^2$); (iii) "$m_{{\rm scale},5}$ because it is the n=1 corner" fixes the corner but not the squared-reciprocal-times-sphere-volume formula; (iv) the only physical-looking thread, $\alpha_G\propto(m_{{\rm scale},5}/m_e)^4$ from the quartic T2 kernel, conflates the matter self-interaction with gravity-as-geometry — different objects. **Status: ❓ numerical near-coincidence (0.31%), no physical derivation; not promoted.** The one solid sub-fact is the dimensional selection of the $(a,b)=(3,-2)$ power law. *Self-binding mechanism tested and rejected (2026-06-04, `claude/` quick calc):* the proposal that the confining well $V_d$ **is** the gravitational well ("mass bends space, mass seeks low spots") fails by 34–45 orders — $\alpha_G=G_N m_e^2=1.75\times10^{-45}$, so gravity is 45 orders weaker than the confinement that sets the masses ($V_d\neq$ gravity), and the self-binding balance (with the genuine 4D Gauss factor $2\pi^2=\mathrm{Vol}(S^3)$) predicts $M_{\rm Pl}=\frac{\pi}{2}m_{{\rm scale},5}\sim10^{-12}$ MeV vs measured $10^{22}$ — wrong by $10^{34}$ and the wrong structure ($\propto m_{{\rm scale},5}$, not $m_e^3/m_{{\rm scale},5}^2$). The $2\pi^2$ has a real home (4D gravity Gauss constant) but cannot rescue a 34-order magnitude miss. **Standing conclusion (all routes — seesaw, n=1, self-binding): $M_{\rm Pl}$ is a second dimensional input** (Part 4 §3.12.4); only the *source-side* gravity picture ($|\partial\Psi|^2\to$ mass, EP from corner outside band) is established.

**Bottom-quark beat: arithmetic mean instead of geometric**
Conjecture: the b-quark beat at k₀=16 should use the arithmetic mean ½(S(16,3)+S(17,3)) of the two adjacent mode counts rather than the geometric mean √(S(16,3)·S(17,3)), so m_b would carry the same +0.68% offset as the other d=3 quarks (down, strange).
Checked (2026-06-04):
- Arithmetic mean → m_b = 4196 MeV (+0.39% vs PDG 4180), not the +0.68% sector offset. No Pythagorean mean of {816,969} reproduces +0.68%: geometric +0.02%, arithmetic +0.39%, RMS +0.76%; the uniform offset needs a beat count of 895.1, between the arithmetic 892.5 and RMS 895.8.
- The arithmetic mean degrades the downstream heavy-meson family: B±/B⁰/B_s/Υ(1S) move from a tight −0.11…−0.19% (geometric m_b feeding E_bind=√(m_b·Λ_QCD)) to a scattered +0.14…+0.22%.
Result: rejected. The geometric mean is retained as the energy scale of the quartic density–density beat coupling |Ψ₁₆|²|Ψ₁₇|² (cross-term ∝ E₁₆E₁₇, dimension energy², so the beat sits at its square root). The earlier "equal-weight linear amplitude" justification was a non-sequitur — equal weight in a Hermitian 2-level coupling gives the arithmetic mean — and Part 2 §8 / Part 7 now state the quartic argument. Status 🔶: the dimensional argument is heuristic; a closed derivation from the quartic kernel eigenvalue problem is open.

**Dark sector (velinos / umbrons / liminons)**
Conjecture: mode indices n∈Σ that pass Stage-2 stability are stable in *any* sector d, producing extra stable particles in unused sectors — a dark sector that passes Stage-2 but fails Stage-1 visibility.
Checked: Stage-2 selects the *pair* (n,d), not n alone. Σ_pairs (15 elements) is the complete Stage-2 solution set; adding any non-Σ_pairs pair breaks closure, and sector-universal stability is not derivable from P8.
Result: retracted 2026-05-29 (commit d1f2e5f; Part 1 P8 note + summary table, Part 6, Part 7 §1.3/§2.6). No dark sector exists under the current construction. One would require either extending the coupling construction to d=7,8,9 or a derived sector-universal stability argument from the EOM — neither done. Flag any reappearance of velinos/umbrons/liminons as retracted.

**§18 adjacent-sector ratio as a selection constraint on the mode set**
Conjecture: the §18 ratio S(n,d)/S(n,d+1) = (d+1)/(n+d), evaluated on the physical {n,d}, surfaces an interlocking pattern or a constraint on which modes are selected.
Checked (2026-06-04, `claude/explore_s18_ladder.py`): §18 is a ⭐ identity valid for all (n,d), so it is structurally incapable of distinguishing the co-fixed-point set from any other pairs. Selection test in d=3: the step (n+d)/(d+1) runs 1, 5/4, 3/2, 7/4, 2 for n=1..5 — selected (n=1,4) and unselected (n=2,3,5) interleave with no distinguishing value. Only two isolated hits across the 15 particles (down: n+d=4=n_s; tau: step (n+d)/(d+1)=3=n_u), forming no pattern. The tau hit was independently refound 2026-06-10 in the equivalent forms n_τ + d_τ = N_c(d_τ+1) and n_τ = (N_c−1)d_τ + N_c (N_c = n_u = 3 at n_s=4, so the two readings are indistinguishable); it is unique over the 15 but fails at n_s = 3, 5, 6 under either reading (`claude/verify_gifts_fusion_stepping.py`) — still an isolated ❓ hit, not a terminal-sector selection rule. Do not re-run as a "Rule B bridge" without a mechanism that generalises in n_s.
Result: no selection constraint from §18, as expected for a universal identity. The positive content — §18 as the multiplicative across-sector recursion dual to the additive hockey-stick — is recorded at §18.

**Fixed-point lens: is Σ_pairs the fixed point of a NATURAL operation functor?**
Conjecture: the co-fixed-point property F(Σ)=Σ upgrades to ✅ if Σ is the least fixed point (forward closure from the seeds) of a natural operation functor F(X)=X∪ops(X), with the off-Σ lattice points being transients (no finite derivation).
Checked (2026-06-05, `claude/explore_fixedpoint_lens.py`, `explore_fixedpoint_halt.py`, `explore_fixedpoint_parity_gate.py`):
- The forward closure under the 13 **hand-listed named productions** (Part 2 §6 DAG, encoded as deterministic value-level rules) reproduces Σ_pairs exactly — 15/15, zero false positives, and halts. But this only re-encodes the DAG: each production hard-codes which (n,d) it emits.
- When the same operations are lifted to **generic schemas** (simplex S(n,k) into every sector, g-rule into d=2, pairwise additive into every sector) and applied to all present pairs, the closure blows up: 1191 false positives are admitted while collecting the 15 (cf. the §15 operational-closure and value-closure dead ends, ~186 extras at value level). The selection is therefore a **specific directed derivation path** (the acyclic DAG), not the fixed point of a natural functor.
- Using the kernel **l-parity reachability rule as the production gate** (a production fires only if the hop is l=0→l=0 allowed: intra-sector requires odd n, cross-sector requires a protected simplex image of a reached odd index) does NOT tame the blow-up — gated closures still admit 130–640 false positives (8–11/15 hits). l-parity is a genuine necessary obstruction but is far from sufficient: it removes odd-level (n even) modes, yet the surviving odd-n modes still vastly outnumber the 15.
Result: the dynamical-systems framing does not by itself produce a ✅ selector. F(Σ)=Σ holds only for the hand-listed productions (a closure property, not a derivation). The honest content the lens does establish: (i) Σ_pairs is the image of a **unique terminating derivation** — the tower DAG is finite, acyclic, has unique source nodes {(1,3),(3,4)}, trivial automorphism group, and **halts intrinsically** because every production consumes already-derived indices and no production regenerates the seeds (verified §13b); (ii) the 6 parity-forbidden (even-n) Σ modes — strange(4,3), nu1(10,5), charm(20,4), nu3(22,5), top(72,4), W(76,2) — are admitted only through cross-sector seed-image protection, exactly as the l-parity argument predicts. The missing ✅ ingredient is unchanged: a physical principle that selects WHICH production fires, replacing the hand-list. The l=0/l=2 kernel gate supplies necessity (the inverse-direction exclusion of odd-level modes is ⭐), not sufficiency.

**Tower-selection workflow run #1 — adversarially-verified candidates (2026-06-05, forward + inverse)**
Conjecture: a forward selector or an inverse/complement characterization, run against the full lattice (d∈D, n∈[0,200]) and adversarially verified, upgrades T0.5 from 🔶. Six mathematical lenses; four candidates reached numerical execution. Scripts: `claude/verify_sel_*.py`; running record `claude/tower_selection_search_log.md`.
Checked:
- `fp-terminating-derivation` (forward; named DAG + intrinsic-halt package): the named 15-operation DAG selects exactly NS (FP=0, FN=0) and is acyclic with strict Lyapunov depth-grading (max depth 6) and sources = seeds {(1,3),(3,4)} (composite (4,3) at depth 1). Generic-schema lift of the same operations → 1191 false positives. Re-confirms the §15 fixed-point-lens result: a specific terminating derivation, not a forced one.
- `fp-parity-complement` (inverse): the parity cut alone (n odd or 0) gives 9/15, misses the 6 even-n NS modes, 597 FP. Necessary, not sufficient.
- `fp-crosssector-reachability-gate` (inverse; dephasing/resonance coupling-to-seed R): **necessary-not-sufficient**, best FP=5 FN=12. The Σ odd-level d=3 modes have R = 0 exactly (parity), but non-Σ R is **continuous down to 1.5×10⁻⁹** — no untuned threshold separates physical from excluded.
- `spectral-graded-1` (l∈{0,2} overlap window): 15/15 hits but ~1190 FP; the overlap gate passes almost everything.
Result: null for a new clean selector — but it sharpens the gap to a single hinge. The odd-level exclusion is an **exact zero** (⭐ parity); the even-level (n odd) exclusion is, on every test, only a **small-but-nonzero quantity** — there is no exact structural cut, only a continuum, so no threshold upgrades it without tuning. The status of T0.5 therefore turns on one question, recorded for the next round: **is the even-level physical/excluded separation provably exact (a hidden zero / conserved quantity), or provably only quantitative?** If only quantitative, 🔵 is the ceiling and that bound should itself be proved. The forward "why this DAG" question reduces to the same hinge (the DAG's even-level productions are the unprotected ones).

**T0.5 hinge resolved: the even-level exclusion is provably ONLY quantitative — 🔵 is the proven ceiling (2026-06-05, run #2)**
Conjecture: the even-level (n odd, l-parity-reachable) physical-vs-excluded separation is either provably EXACT (a hidden zero / conserved quantity / second selection rule analogous to l-parity, which would upgrade T0.5 toward ✅) or provably ONLY quantitative (no structural cut, bounding the even-level exclusion at 🔵).
Checked (three independent legs):
- *No integer/Diophantine cut.* No single natural integer condition on n isolates the 8 even-level NS modes among even-level lattice points (n ≤ 200, d ∈ D). The additive tower closure (n = sum of two tower indices) hits all 8 but admits 35+ excluded modes — necessary, not sufficient. Script: `claude/run2_crosssector_levelmatch_exact.py`.
- *No self-energy fixed point ("return to bare level").* The 2nd-order self-energy shift δE(n)/E₀ of the even-level d=3 modes is a smooth, monotonically decreasing function of n with no zero; the seed itself (down, n=1) has the largest relative shift, not a return-to-bare. So "a mode is stable iff its perturbed energy returns to its bare level" is a minimum, never an exact zero, and selects nothing structural. Script: `claude/run2_selfenergy_return_fixedpoint.py`.
- *Analytic ceiling-proof — the seed-coupling has no node.* The l=0 kernel overlap coupling an even-level d=3 mode (radial quantum number n_r=(n−1)/2, angular l=0) to the l=0 vacuum has the exact closed form (with u the scaled radial variable, s the effective Gaussian weight)
$$J_{n_r}(s)=\int_0^\infty L_{n_r}^{(1/2)}(u)\,e^{-su}\,u^{1/2}\,du=\frac{\Gamma(n_r+3/2)}{n_r!}\cdot\frac{(s-1)^{n_r}}{s^{\,n_r+3/2}},\qquad \Gamma(n_r+\tfrac32)=\frac{\sqrt{\pi}\,(2n_r+1)!!}{2^{\,n_r+1}}.$$
Its only zero in s is at s=1 (the Laguerre orthogonality point), independent of the positive $n_r$-prefactor. The IDWT kernel structurally fixes s=3/2 (the vacuum density e^{−u} multiplied by the mode envelope e^{−u/2}), where the $n_r$-dependent factor $((s-1)/s)^{n_r}=(1/3)^{n_r}>0$ for every n_r. Every even-level mode couples to the seed; the coupling never vanishes; it decays geometrically (successive ratio → 1/3). Verified against direct quadrature in `files/idwt.py` STEP 34 (closed form matches the numerical integral). Scripts: `claude/run2_overlap_nonzero_proof.py`, `claude/run2_ceiling_proof_summary.py`.
Result: **the even-level exclusion is provably only quantitative** under the $(ξ_d·ξ_{d'})^2$ kernel. l-parity gives an exact zero only across parity (odd-l unreachable from even-l, ⭐); within the reachable even-l class there is no analogous symmetry, because the kernel weight s=3/2≠1 moves the overlap off its sole zero. The even/excluded distinction lives entirely in the magnitude of a never-vanishing, smoothly-decaying coupling — a continuum with no structural cut (this is the structural reason run #1 saw the coupling "continuous down to 1.5×10⁻⁹": the floor is $(1/3)^{n_r}$, not a zero). **🔵 is therefore the proven ceiling for the even-level class**; an exact ✅ cut is structurally impossible under this kernel. The remaining honest open question is no longer "is there a hidden zero" (answered: no) but the quantitative one — whether the IDWT EOM yields a sharp survival condition Γ(n,d) < ΔE satisfied by exactly the tower indices. Running record: `claude/tower_selection_search_log.md`.

**Survival condition Γ(n,d) < ΔE(n,d) does NOT select the tower — survival-ratio avenue closed (2026-06-05, run #3)**
Conjecture (the run #2 next-step): a mode (n,d) is stable iff its dephasing rate stays below the local level spacing, Γ(n,d) < ΔE(n,d); since the sector scale m_scale,d cancels, the dimensionless survival ratio ρ(n,d)=Γ/ΔE=|ME(n,d)|/[S(n+1,d)−S(n,d)] should cross its natural threshold (ρ=1) exactly at the tower boundary, selecting the 15 indices and excluding all others (d ∈ D, n ∈ [0,200]).
Checked (`claude/run3_survival_ratio.py`, runnable; self-calibrated against STEP 30's ME(n=3→n=1)≈6.3 and STEP 34's no-node overlap):
- Level spacing: the exact hockey-stick forward increment ΔE(n,d)=m_scale,d·[S(n+1,d)−S(n,d)]=m_scale,d·C(n+d−1,d−1) (backward spacing C(n+d−2,d−1) tested too; same conclusion). The dephasing ME rides the no-node overlap envelope ME(n,d)=C₀·|J(n_r,3/2)|, n_r=⌊(n−1)/2⌋, with C₀ fixed by the one known matrix element.
- ρ(n,d) is **strictly monotonically decreasing in n in every sector** (ME ~ (1/3)^{n_r} geometric; spacing ~ n^{d−1} polynomial). A single threshold on a monotone ρ selects a contiguous low-n band.
- The tower indices are scattered, not a low-n prefix: NS ρ-values span the entire range, from 4.2 (down, n=1) down to 9×10⁻²³ (Higgs, n=95) and 7×10⁻¹³ (muon, n=35) — the heavy NS modes have *smaller* ρ than thousands of excluded light modes. NS ρ-ranks within their sector: d=4 → {2,19,71}, d=2 → {75,80,94,200}, d=5 → {9,14,21}.
- Natural threshold ρ=1 (Γ=ΔE): TP=1/15 (only the down quark); the other 14 NS modes are deep in Γ≪ΔE alongside the excluded modes. Best single threshold (ρ>0) = 14/15 TP but 1186 FP (restates run #2: every even-level mode couples; none vanishes). Most-generous **per-sector tuned** thresholds still give total FP=120, FN=9 — it fails *within* each sector, because the NS indices are scattered inside each sector too.
Result: **necessary-not-sufficient; the survival-ratio avenue is closed.** A survival ratio with one threshold can only carve a monotone-in-n boundary, so it cannot equal a scattered set of hockey-stick/additive tower images (n=3,20,72 in d=4 are simplex images, not a smooth prefix). The failure is in the *shape*, not the normalization: rescaling C₀ or multiplying ME by any smooth positive factor leaves ρ monotone and the NS scattered, so no choice of constant fixes it. This is the structural trap run #2 explicitly anticipated. 🔵 remains the proven ceiling for the even-level exclusion, now doubly closed: run #2 killed the hidden-zero route, run #3 kills the dynamical-threshold route. An ✅ upgrade of the *selection* principle is not reachable from the kernel's coupling magnitudes. The one remaining avenue the magnitude tests cannot reach is a discrete fixed-point/closure property of Σ_indices under the tower operations (run #2 leg-1 additive closure over-generates; the open question is whether a *minimal* closed set under the full hockey-stick + additive + g operation set equals NS exactly). Running record: `claude/tower_selection_search_log.md`.

**Hockey-stick is the FP-free generator of the primary spectrum; over-generation is entirely additive (2026-06-05, run #4)**
Conjecture (Fedge lead): the hockey-stick identity constrains n to the observed spectrum.
Checked (`claude/run4_hockeystick_combinatoric.py`): pure hockey-stick closure n→S(n,d_eval) with **no additive steps**, iterated from the seed indices {1,3,4}, restricted to the quark engine sectors d_eval∈{3,4}, produces **exactly {1,3,4,10,15,20,35}** — the 7 primary NS modes (down, up, strange, ν₁, ν₂, charm, μ) — with **zero false positives** in the physical range n≤95 (the Higgs cutoff). Mechanism: the simplex count grows superlinearly (S(10,3)=220), so depth-1 HS images of the seeds land in range and depth-2 overshoots the whole spectrum — FP-free by construction, no tuning. Allowing all sectors d_eval∈D adds 9 false positives (6, 21, 28, 55, 56, 66, 84, 120, 126 — the d=5,6 simplex numbers); restoring the additive operation a+b−c reproduces the ~80-extra over-generation of the loose-orbit dead-end above. So the over-generation that sinks every combinatoric closure lives **entirely in the additive/composite layer, not the hockey-stick**. The 8 missed modes (photon 0, e 13, ν₃ 22, τ 23, top 72, W 76, Z 81, H 95) are the heterogeneous composite layer (additive sum, inclusion-exclusion, the Euler-product 3·4·6 for the top, the g-rule for W/Z) and are all **non-simplex numbers**.
Result: necessary-not-sufficient for forcing all 15, but a genuine refinement of the search. The hockey-stick is the **tight (FP-free) generator** of the 7 primary (simplex) modes; the per-(n,d) selection difficulty is concentrated in the composite layer — exactly where the framework's un-derived rules already sit (top product, boson g-rule, Higgs closure = the §13a "graph sources"). Consistent with g₂₂ and the CKM formula being state-counting (IDOS) results (§15, §20a): the hockey-stick is the IDOS engine and it is clean; the open problem is in how the counts are **combined** (the §13b DAG / MC-4), not in a missing hockey-stick identity.

**Composite layer reduces to the top's Euler product (the keystone) (2026-06-05, run #5)**
Conjecture: characterize the 8 composite (non-simplex) NS modes left by run #4 — is there a tight operation generating them from the 7 primaries, or are they irreducibly heterogeneous?
Checked (`claude/run5_composite_layer.py`), per-composite minimal route (n≤95):
- **e=13** = 10+3 and **τ=23** = 20+3 (primary+primary); **ν₃=22** = 10+15−3 (primary+primary−seed) — three tight depth-1 additive/inclusion-exclusion combos of primaries. (Loose additive/IE closures over-generate, 22–38 false positives, so it is the *specific* edges, not a closure.)
- **top=72** = χ(CP²)·χ(CP³)·χ(CP⁵) = 3·4·6, an **Euler product** (T15) — not reachable from lighter modes by hockey-stick, additive, or g-rule. The one irreducible non-hockey-stick structural input.
- **W=76** = g(5,72), **Z=81** = g(10,72), **H=95** = 3+20+72: the entire heavy-boson branch is a g-rule/additive **cascade off the top**.
- **photon=0** = the d=2 ground state S(0,d)=0 (trivial zero mode).
Result: the full 15-particle combinatoric content bottoms out at a small irreducible core — seeds {n_d=1, n_u=3} and composite n_s=4 (→ hockey-stick → 7 primaries → 3 light additive composites) + **n_top = 3·4·6** (Euler product), with the photon the trivial zero mode. The heavy sector (top, W, Z, H) all hangs off the single Euler-product fact n_top, which is therefore the **keystone** of the spectrum's combinatoric structure. This sharpens §13a (graph sources = photon, muon, top, Higgs) and §5 (n_top open): the search localizes the irreducibility to n_top. What stays open (MC-4) is *which* specific additive/g edges fire — loose closures over-generate, so the composite edges are the "specific sequence" and n_top's Euler product is an independent input — but the mystery is now a small named core, not spread across all fifteen. The hockey-stick is vindicated as the tight (FP-free) engine; the residue is dynamics.

**d-guided n: sector Euler characteristics seed the per-sector generators (2026-06-05, run #6)**
Conjecture (Fedge lead): invert the §15 "d is not a function of n" dead-end — use the sector d to constrain the admissible n *within* each sector.
Checked (`claude/run6_d_guided.py`): the observed per-sector n-spectra [d=2 {0,76,81,95}; d=3 {1,4}; d=4 {3,20,72}; d=5 {10,15,22}; d=6 {13,35}; d=10 {23}] are organized by sector geometry, with the **Euler characteristic χ(sector) the geometric input that seeds each sector's n's**: n_u = χ(CP²) = 3 (d=4's first up-type mode is its own Euler char); n_e = χ(CP³)² − n_u = 16−3 = 13; n_μ = S(χ(CP³), χ(CP³)) = S(4,4) = 35; n_top = χ(CP²)·χ(CP³)·χ(CP⁵) = 3·4·6; the composite n_s = 4 = χ(CP³). Base sectors (even d, CP^{d/2}) are Euler-char-driven; total sectors (odd d, Sᵈ, χ=0) are Hopf-image-driven (d=5: S(n_u,3), S(n_u,4), inclusion-exclusion). Per-sector generation counts [d=3..6] = [2,3,3,2], symmetric about d=4.5 (the bottom is a beat in d=3, the tau is displaced d=6→d=10).
Result: the d-guided lens re-organizes the known T15 Euler-characteristic identities under "d seeds n" and confirms the geometric inputs are the sector χ's, not arbitrary — but each sector still uses its own generator, so there is no single uniform d→n formula (the same heterogeneity as runs #4/#5, seen from the d→n side). It opens the genuinely new operator-level question (run #6b): does each sector's **Dirac operator spectrum** select its observed n's, the way Theorem S1's cumulative Dirac count gives S(n,3) = ½ N_D(n−1) on S³? That is uncomputed for the CPᵏ sectors and is where a real d→n selection rule would live.

**d-guided n: the sector Dirac spectrum does NOT spectrally select the per-sector n's (2026-06-05, run #6b)**
Conjecture (run #6 follow-up): each sector's Dirac/Laplace spectrum on its own manifold (S³, S⁵, CP², CP³, CP⁵) selects that sector's observed mode indices n, the way Theorem S1's cumulative S³ Dirac count grounds S(n,3).
Checked (`claude/run6b_sector_dirac.py`): computed the standard spectra — S^d Dirac eigenvalues ±(k+d/2) with multiplicity 2^{⌊d/2⌋}C(k+d−1,d−1) (Bär 1996); CP^k scalar Laplacian eigenvalues 4m(m+k) with multiplicity (2m+k)/k · C(m+k−1,m)² (Ikeda–Taniguchi; verified to reproduce the S² multiplicities 2m+1 for CP¹ and 1,8,27,64,… for CP²); the spin^c Dirac/HRR index ladder ind(D^c⊗O(j)) = C(j+k,k) = S(j+1,k) (Part 8 §2.2). Five selection conditions were tested per sector against the observed n's ({3,20,72} CP², {13,35} CP³, {23} CP⁵, {10,15,22} S⁵): C1 level where a multiplicity equals χ; C2 n is a spin^c index C(j+k,k); C3 Dirac/Laplace eigenvalue resonant with the harmonic level 2N+d; C4 n appears as a Laplace multiplicity value; C5 n equals a Laplace eigenvalue index m.
Result: **negative — no sector-spectral condition selects the observed n's.** Per sector, every condition either misses the n's entirely (C1, C3, C4), hits at most one via an already-known χ-identity (C2 hits n=3 in CP² because 3=C(2,2) is the index, and n=35=C(7,2) in CP³, both restatements of T15), or over-generates by 100+ false positives (C5). The decisive structural reason: **Theorem S1's cumulative Dirac count IS a mass law, not a selector — it holds at *every* level n** (verified: cumulative S^d positive-Dirac count = 2^{⌊d/2⌋}S(n,d) for all n≤120 in d=3,5), assigning a mass S(n,d) to each candidate n without distinguishing the physical ones. The S⁵ values {10,15,22} carry no intrinsic S⁵ spectral mark; they are the cross-sector Hopf/inclusion-exclusion images of d=4 (10=S(n_u,3), 15=S(n_u,4), 22=10+15−3), i.e. d=4→d=5 arithmetic, not an S⁵-intrinsic selection. **Honest verdict: the sector geometry SEEDS the per-sector generators (via χ, run #6) but does not spectrally SELECT the n's.** The manifold's intrinsic Dirac/Laplace spectrum imposes no per-sector cut on which harmonic n are physical; that selection lives in the cross-sector tower combinatorics (runs #4/#5: hockey-stick engine + n_top Euler product + specific composite edges), not in any single sector's operator spectrum. The d-guided lead is thereby bounded: χ-seeding is real and geometric; spectral selection is absent. ❓→ closed as null for the spectral-selection form.

**Cross-sector branching does NOT select the d=5/d=6 n's — it CARRIES the known Hopf-image structure (2026-06-05, run #7)**
Conjecture (run #6b follow-up, the last operator-level avenue): the *cross-sector* maps — the Hopf fibration S¹→S⁵→CP² and the inclusion CP²↪CP³ — select the observed cross-sector indices through their **representation-theory branching multiplicities** (U(1) charge sectors on S⁵; SU(4)↓SU(3) induced-rep multiplicities on CP³), rather than through any single sector's bare spectrum. A genuine selection would mark {10,15,22} (d=5) and {13,35} (d=6) by a structural rule (first-occurrence, charge==χ threshold, clean degeneracy) with low/zero over-generation, from the actual branching rather than from the Hopf-image arithmetic re-labeled.
Checked (`claude/run7_crosssector_branching.py`): (A) **S⁵→CP² Hopf U(1) decomposition.** L²(S⁵) = ⊕_{p,q≥0} V(p,q) over SU(3) irreps graded by Hopf charge r=p−q at harmonic level N=p+q (dim V(p,q) = ½(p+1)(q+1)(p+q+2), Weyl). The decomposition is exact and reproduces the CP² charge-0 (p,p) harmonics with dims 1,8,27,64,… (=(p+1)³, the run #6b values). At level N=3 the SU(3) irreps are V(3,0),V(2,1),V(1,2),V(0,3) of dims **10, 15, 15, 10** — and {10,15} are n_ν₁,n_ν₂. (B) **CP²↪CP³ branching SU(4)↓SU(3)** via Gelfand–Tsetlin interlacing: the CP³ spherical harmonics (the (m,0,m) reps, U(4) partition (2m,m,m,0)) decompose into SU(3) irreps, each with multiplicity 1, totalling (m+1)² irreps at level m. Tested rules: A1 "n is a V(p,q) dim in L²(S⁵)"; A2 "n is a CP² charge-0 harmonic dim"; B1 "n is an SU(4)↓SU(3) branching multiplicity"; B2/B3 "n is the irrep-count / total multiplicity of a CP³ level."
Result: **negative for selection — the branching carries the structure but does not select it.** (A) The appearance of 10 and 15 as level-3 V(p,q) dims is the *same Hopf-image arithmetic re-labeled, not an independent mark*: dim V(3,0)=10 and dim V(2,1)=15 are precisely S(n_u,3) and S(n_u,4), and recovering them requires putting n_u=3=χ(CP²) in as the charge/level input — exactly what run #6 already established as χ-seeding. The two values sit in *different* charge sectors at the same level (10 at r=±3 minimal-level, 15 at r=±1 non-minimal), so no single charge rule yields both; and ν₃=22 is not a V(p,q) dim at all (it is the IE composite 10+15−3). The rule "n is a V(p,q) dim" over-generates badly: FP=27, marking 1,3,6,8,21,24,27,28,35,36,… before and around the observed values. (B) The SU(4)↓SU(3) branching multiplicities are all 1 for the (m,0,m) class, so they mark *nothing* — no multiplicity equals 13 or 35, and the level counts (m+1)² miss both (B1–B3 all FN with FP=1–11). n_e=13=χ(CP³)²−n_u and n_μ=S(4,4)=35 are Euler-character arithmetic the branching does not reproduce. **Bottom line: the cross-sector geometry CARRIES the neutrino/lepton structure — the Hopf map genuinely relates d=5 to d=4 and the branching dims contain {10,15} — but it does not SELECT the n's by a branching rule; every "hit" is the known χ-seeded Hopf-image identity restated in rep-theory language, and the rules over- or under-generate.** This closes the last operator-level avenue: the per-(n,d) selection is not in coupling magnitudes (runs #1–3), flat combinatorics beyond the hockey-stick primaries (#4–5), any sector's own Dirac/Laplace spectrum (#6b), or the cross-sector Hopf/inclusion branching (#7). The residue is unambiguously dynamical — the tower DAG (MC-4): the hockey-stick is the FP-free engine, χ seeds the generators, the Hopf geometry carries d=4→d=5, and *which* composite edges fire is the open input, to be settled at the level of the equations of motion, not by any operator-spectral or branching cut. ⭐ for the exact branchings computed (Weyl/GT, verified); the selection claim is null. ❓→ closed as null for the cross-sector-branching form.

**MC-4.4 — DAG selection is not in the EOM energetics (2026-06-05, `claude/mc4_4_exploration.py`)**  
Conjecture (to test): the sufficient selector that fires the DAG rather than other BdG-stable even-level modes lives in the EOM energetics — specifically in one of: (1) Hartree mean-field self-consistency, (2) cross-sector energy resonance locking at the additive edges, (3) the χ-product index n_top=72 as an EOM kernel eigenvector condition, (4) a Lyapunov / conserved-charge level set of the kernel.  
Checked all four avenues (MC-4.4):  
- (1) Hartree: the l=0 diagonal shift λ_d=(g_dd/2)^{2/3} is smooth and present for all n; it fixes the well, not the excited indices. A cross-sector Hartree lock E_{n,d}+ΔE=E_{n',d'} needs energy near-degeneracy at the IE edges — (2) shows none exists.  
- (2) Cross-sector resonance locking: neither the IDWT mass m(n,d)=m_scale_d·S(n,d) nor the sector HO eigenvalue E_HO=(2(n−1)+d)√λ_d closes additively at the IE edges. Mass ratio at e=ν₁+up: 0.235 (should be 1); E_HO ratio at e: 0.757; at τ=ν₃+down: 1.054. The edges are pure index (count) relations, not energy resonances. DECISIVE NEGATIVE.  
- (3) n_top=72 = χ(CP²)·χ(CP³)·χ(CP⁵) = χ(CP²×CP³×CP⁵) by multiplicativity of χ. A topological identity, not a kernel eigenvector condition. It re-describes the value; it does not say why 72 fires and not 48 or 96.  
- (4) Lyapunov / conserved charge: the kernel's ONLY exact conserved charge is l-parity P=(n−1) mod 2 (STEP 30). Within a parity class the kernel admits ~half of every sector (≥60 d=3 modes per parity; DAG d=3 count = 4; reach/DAG = 15). No non-trivial linear charge is constant on the 15 modes. A depth-Lyapunov exists for the named DAG (acyclic, sources {(1,3),(4,3)}, max depth 6) but it grades the DAG *given* the productions; generic-schema lift → 1191 false positives.  
Positive byproduct: the quartic kernel level-law n_comp=n₁+n₂−1 (leading level N₁+N₂) plus the S(1,d)=1 ground-state offset reproduces the IE additive index n₁+n₂. The additive edges have a genuine kernel reading (two-density product seeded on the ground state) — it explains the edge **form** (🔶 motivated), not which pairs bind.  
Result: the SUFFICIENT selector is NOT in the EOM energetics. The selection is a **directed index derivation** — a terminating acyclic generator closure whose generators are motivated (hockey-stick ⭐, χ-seeding ✅, Hopf routing ✅) but whose firing-as-a-set is a postulated selection rule, not an EOM consequence. MC-4.1–4.3 establish the NECESSARY stability filter (BdG-stable Σ modes, dephasing non-Σ); the sufficient half is a combinatorial/topological question, not energetics. All four energetic/variational avenues are now closed. STEP 37 in `files/idwt.py` records the three checks with self-verified numerical output.

**MC-4.5 — the generator closure is not forced by any combinatorial/topological completeness condition (2026-06-05, `claude/mc4_5_exploration.py`)**  
Five angles tested; all clean negatives for distinct structural reasons:  
- **(A) Minimality:** NS is not the unique minimal closed set — three leaf modes (H, μ, τ) can be dropped; proper closed subsets exist. Generic-schema lift → 576 closures (15 hits, 561 FP). The 15 are isolated only by the specific predecessor-restricted productions.  
- **(B) IE-offset topology:** The level↔index +1 shift is an exact identity (S(1,d)=1, the χ=1 Gaussian vacuum), fixing the additive **form** of the kernel level-law ⭐. But the observed composite offset is non-uniform (e, τ: bare n₁+n₂; ν₃: n₁+n₂−n_up inclusion-exclusion). No single Euler/Hopf/Chern index forces a universal offset k=0.  
- **(C) Sector coverage:** Minimal coverage forces only 6 modes (one per sector); NS has 15. The 9 "extra" modes are unconstrained by coverage; routing is already forced by T3, not coverage.  
- **(D) DAG automorphism:** Aut(DAG) is trivial ⭐ (already in §13b). No natural S(n,d)/D symmetry (Pascal reflection, Hopf pairing) leaves NS invariant. Trivial Aut is rigidity, not forcing.  
- **(E) Schur-positivity / branching completeness:** NS d=5 is neither a complete level-truncation nor a Schur-positive sub-collection of L²(S⁵) (22 is not an irrep dim; {1,3,6,8} are dims not in NS). d=6 branching multiplicities are all 1. Consistent with run #7.  
Result: the generator closure is forced **only relative to the chosen generator list**, not by any minimality, topological-offset, coverage, symmetry, or branching-completeness condition. The generator list is motivated (HS ⭐, χ-seeding ✅, Hopf routing ✅) but its firing-as-a-set is postulated. P7/P8 remain 🔶.  
**Most promising remaining direction:** n_top=χ(CP²)·χ(CP³)·χ(CP⁵)=χ(CP²×CP³×CP⁵) as a cobordism or characteristic-number invariant of the product of the three deep Kähler matter sectors — the only route the MC-4.4–4.5 sweeps did not exhaust. None of the five angles addressed *why the heavy branch hangs off a single Euler product*; that is a question about the product manifold's characteristic classes, not the DAG's index arithmetic.

**MC-4.6 — characteristic-class invariant route exhausted (2026-06-05, `claude/mc4_6_exploration.py`)**  
Question: does the characteristic-class theory of CP²×CP³×CP⁵ (real dim 20, complex dim 10) provide an independent derivation of n_top = 72, or establish χ = 72 as the uniquely forced characteristic number?  
Method: computed all standard characteristic numbers of the product manifold: Euler characteristic (top Chern number), Todd genus (Hirzebruch χ_y at y=0), signature (χ_y at y=−1), Â-genus, all Pontryagin numbers, and sample Chern numbers (c₁^{10}).  
Results:

- **χ(CP²×CP³×CP⁵) = 72** via χ-multiplicativity (χ(X×Y)=χ(X)χ(Y)). This is c_{top} = c₂(CP²)·c₃(CP³)·c₅(CP⁵) = 3·4·6. The T15b identity n_top = χ(CP²)·χ(CP³)·χ(CP⁵) upgrades from "topological cross-check" to a genuine **characteristic-class theorem** (top Chern number of the product).
- **All Pontryagin numbers = 0** (structural, not a coincidence). The Pontryagin polynomial p(TCP^k) = (1+h²)^{k+1} carries only even powers of h, but the fundamental class of CP³ requires h₂^3 (odd power) — so no Pontryagin monomial can integrate non-trivially over the product. This forces σ=0 and Â=0 independently.
- **Signature = 0, Â-genus = 0, Todd genus = 1.**
- **c₁^{10} = 11,287,019,520** (≫ 72; Chern numbers other than c_{top} are astronomically large).
- **Spin structure:** CP² is not spin; CP³, CP⁵ are spin. The product is not spin → Dirac index = 0. No index-theorem route to n_top.
- **χ = 72 is the unique nonzero, non-trivial, purely topological characteristic number** compatible with an IDWT mode index. All other candidates are 0, 1, or O(10^{10}).

Conclusion (null result on forcing; positive result on uniqueness and status):  
The characteristic-class approach does NOT provide an independent derivation of n_top — the forcing still comes from T15. However, χ = 72 has a **uniqueness certificate**: it is the only characteristic number of CP²×CP³×CP⁵ that could plausibly equal n_top, and the T15b identity is now a characteristic-class theorem rather than arithmetic. Status of MC-4.6 route: **EXHAUSTED**. No further characteristic-class or cobordism angles remain. The standing goal (T0.5 from 🔶 toward ✅) remains open with no currently identified avenue.

**e⁺e⁻ → 3 jets explained by 4D (and 3D) quarks, with no gluon (2026-06-06)**  
Conjecture (Fedge, prompted by an external "IDWT predicts triple jets" take): the third jet in e⁺e⁻ → 3 jets is not gluon bremsstrahlung but a consequence of up-type quarks being d=4 (CP²) — the extra sector coordinate absorbs/re-emits the momentum that QCD attributes to a radiated spin-1 gluon. IDWT has no propagating gluon (colour is the d=4 kernel contact term, no kinetic term: Part 3 §0.2, §0.6; Part 8 §confinement-open). Test whether the d=4 (and d=3) quark structure reproduces the measured 3-jet phenomenon.  
Checked (four independent, model-independent observables, each fatal):  
- **Soft/collinear scaling.** The measured 3-jet rate diverges as α_s·ln²(1/y_cut) as the jet-resolution y_cut→0 — the unique signature of bremsstrahlung of a *massless propagating vector*. IDWT colour has no kinetic term, hence no propagating mode and no soft/collinear enhancement; a point-like contact vertex (g_{44} or g_{33}) gives a finite, non-divergent rate with no ln²(1/y_cut). Cannot be reconciled.  
- **3D kinematic balance.** Real 3-jet events are coplanar and 3-momentum-balanced in the CM frame; the third jet carries up to ≈⅓√s of *visible* energy. A "momentum kick into the hidden 4th coordinate" would register as MISSING 3-momentum (the bound-within/free-without projection rule), not a balanced visible jet. The energy demonstrably stays in the 3D slice. Excludes the extra-coordinate mechanism.  
- **Flavour universality.** Three-jet events occur off down-type primaries — b, s, d are d=3 (S³), with NO fourth coordinate — at the same rate as up-type; bb̄g is well measured at LEP. The 4D-extra-coordinate mechanism predicts ≈0 third-jet rate for 3 of the 5 accessible flavours. Falsified directly.  
- **Quark vs gluon jet difference.** The measured gluon/quark jet multiplicity ratio trends toward C_A/C_F = 9/4 (observed ≈1.5 at finite energy, ≠ 1). This requires an octet colour charge; IDWT has no octet object, so it predicts ratio = 1.  
- Numerology check: IDWT g²_eff = 2g_{44}/π² = 0.919 ⇒ g²_eff/(4π) = 0.073, not α_s(M_Z) ≈ 0.118; and IDWT does not run couplings, so the comparison is cross-framework only.  
Result: NEGATIVE. The 4D/3D-quark mechanism is excluded *upstream of any matrix-element computation* by the soft/collinear, kinematic-balance, and flavour-universality tests — computing the contact-term amplitude is therefore moot. The structural negative that IS IDWT (no fundamental gluon ⇒ the third jet is not gluon bremsstrahlung) stands, but IDWT has no positive account of the 3-jet final state; 2-jet (1+cos²θ) production is fine (spin-½ quarks). Together the four observables make e⁺e⁻ → 3 jets strong evidence for a propagating spin-1 colour-octet gluon, which IDWT explicitly lacks — a genuine falsifiability-pressure point for the colour sector. Candidate home if developed: Part 6 Falsifiability (Fedge decision pending). Do not repeat this search.

**Quantum tunnelling time / Hartman effect as a hidden-dimension shortcut (2026-06-06)**  
Conjecture: the near-zero, barrier-width-independent tunnelling times (Hartman effect; attoclock results consistent with ~0 delay) are because the d=6 electron routes "around" a 3D-built barrier through its hidden coordinates — the AB "a 3D wall can't contain a 6D object" mechanism applied to a potential barrier.  
Test (analytic, with numerical confirmation): a tunnelling barrier is a potential $V$ created by 3D sources; by the 1/R projection theorem (Part 3 §0.8a) the coherent potential the electron feels is a function of the observable coordinate(s) only — $V=V(z)$ — and is **uniform in the hidden coordinates** $\xi_{4,5,6}$. The 6D Schrödinger problem then *separates*: the hidden coordinates are free transverse modes, decoupled from the barrier, and the tunnelling reduces to the standard 1D problem in $z$ with $E_z=E-E_\perp$. Confirmed numerically: at fixed $E_z$ the Wigner phase time is identical regardless of the number of free transverse (hidden) dimensions or the energy in them (`claude/koide_check.py` sibling check, rectangular barrier).  
Result: NEGATIVE. The hidden dimensions provide **no spatial shortcut** (the barrier is uniform — effectively infinite — in those directions, so there is nothing to go around) and **no timing change** (decoupled free modes). IDWT reproduces the standard 1D tunnelling time and inherits the Hartman effect unchanged — no distinctive prediction. 

*Why it fails where AB/AC succeed — a reusable criterion (⭐ structural).* Both the AB/AC field and a tunnelling barrier are uniform in the hidden coordinates ("free without"), so the distinction is NOT localized-vs-uniform — it is what the hidden dimensions are asked to do. **AB/AC:** a 3D shield tries to keep a field's influence off the electron and fails, because that influence is not confined to the blocked 3D region — it reaches the electron through the hidden coordinates it shares with the field. The hidden dimensions carry an influence *around* the shield. **Tunnelling:** the electron must cross a barrier $V(z)$ along an *observable* direction $z$; the hidden coordinates are transverse to $z$, and (by the 1/R projection theorem, Part 3 §0.8a) the barrier takes the same value at every hidden-coordinate value, so moving in them neither advances $z$ through the forbidden region nor lowers the barrier. The hidden dimensions cannot substitute for blocked observable motion. **Criterion:** the slice mechanism yields a distinctive effect when the experiment relies on *confining a field/influence inside a 3D region* (containment fails — influence leaks through the hidden coordinates: AB, AC, and the marginal/cloud and entanglement cases); it yields nothing when the experiment relies on *traversing a barrier defined along an observable coordinate* (the transverse hidden dimensions offer no detour — tunnelling, where IDWT reduces to the standard 1D problem). One line: **hidden dimensions bypass shields, not walls.** Do not re-attempt the tunnelling shortcut.

**Cross-sector scale incommensurability — proved lemma ✅ (2026-06-09, `claude/explore_scale_incommensurability.py`)**

Claim: every cross-sector ratio $m_{\rm scale,d}/m_{\rm scale,d'}$ is irrational except $m_{\rm scale,6}/m_{\rm scale,10} = 1$.

Verified exactly by symbolic algebra (sympy) over the algebraic definitions of all six scales (Part 2 §10, Part 2 §9c). All 15 cross-sector pairs checked; the only rational ratio is $m_{\rm scale,6}/m_{\rm scale,10} = 1$ (the μ–τ symmetric pair, an exact consequence of $m_{\rm scale,10} \equiv m_{\rm scale,6}$). The irrational ratios split into two algebraic classes: pairs involving exactly one sector from $\{3,4\}$ crossed with $\{2,5,6,10\}$ have ratio² in $\mathbb{Q}\cdot\sqrt{7}$ ($\sqrt{7} = \sqrt{n_s+n_u}$, the quark discriminant); all other pairs (within $\{2,5,6,10\}$, and the pair (3,4) internally) have rational ratio². Numerical summary: `files/idwt.py` STEP 40.

Consequence: the "no common revival period" step in Part 7 §1.2 Mechanism 2 is upgraded from "motivated by the incommensurate spectrum" to a proved lemma for 14 of the 15 cross-sector pairs. The unique commensurate pair (d=6, d=10) is the μ–τ symmetric pair; its commensurability reflects the tower identity $m_{\rm scale,6}=m_{\rm scale,10}$ and provides a new structural reading of why the tau at d=10 phase-locks with the muon at d=6.

**Gaussian-binomial / finite-geometry values as a mode-index selector (2026-06-09, `claude/explore_gaussian_binomial.py`)**  
Conjecture (Fable-5 pass): the 15 mode indices are Gaussian-binomial counts $[m\,k]_q$ at small prime powers $q$, extending the two known finite-geometry identities — $n_e = N_c^2+N_c+1$ = points of $PG(2,3)$ = the Poincaré polynomial of $\mathbb{CP}^2$ at $x=N_c$ (the $q$-deformed $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^2)$ at $q=N_c$), $n_s = 1+N_c$ = $\chi_q(\mathbb{CP}^1)|_{q=N_c}$, and Part 9 T4's $PG(3,2)$ remark ($n_\mu = 35$ = lines, $q$-vertex $15$ = points).  
Checked: all values $[m\,k]_q \le 95$ for $q\in\{2,3,4\}$, $m\le14$ — 12 such integers exist. NS hits 5/14: $3=[2\,1]_2$, $4=[2\,1]_3$, $13=[3\,1]_3$, $15=[4\,1]_2$, $35=[4\,2]_2$. Misses all composites and bosons $\{1,10,20,22,23,72,76,81,95\}$. Hypergeometric null (14 indices from $[1..95]$): $p=0.015$ for $\ge5$ hits — before any look-elsewhere over the choice of $q$-set and range, so consistent with chance.  
Result: NULL as a selector — the $q$-hits do not cover NS and the enrichment is not significant after look-elsewhere. The positive residue (kept as ❓ observations, not used anywhere): the $q=N_c$ hits are exactly $\{n_s, n_e\}$ — the $q$-deformed Euler characteristics of the first two Hopf bases ($\chi(\mathbb{CP}^1)=2\to n_s=4$, $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^2)=n_u\to n_e=13$) — and the $q=2$ hits $\{3,15,35\}$ are the $PG(\cdot,2)$ family. A "mode indices are $q$-deformations of the $\chi$-seeds" reading exists for the five hits but mixes $q$ values and explains no composite. Do not re-run as a flat search; any revival needs a principle fixing $q$ per sector first.

**Universal heat-kernel curvature-correction template $\chi/(24\,S)$ (2026-06-09, `claude/explore_curvature_template.py`)**  
Conjecture (Fable-5 pass): the three documented small multiplicative corrections — Cabibbo $1+1/240$, tau $1+1/1680$, GTC $\varepsilon=1/(280\sqrt{7})$ — are instances of one heat-kernel law $1 + R(\mathbb{CP}^k)/(24\,S)$, generalising the Cabibbo case (Part 3 §12), where $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^1)/(24\,S(n_s,3)) = 2/(24\cdot20) = 1/240$.  
Checked: the Cabibbo form uses $R(\mathbb{CP}^1)=2$, which equals $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^1)$ only because $k=1$. The actual Fubini–Study scalar curvature (unit-$\mathbb{CP}^1$ normalisation, holomorphic sectional curvature $c=1$) is $R(\mathbb{CP}^k)=k(k+1)$: $\{2,6,12,30\}$ for $k=1,2,3,5$ — equal to $k\cdot\chi(\mathbb{CP}^k)$, not $\chi$. Solving the template for the denominator the tau correction would need gives $S=280$ (with $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^3)=4$) or $S=840$ (with the true $R=12$); the GTC needs $S\approx185$ or $\approx926$. None is a tower mode index, and $280$ in the GTC carries an explicit $\sqrt{7}$ from $g_{33}=8\sqrt7$ — a coupling, not a curvature.  
Result: NULL as a unifying law. The clean $\chi/(24S)$ form does not extend beyond $\mathbb{CP}^1$ (where $R=\chi$ accidentally), and the three corrections have distinct documented mechanisms — Cabibbo a heat-kernel curvature correction, tau a back-reaction resummation ($1680=n_u\,n_s^2\,S(n_s,4)$), GTC a per-quark coupling shift ($\varepsilon\,g_{33}=1/35$). They are not three instances of one template. Do not re-attempt the unified-curvature reading.

**Generator route-multiplicity ($\ge 2$ independent routes) as the T0.5 selector (2026-06-09, `claude/explore_route_multiplicity.py`)**  
Conjecture (Fable-5 pass): the physical mode indices are exactly those reachable by $\ge 2$ *independent* generator routes (multiply-derivable = "co-fixed" under several generation maps at once), a sharper condition than the reachability/closure scans already in §15. Motivated by the §11 join table listing several indices with two side-by-side derivations ($n_e=g(d{=}4,n_{\nu_1})=g(d{=}10,n_s)=13$; $n_\tau=n_c+n_u=g_{3,4}(n_s,n_c)=23$).  
Checked: counted distinct generator routes for every integer in $[0,100]$ under the documented generators — simplex $S(k,d)$, join $g(a,b)=a{+}b{-}1$, additive $a{+}b$, subtractive $a{+}b{-}c$ ($c\in\{1,n_u,n_s\}$) — with inputs restricted to the 15 NS indices $\cup\;D$. Every NS index has high multiplicity (6–14 routes), so the threshold $\ge 2$ admits all 15 with zero misses — but it also admits 71 non-NS integers (86 selected total; 71 false positives at threshold 2, still 59 at threshold 4).  
Result: NULL — route-multiplicity does not separate NS from the unoccupied integers; it reproduces the over-generation of the §15 operational-closure dead ends (the generator set is too permissive, so high multiplicity is generic, not specific to NS). The redundancy noted in §11 is real but is a consequence of the rich Pascal arithmetic, not a selection principle. Do not re-run multiplicity thresholds; any selector must restrict *which* routes are admissible (the specific directed DAG), not count them.

**Crystallographic / cyclotomic criterion $\varphi(\chi)\le 2$ as a derivation of the d=8 gap (2026-06-09, `claude/explore_f1_cyclotomic_obstruction.py`)**  
Conjecture (Fable-5 pass, F1): the active even sectors $d=2k$ have bases $\mathbb{CP}^k$ with $\chi(\mathbb{CP}^k)=k+1\in\{2,3,4,6\}$ for $d\in\{2,4,6,10\}$, and this set is exactly $\{\chi\ge2:\varphi(\chi)\le2\}$ — the crystallographic restriction (cyclic orders compatible with a rank-2 lattice; equivalently $\mathbb{Q}(\zeta_\chi)$ at most quadratic). Proposed as an independent derivation of the $d=8$ gap ($\chi=5$, $\varphi=4$) and the even-chain termination after $d=10$, via either (a) a $Z_\chi$ lattice symmetry on a sector rank-2 lattice or (b) the requirement $\zeta_\chi\in$ the (degree-$\le2$) kernel coupling field.  
Checked (opus derivation attempt, both legs): **(b) FIELD route gives the wrong set.** The even-sector couplings are $g_{22}=1445/2$, $g_{44}=12/\sqrt7$, $g_{66}=g_{10,10}=1/4$, generating the **real** quadratic field $\mathbb{Q}(\sqrt7)$ ($\sqrt7=\sqrt{n_s+n_u}$, from the seed self-consistency discriminant). The cyclotomic fields for the active $\chi$ are $\mathbb{Q}(\zeta_3)=\mathbb{Q}(\sqrt{-3})$, $\mathbb{Q}(\zeta_4)=\mathbb{Q}(i)$, $\mathbb{Q}(\zeta_6)=\mathbb{Q}(\sqrt{-3})$ — all **imaginary** quadratic, none a subfield of the real $\mathbb{Q}(\sqrt7)$. So "$\zeta_\chi$ in the coupling field" holds only for $\chi=2$ ($\zeta_2=-1\in\mathbb{Q}$); the criterion that matches $\{2,3,4,6\}$ is the *abstract* cyclotomic degree $\varphi(\chi)\le2$, not embeddability in the coupling field, and the two are inequivalent. The actual couplings $g_{66}=g_{10,10}=1/4$ are rational and carry no $Z_\chi$ symmetry — the premise that the coupling "knows about" $\zeta_\chi$ is false. **(a) LATTICE route has no carrier.** There is no rank-2 $\mathbb{Z}$-lattice intrinsic to the sector for $Z_\chi$ to act on: the frequency comb $H_d(\omega)$ is a 1D phase filter (Part 2 §2), $H^2(\mathbb{CP}^k;\mathbb{Z})=\mathbb{Z}$ is rank 1 with the cyclic coordinate symmetry fixing the hyperplane class (trivial action), and the $k+1$ torus-fixed cells form a poset, not a geometric lattice.  
Result: NULL — the derivation does not close. The extensional match $\varphi(\chi)\le2\Leftrightarrow\{2,3,4,6\}$ is exact but coincidental between two inequivalent characterizations of the set; neither proposed IDWT mechanism bridges them (field route selects only $\chi=2$; lattice route has no rank-2 carrier). This is the "famous-small-set" trap the conjecture itself flagged. The $d=8$ gap and the $d=10$ termination remain established by their existing independent routes — T3 Rule A (Hopf-chain coupling termination) and Rule B / T5 (Gegenbauer criticality $b=1/2$). F1 is not an independent third route and is not promoted. Do not re-attempt the cyclotomic-degree derivation without first exhibiting a genuine rank-2 lattice (or a coupling-field embedding) that the active sectors actually carry.

**Three-mode cross-sector kernel ME as a resonance condition for the additive tower edges (2026-06-10, `claude/explore_threemode_kernel_me.py`)**
Conjecture (from gifts-from-claude, 2026-06-10, approved by Fedge): for the documented additive edges $n_c = n_a + n_b$ of the generation tower (strange = down+up; e = up+ν₁; μ = charm+ν₂ and ν₃+e; τ = down+ν₃ and ν₁+e; W = strange+top; H = top+τ), the shared-coordinate overlap $\mathrm{ME}(n_c) = \langle (n_c,d_c)|V|(n_a,d_a)\otimes(n_b,d_b)\rangle$ is extremal exactly at $n_c = n_a+n_b$, which would give the additive index rule a kernel fixed-point reading and an upgrade path for T0.5. A per-edge resonance question, not a set-level selector, so not covered by the 2026-06-05 fixed-point-lens blow-up null above.
Checked: radial oscillator mode functions and λ_d exactly as in `files/idwt.py` STEP 30 / §3.10.4 table; lowest-l channel per mode (l-parity, §22); a and b uniform beyond their own sectors (STEP 33), so the product contributes $R_a(r)R_b(r)$ on the shared radial coordinate; two integrand variants for robustness — plain overlap $\int R_c R_a R_b\, r^{d_c-1} dr$ and kernel-weighted $\int R_c R_a R_b\, r^4 r^{d_c-1} dr$ (the $(\xi\cdot\xi')^2$ radial dependence). Scanned $n_c \in [1, n_a+n_b+25]$ for all 8 edges × 2 variants.
Result: NULL. In 15 of 16 scans the target $n_c = n_a+n_b$ is neither the global maximum nor a local extremum of $|\mathrm{ME}(n_c)|$; target ranks are mid-pack (e.g. μ = ν₃+e: rank 44/60; H = top+τ: rank 100/120). The single hit (strange = down+up, kernel-weighted variant, argmax exactly at $n_c=4$) is consistent with chance given the tiny index range and 16 scans. The shared-coordinate kernel overlap is a smooth envelope with no structure at the additive edges; the additive index rule does not have a kernel-resonance reading under the $(\xi\cdot\xi')^2$ kernel with the established mode functions. Analytic side note: exact selection by level addition (disjoint excitation subspaces at a common frequency, $N_c = N_a+N_b$) would force $n_c = n_a+n_b-1$ — one below every tower edge — and is unavailable anyway because the sector frequencies λ_d differ; the tower's $+1$ relative to level addition is the same unexplained $+1 = n_{\rm down}$ offset noted in §10. The avenue is closed; with it, the gifts-from-claude fixed-point suggestion is fully dispositioned. Any revival needs a different coupling object (e.g. an EOM-derived vertex), not a different scan of this overlap.

**Sector assignment n → d from blind-lattice arithmetic invariants (2026-06-10, `claude/explore_prism_latesplit.py`, Test A; Fedge late-split proposal)**
Conjecture (Fedge): if the sector geometries and scales act downstream of the index selection ("prism / late-split" picture — supported by the Part 2 §12 two-layer mass structure, the rank-1 sector-uniform shifts, and the sector-blind index arithmetic of the additive edges and the k₀=16 multi-characterisation), then the assignment of each selected index n to its sector d should be at least partially recoverable from arithmetic invariants of the index set alone, with no sector input.
Checked: 22 single invariants of n over the 15 particles — n mod m and level (n−1) mod m for m=2..10, level parity, Ω(n), Pascal-column membership, tower-DAG depth — each scored as a partition against the true sector partition (Adjusted Rand Index, 20000-shuffle permutation p). Also scanned all invariant pairs for an exact sector-pure map.
Result: NULL as an assignment map. Best single invariant is DAG depth (ARI 0.344, raw p = 0.0085 — not significant against the 22-invariant look-elsewhere, and structurally expected since the derivation visits sectors in order; its pure classes are up+charm (d=4), ν₁+ν₂ (d=5), W+H (d=2)). All other invariants are chance-level (|ARI| ≤ 0.05). No invariant pair gives a non-trivial exact map (the only sector-pure pairings need 14 classes for 15 particles — memorisation, not a rule). The sector assignment carries information not present in the bare integers: the split is genuinely physical (Hopf-chain manifold assignment, §13b), not arithmetic bookkeeping. This computationally confirms the documented two-chain statement of Part 7 ("d cannot be recovered from n alone"; the tower derives n, the Part 1 §3 sector structure assigns d). It does not refute the late-split picture — it locates the prism's content in the geometry, not the lattice.

**Conjunction of all documented selection gates saturates the lattice — the gates constrain channel type, never operand choice (2026-06-12, `claude/explore_a3_tower_census.py` Part 2; run #8 in the tower-selection series).**
Conjecture: imposing ALL documented necessary selection gates SIMULTANEOUSLY in one generative closure from the re-rooted seeds {(1,3), (3,4)} — G1 l-parity channel typing (odd levels only via the parity-flip offset/IE/g channels or protected simplex images), G2 the run-#4 FP-free hockey-stick restriction (d_eval ∈ {3,4}), G3 the §25 insertion-parity rule (plain additive = 1 insertion → matter sectors only; g-rule = 0 and triple additive = 2 insertions → d=2 allowed), G4 g-rule increments d′−1 with d′ ∈ D, G5 the Euler product n_top = 3·4·6 as the single non-combinatoric input — with depth cap 6 (the §13b DAG maximum), reduces the over-generation below the prior single-gate baselines (1191 FP generic; 130–640 FP parity-gated).
Checked: BFS closure over (n,d), d ∈ D, n ≤ 95, all five gates active, depth ≤ 6.
Result: NULL — total saturation. All 96 index values in [0,95] are reached (15/15 NS hits, 81 value-level false positives; 556 (n,d) false positives). The structural reason is sharper than the FP count: every documented gate is a constraint on the *channel type* of a production (its level-parity behaviour, its insertion count, its target sector, its increment set) — none restricts *which operands* may combine. Since the additive/IE/g channels accept arbitrary reached operands, the closure saturates regardless of how the channels are typed. This sharpens MC-4.5 and the fixed-point-lens null: the entire residue of T0.5 is operand selection (which specific pairs fire), a question on which the channel-typing gates — l-parity, insertion parity, sector targeting — provably have zero purchase. Any future selector must constrain operand choice directly (e.g. from the nonlinear EoM's amplitude dynamics), not the production channels.

**Modulational-instability / four-wave-mixing-comb lens on the tower (2026-06-13, `claude/explore_mi_prism{,2,3}.py`; Fedge "laser-cavity / intense-source" prompt).**
Conjecture: the master-field analogy in T1 (S(n,d) = transverse-mode count of a sector cavity) extends to mode *selection* — the tower is the modulational-instability sideband comb of an intense sector-blind master field four-wave-mixing off its own carrier (late-prism Layer-1, pre-split), with the Hopf chain prisming the selected integers into sector rays (Test A). Two concrete sub-claims: (i) a linear Bogoliubov / modulational-stability spectrum around the condensate selects the comb; (ii) the comb is a four-wave-resonant (phase-matched) set in index space.
Checked (three scripts): index-space 3-/4-wave resonance census on the 14 indices; FWM closure from the seeds; Bogoliubov–de Gennes spectrum (repulsive and focusing sign) on the (ξ·ξ′)² r²-coupling kernel; the l=0→even-l angular cascade; the Pascal-block (a,b) sweep; carrier/sideband reflection through candidate carriers.
Results:
- **(i) Linear modulational instability is NON-SELECTIVE — NULL.** The BdG block [[A,B],[−B,−A]] with A=H₀+2gρK, B=gρK is fully stable for the repulsive sign (zero complex eigenfrequencies, every g,ρ tested) and pervasively unstable for the focusing sign (10–38 complex eigenfrequencies, max|Im| growing with |g|). Neither isolates the scattered tower levels. The selection is not a linear-instability band — same verdict the MC-4.4 energetics sweep reached from the Hartree side, now confirmed for the modulational-stability operator directly. The cavity lens supplies no *linear* selector.
- **(ii) The index lattice IS four-wave-resonance-saturated (positive structure, ⭐ arithmetic).** The 14 indices carry 9 exact 3-wave relations n_i+n_j=n_k, and they are precisely the documented production edges (1+3=4 strange; 3+10=13 e; 13+22=35 and 15+20=35 μ; 1+22=3+20=10+13=23 τ; 4+72=76 W; 23+72=95 H), plus 3 degenerate-FWM carriers (2·13=3+23=4+22; 2·15=10+20). τ is a 3-fold resonance sink; the seed invariant 96 = n_s³n_u/2 = g₃₃g₄₄ = g₂₂g₅₅ is a 3-fold 4-wave total (down+H = ν₂+Z = charm+W = 96). The index comb is genuinely FWM-locked; this is run #5's edge set re-read as a phase-matched comb in the massless Layer-1 lattice (where the conserved "momentum" is the index, not energy — consistent with the three-mode-kernel-ME null 2026-06-10, which showed the edges are index, not energy, resonances).
- **Two-layer separation, quantified.** Index lattice: 9 three-wave resonances (resonance-rich). S-value lattice: 0 three-wave resonances (sum-free; partly a sparseness artifact, noted). Phase-matching lives in the index/level lattice, energy non-resonance protects the realized modes — the modulational reading of the Part 1 §5 spectral-independence / stability-equivalence pair.
- **Candidate identity (❓, not placed): the three massive d=2 bosons are Hopf-invariant reflections of one matter primary from each of d=3,4,5.** W,Z,H = 96 − {charm(20,d=4), ν₂(15,d=5), down(1,d=3)} exactly, with 96 the Hopf coupling invariant. An alternative decomposition to run #5's "heavy-boson cascade off the top" (W=g(5,72), Z=g(10,72), H=3+20+72). Honest caveat: 96 − {7 primaries} also produces 4 non-tower values {61,86,92,93}, so the reflection is an exact identity for {W,Z,H} but not a spurious-free generator on its own. Do not place in any document without Fedge's view; verify against §13/§25 first.
- FWM closure from the seeds {1,3,4} reaches 14/14 but over-generates (101 values, 87 spurious) — the perennial closure blow-up; the Pascal block a=3,b=4 remains uniquely 14/14 (next best 11/14, all a=3), i.e. a restatement, not a dynamical selector (Part 9 T0.5).
Net: the cavity/MI lens contributes real positive structure (the comb is an index-space four-wave-locked frequency comb with a Hopf-invariant carrier) and one honest negative of consequence (linear modulational instability does not select the comb), converging with every prior selection null onto the same residue: operand selection is nonlinear/amplitude-level, not kinematic. T0.5 unchanged (🔶 backbone + 🔵 persistence; odd-level ⭐). The l=0→even-l angular cascade reproduces the ⭐ l-parity cut exactly. No document status edited.

**Companion — the nonlinear GP *dynamics* of the vacuum functional reproduces l-parity but does NOT select the even-level tower (2026-06-13, `claude/explore_gp_dynamics.py`).** Closes the last route flagged by the modulational run: the time-dependent basin-of-attraction question. Integrated the self-consistent GP flow of the explicit vacuum functional (E[Ψ]=∫|∇Ψ|²+(g/2)∫∫(ξ·ξ')²|Ψ|²|Ψ'|², separable mean field i Ȧ = [diag(ε)+gQ·M]A, Q=A†MA, M=(cosγ)² bounded angular kernel coupling l↔l,l±2) from the condensate seed A_{n=1}=1 plus 10⁻³ noise, norm-conserving RK4 (verified ‖A‖²=1.0000), g of both signs. Results: (i) **l-parity reproduced exactly** — population stays 100.00% on even levels (odd n), 0.00% on odd levels, for every g, since the kernel's l±2 structure connects N=0 only to even N (the ⭐ cut, dynamically). (ii) **First injection is clean** — the condensate feeds n=3 (up, a tower mode) at ~2×10⁻³, distinctly above the floor (the direct l=2 parametric daughter). (iii) **No tower selection beyond that** — the remaining amplitude sprays uniformly across the whole even ladder at ~10⁻⁶; tower members (5–6 of 14 reached) sit at the same population as non-tower even modes, and *which* tower members are reached changes with g (g=−0.5→{1,3,20,22,35}; g=+0.5→{1,3,13,15,20,23}) — i.e. noise-dependent, not selective. The conservative flow populates the even ladder; it does not pick the tower subset of it. Convergent conclusion across the whole 2026-06-13 investigation: the conservative dynamics (closed GP flow) supplies exactly the l-parity cut (⭐) and the condensate→up first step, and nothing finer; the even-level selection is not in it. The only dynamical home left for the even-level cut is the dissipative channel — spatial radiation through the downward kernel links — i.e. the Part 7 §1.2 stability equivalence (which even modes are protected against radiative decay), exactly where the documents already locate it. T0.5 unchanged. No document status edited.

**Quasicrystal cut-and-project / model-set reading of the tower selection — NULL for the operand, but the failure mechanism is informative (2026-06-13, Fedge request; `claude/explore_cut_project.py`; run #9 in the tower-selection series).** A genuine cut-and-project set selects lattice points whose projection into an internal space lands in a bounded acceptance window; its defining feature is an *irrational slope* of the physical space relative to the lattice. Dictionary tested: lattice = the integer mode pairs $(n,d)$ with $d$ restricted to the active set $D=\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$ (sector selection by Rule A/B is assumed — only the open *n*-within-sector operand selection is at issue, the T0.5 residue); internal coordinate $s(n,d)=\mathrm{frac}(\alpha n+\beta d)$; window = the smallest torus arc covering all 15 members. IDWT-native irrational slopes were used ($\sqrt7$ from $g_{33}=8\sqrt7$, golden $\varphi$, the seed ratios $\sqrt7/4$, $1/\sqrt7$, $\sqrt2$), plus a rational control $4/3$. **Result — null:** no single irrational slope produces a window that selects the $n$-index above chance. Best selectivity $=0.040$ ($1/\sqrt7$): the window accepts 356 non-members, against a no-structure baseline of $\sim362$ for a window of the same length over 554 candidates — i.e. the accepted count tracks window *length*, not membership; the rational control does worse, as a periodic slope should. **Why it fails (the informative part):** a model set is a Delone set — its gaps are *bounded* (this is forced by the linear projection through a finite window). The tower indices grow binomially, $S(n,d)=\binom{n+d-1}{d}$, so the within-sector spacings *grow* with $n$ (d=4: gaps 17 then 52; d=2: up to 74) instead of staying bounded. No fixed acceptance window can track a polynomially sparsening set. The tower's operand selection is combinatorial (binomial), not the linear/kinematic projection a cut-and-project window supplies — the same conclusion runs #1–8 reached from the coupling-magnitude, flat-combinatoric, spectral, and branching sides, now reconfirmed from the geometric (Delone) side. **Two positives kept honestly.** (1) IDWT *does* satisfy the model-set irrational-slope precondition: the incommensurability lemma (14/15 cross-sector scale ratios irrational, ✅, §15 STEP 40) is exactly the irrational-winding condition, and the torus-orbit time-average it drives is the cut-and-project reading of the even-level dephasing (the 🔵 bound) — but upgrading the status would require a *sharp* window (an exact accept/reject), and the test shows none exists; consistency with the GPT "acceptance-window" framing of the depth strip $d-k_{\min}\in\{2,3,4\}$ (§31) holds only at the necessary-not-sufficient level, matching run #8. (2) The per-sector index sets have $\le 3$ distinct consecutive gaps (d=3 $\{3,12\}$, d=4 $\{17,52\}$, d=5 $\{5,7\}$, d=2 $\{5,14,74\}$), nominally a Sturmian signature — but with 2–4 points per sector this is undersampled and not evidence. **Correction recorded:** a naive $(N\bmod 2)$ internal coordinate is *not* the $l$-parity window — only 8 of 16 members carry $n$ odd, so $n$-parity does not reproduce the cut; the exact $l$-parity window (⭐) lives in the angular-momentum $l$ on the sector sphere, not in the parity of the mode index. Net: the cut-and-project lens converges with every prior selection null; the residue stays the dissipative dynamical route (Part 7 §1.2). T0.5 unchanged. No document status edited.

**Complement decomposition of the tower selection — half the anti-tower is an exact infinite exclusion; the open core is one parity class (2026-06-13, Fedge directive "the complement is as significant as the tower"; `claude/explore_complement.py`; complement companion to runs #1–9).** Worked the selection from $\Sigma^c$ (every admissible $(n,d)$ that is NOT a physical particle) on equal footing with $\Sigma$, since $\chi_{\Sigma^c}=1-\chi_\Sigma$. **Clean statement (the deliverable):** $\Sigma^c$ splits exactly by level parity ($N=n-1$). (1) **Odd-level half ($n$ even), exact ⭐:** the $l$-content at odd $N$ is odd-$l$ only, kernel-disconnected from the even-$l$ ($l=0$) vacuum — no power of $V_{\rm kernel}$ reaches it (Part 7 §1.2). So no odd-level mode can be a spontaneously-populated stable resonance; this is an exact, infinite exclusion. The seven even-$n$ *members* ($\gamma,W$ in d=2; strange in d=3; charm, top in d=4; $\nu_1,\nu_3$ in d=5) are not counterexamples: they enter the spectrum only as composite tower *outputs* via the parity-flipping offset-additive / cross-sector channels (🔶 MC-4.4), a production statement distinct from kernel excitation, and persist by cross-sector coupling. (2) **Even-level half ($n$ odd), open 🔵:** the dephasing residue — and it is *exactly* the tower's even-level selection viewed from the complement, hitting the same proven ceiling (no exact kernel node at $s=3/2$, STEP 34 / run #2). Over $n\le120$, $d\in D$ the two halves are 353 vs 352 modes — the complement is ~50% exactly closed, and the open core is precisely the even-level (n odd) non-members. **Structural note:** d=6 and d=10 (charged leptons $e,\mu$ and $\tau$) have *zero* odd-level members — purely even-level; the quark/neutrino/boson sectors are mixed-parity. **Three complement-native sharp-rule probes on the open half — all null:** (i) additive-resonance "drain" ($n=n_a+n_b$ into lighter comb modes) over-protects 124 of 352 non-members and members are themselves sums (run #8 edges), so it does not separate; (ii) the downward-radiation shadow $\{(n-2,d)\}$ is finite (covers 7) against the infinite tail — but reconfirms downward-independence: every member's $(n-2,d)$ target is a non-member (STEP 64); (iii) on $S$-values the *members* are sum-free ($\{1,3,15,20,2002,\dots\}$, no member is a sum of two members — Part 1 §5 spectral-independence ⭐ reconfirmed), which characterizes the tower, not its complement. Net: the complement framing closes half the anti-tower exactly and pins the open part to a single parity class, but supplies no new exact cut for that class — converging with runs #1–9 on the dissipative-dynamics residue (Part 7 §1.2). The ⭐/🔵 split coincides with the late-prism Layer-1/Layer-2 seam: the exact half is selected by the parity of the sector-blind integer $n$ (pre-split, prism-immune $\Rightarrow$ exact), the open half by post-split scale-dependent dephasing (carries the scales $m_{\rm scale,d}$ $\Rightarrow$ 🔵) — full synthesis in `claude/late_prism_notes.md`. T0.5 unchanged. No document status edited. (Offer to Fedge: a short "complement decomposition" paragraph could be added to Part 7 §1.2 to record that the odd-level exclusion closes half of $\Sigma^c$ exactly — reported, not written.)

**Prism split into 6 sectors, and a parity×split-type observation (2026-06-13, Fedge directive "learn how the prism splits into 6"; `claude/explore_prism_split.py`, `claude/explore_orphan_parity.py`; full synthesis `claude/late_prism_notes.md`; diagram `claude/prism_split.svg`).** The prism = the complex Hopf chain $S^1\to S^{2n+1}\to\mathbb{CP}^n$; each step gives a (Kähler base $\mathbb{CP}^n=d{=}2n$, real total $S^{2n+1}=d{=}2n{+}1$) pair, and $D=\{2,3,4,5,6,10\}$ assembles as 4 Kähler bases $\{2,4,6,10\}$ + 2 real totals $\{3,5\}$ (verified to reproduce T3). Two termination edges: the real totals stop after $n{=}2$ ($d{=}5$) by Rule A (coupling chain terminates at $d{=}6$); the Kähler bases stop at $d{=}10$ by Rule B (Gegenbauer endpoint, $b_{k_0}(10)=\tfrac12$ exact, $d{=}8$ removed earlier by the $\chi{=}5$ gap). Through the meta-principle: the split's *which-rays + geometry* is scale-free/exact (⭐/✅, bar the Rule A $d{=}7$ residual 🔶); the scales $m_{\rm scale,d}$ are the scale-bearing Layer-2 datum (non-monotonic in $d$; 6/10 degenerate). **Parity×split-type pass (❓, weak).** The two orphan Kähler bases $d{=}6,10$ (leptons, terminated at the chain end) host *only* even-level ($n$ odd, $l{=}0$-present) members; the four paired sectors carry a doublet of odd-level ($n$ even) members each (exactly 2 — but that count needs the $b$-quark beat included; without it $d{=}3$ has 1). Significance is the robust $P=\tfrac18$ (orphans both zero) under an iid-parity null — suggestive, not significant; the "exactly 2" pattern is post-hoc ($P\approx1/404$ but cherry-picked). Mechanism (DAG-level, not derived): the orphan lepton bases are fed only by additive $\nu+$quark productions, each (even-$n$)+(odd-$n$)=odd-$n$=even-level; the odd-level (even-$n$) members elsewhere come from simplex/g-rule/IE/beat/reference channels feeding the quark/$\nu$/boson sectors. So parity content tracks the feeding channel, which tracks split position — recorded as a ❓ observation, not a structural claim. No document status edited.

**Single-sector effective-energy functional search for the Part 2 §5 vacuum-stability minima (2026-06-12, `claude/explore_vacuum_functional.py`)**

Conjecture: an effective energy E(n) built from documented T2 kernel vocabulary — simplex mass S(n,d), Gegenbauer weight 1/DegS, kernel coupling gc2=n(n+1)/S(n,d+1), and derived weights — has local minima at exactly {n=1, n=4} in d=3 at g₃₃=8√7, and the same functional form selects the d=4 seed n_u=3 at g₄₄=12/√7. This is the functional asserted (but not written) in Part 2 §5 line 242: "effective energy has local minima at exactly n=1 and n=4 at g₃₃=8√7."

Checked: 30 candidate combinations — 5 functional families × 6 weights. Families: (A) additive binding E=S−g·w; (B) multiplicative E=S(1−g·w); (C) Casimir two-level mixing (lower branch of the 2×2 problem with Casimir partner Cas(n)=n(n+1)); (D) scale self-consistency E=S√(g·w); (E) second-order ΔN=±2 E=S−(g·w)²/4. Weights: b=1/DegS, gc2=n(n+1)/S(n,d+1), gc=√gc2, S/M=S/DegS, dN·b=n(n−1)/DegS, cas/S=n(n+1)/S. Joint test: d=3 minima = {1,4} at g₃₃ AND d=4 minima containing 3 at g₄₄. g-window scan 0..100, step 0.02.

Results (all null):
- No candidate has d=3 minima = {1,4} at g₃₃ (complete null at the documented coupling).
- g-window scan: NONE — for no g in [0,100] do any of the 30 candidates produce d=3 minima == {1,4}. The d=3 minimum is always at n=1 (binding weak) or slides to n=3 or higher (binding too strong); the two-sided n=4 pocket never opens.
- The one d=4 hit is B/gc2 → d=4 minima [3], but d=3 minima [12] (not a d=3 success).
- Degeneracy probes (family A): A/S/M (g[E₁=E₄,d=3]=19.0, 0.898g₃₃) and A/dN·b (15.83, 0.748g₃₃) have positive degeneracy coupling, confirming these weights have the right sign structure. But g₃₃ lies above the degeneracy point — at the documented coupling the n=4 degenerate configuration has already slid to n=3 as the global minimum.
- Marginality probes (family A): the d=3 onset coupling where n=4 first becomes a minimum is 30.0 (1.417g₃₃) for A/S/M and 50.0 (2.362g₃₃) for A/dN·b — both above g₃₃. n=4 never enters as a minimum before g₃₃ is reached; there is no window.

Structural interpretation: a local minimum at n=4 (with n=1 also a local minimum) requires a weight function with a peak or inflection specifically at n=4 — non-monotone in n. Every weight in the documented vocabulary is strictly monotone (increasing or decreasing) in n. The Casimir family C exploits the unique lattice degeneracy S(4,3)=Cas(4)=20 and was explicitly designed to create resonance at n=4, but cannot overcome the global boundary minimum at n=1 for any tested weight. The single-sector ansatz is the likely wrong object. The T2 kernel is inherently cross-sector: the d=3 vacuum field is coupled to the d=4 sector via g₃₄. An effective energy for d=3 modes, after integrating out the d=4 sector at its equilibrium, would include a back-reaction term of the form (g₃₄)² × f(n₃, n₄*)/m_scale₄ — a cross-sector contribution that can break the monotone-weight constraint. The cross-sector effective potential is the natural next candidate for the Part 2 §5 functional; this search closes the single-sector branch.

Note: the three-layer ontology established this session (arithmetic integers → self-consistency loop → excitations) suggests the vacuum-stability functional is a statement about the Layer-2 self-consistency loop closure, where the d=3 and d=4 sectors are jointly constrained. A single-sector treatment cannot capture this.

**Cross-sector vacuum-stability functional search (2026-06-12, `claude/explore_cross_sector_vacuum.py`)**

Follow-up to the single-sector null above. Conjecture: coupling the d=3 effective energy to the d=4 condensate at n_u=3 via the T2 kernel creates a local minimum at n₃=4. Three approaches tested, all null.

Checked: (A) Diagonal cross-sector ME = g₃₄/3 × ⟨r²⟩_{n₃,d=3} × ⟨r_s²⟩_{3,d=4}: strictly monotone increasing in n₃ (kernel positivity, V≥0 always); minimum at n₃=1. Confirmed analytically by the rank-1 factorisation V_kernel = ½Σᵢⱼ(Σ_d v_d Q_ij^{(d)} J_d)²≥0 — a positive-semidefinite operator cannot create energy pockets. (B) Off-diagonal ME |⟨R_{n₃}^{(3)} | r² | R_3^{(4)}⟩|: non-monotone (peaks at n_r=2, i.e. n₃=5), decaying geometrically for larger n_r. However, n₃=4 (level N=3, l=1 and l=3 ONLY, STEP 30) has NO l=0 component — the l=0 cross-sector coupling is identically zero for n₃=4 by l-parity. n₃=4 is invisible to all l=0 kernel channels. (C) 2×2 lower-branch mixing between (n₃,3) and (n₄=3,4): minima at n₃=1, 3, 5 (the l=0 representative modes), not n₃=4. The lower branch at n₃=4 (E_lower=1.12 MeV) is above n₃=3 (E_lower=0.09 MeV) because n₃=4 and n₃=3 share the same n_r=1 in the l=0 approximation, but n₃=4 has the higher S(n,3).

Structural reason for the null: the kernel positivity theorem prevents cross-sector terms from lowering the energy. The mean-field cross-sector term simply shifts λ₃ → λ₃ + δλ (a uniform scale factor), which raises all modes proportionally and leaves the minimum at n₃=1 unchanged. n₃=4 additionally has no l=0 channel, decoupling it from the l=0 vacuum entirely — its energy is the pure mass term S(4,3)×m_scale₃.

Positive structural fact found: n₃=4 is the unique mode that is (i) an odd-parity (l-parity protected) condensate mode AND (ii) the Casimir resonance point S(4,3)=Cas(4)=20 AND (iii) decoupled from all l=0 kernel channels. This combination makes n₃=4 both stable and unperturbed by the vacuum sector — which may be the content of the §5 assertion, stated imprecisely as "local minimum."
